Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
The Obligation of Ihram from the Miqat: Designated Places for Entering Hajj
Explaining the obligation of ihram from the miqat and the locations of miqat for different regions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six miqat locations according to the Hanafi school, explain the ruling of crossing the miqat without ihram, and distinguish between the Hanafi and Shafi‘i positions regarding the legal nature of the miqat requirement.

Core Idea
Crossing the miqat without ihram incurs a dam but does not invalidate Hajj — the Hanafi view holds it as wajib, not rukn.

This lesson introduces the fundamental concept of miqat — the spatial boundaries for entering the state of ihram. You will learn the exact locations designated by the Prophet ﷺ for people from different regions, and understand the legal consequence of bypassing these points without ihram. The text also provides clear hadith evidence, and we will examine why the Hanafi school classifies this obligation as wajib rather than fard.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is 'assuming ihram from the miqat'. What is the hukm? The text states it is necessary (wajib in Hanafi terminology).
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith: the famous hadith of Ibn Abbas listing the miqats, and the hadith of Aisha adding Dhatu ‘Irq for Iraq. Identify that these are ahad hadith.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas is in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The word 'waqqata' (appointed) indicates a fixed boundary; the implication is that one must not cross without ihram. Hanafi usul interprets this as a command, but since the hadith is ahad, the obligation is wajib, not fard.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement? Yes, Imam al-Shafi‘i considers ihram from miqat as a rukn (pillar) of Hajj, meaning omission invalidates the Hajj. The Hanafi school disagrees.
The difference stems from usul: Shafi‘i treats ahad hadith as potentially qat‘i in certain contexts, while Hanafi strictly separates thubut and dalalah.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon for fatwa? The Hanafi view is that crossing without ihram is a wajib omission requiring a dam (sacrifice) but the Hajj remains valid. This is the mufta bihi position.
The authority is Zahir al-Riwayah; there is no intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf recorded here.

Source Text

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
فصل: في كيفية تركيب افعال الحج
(۱۲۹۰ ) اذا اراد الدخول فى الحج احرم من الميقات كرابغ
فصل : افعال حج کی ترتیب و کیفیت کے بیان میں
ضروری نوٹ : اس فصل میں یہ بیان کیا جائے گا کہ حج کیسے کرے، کون سے اعمال کیسے کرے، اور کب کرے، اور اس کی حیثیت کیا ہے۔
ترجمه : (۱۲۹۰) جب حج میں داخل ہونے کا ارادہ کرے تو میقات سے احرام باندھے، مثلاً رابغ سے۔
تشریح : جب حج کا ارادہ کرے تو میقات سے احرام باندھے، میقات سے احرام باندھے بغیر گزرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ مدینہ سے مکہ مکرمہ آتے ہوئے جمعہ سے پہلے رابغ ہے جو اہل شام کی میقات ہے ۔۔ میقات یہ ہیں [1] مدینہ والوں کے لئے ذوالحلیفہ ہے [۲] شام والوں کے لئے جھہ ہے۔ [۳] نجد والوں کے لئے قرن منازل ہے - [۴] یمن والوں کے لئے یلملم ہے ، [۵] ذات عرق عراق والوں کی میقات ہے [۶] اور مکہ والوں کے لئے مکہ ہے ۔
وجه (۱) میقات کی تصریح اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله له لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة، ولاهل الشام الجحفة ، ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ، ولاهل اليمن يلملم من لهن ولمن اتى عليهن من غيرهن ممن اراد الحج والعمرة ومن كان دون ذلك فمن حيث انشاء حتى اهل مكة من مكة. (بخارى شریف ، باب محصل اہل مکتہ لحج والعمر ة ص ۲۰۶ نمبر ۱۵۲۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب مواقیت الحج ص ۱۳۷۴ نمبر ۲۸۰۳/۱۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ یہ مقامات ان لوگوں کے لئے میقات ہیں۔ بغیر احرام کے ان سے آگے گزرنا جائز نہیں (۲) عن عائشة ان رسول الله لا لا لا لا وقت لاهل العراق ذات عرق (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی امواقیت ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۷۳۹ار بخاری شریف باب ذات عرق لاصل العراق ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۵۳۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل عراق کے لئے میقات مقام ذات عرق ہے۔
Chapter: Composition of Hajj acts. Chapter: On how to compose the acts of Hajj. (1290) When one intends to enter into Hajj, he should assume ihram from the miqat, such as from Rabigh. Chapter: On the order and manner of Hajj acts. Essential note: In this chapter, it will be explained how to perform Hajj, which acts to do, when to do them, and their status. Translation: (1290) When one intends to enter into Hajj, he should tie ihram from the miqat, for example from Rabigh. Explanation: When one intends Hajj, he should tie ihram from the miqat; passing beyond the miqat without ihram is not permissible. When coming from Madinah to Makkah, before Juhfah is Rabigh, which is the miqat for the people of Syria. The miqats are: [1] For the people of Madinah, Dhul-Hulayfah. [2] For the people of Syria, Juhfah. [3] For the people of Najd, Qarn al-Manazil. [4] For the people of Yemen, Yalamlam. [5] Dhatu 'Irq is the miqat for the people of Iraq. [6] And for the people of Makkah, Makkah (i.e., they enter ihram from Makkah). Evidence (1): The specification of the miqat is in this hadith: From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah ﷺ appointed Dhul-Hulayfah as the miqat for the people of Madinah, Juhfah for the people of Syria, Qarn al-Manazil for the people of Najd, Yalamlam for the people of Yemen – these are for them and for those who come from other places intending Hajj and Umrah, and those who are within these boundaries should enter ihram from where they start, even the people of Makkah from Makkah. (Sahih al-Bukhari and Sahih Muslim). This hadith proves that these places are miqats for those people. Passing beyond them without ihram is not permissible. (2) From Aisha that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ appointed Dhatu 'Irq for the people of Iraq. (Sunan Abi Dawud and Sahih al-Bukhari). This hadith shows that for the people of Iraq, the miqat is Dhatu 'Irq.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This is the opening of a chapter on the order of Hajj acts. The matn (core text) states that when one intends to perform Hajj, he must enter ihram from the miqat. The commentator explains that passing the miqat without ihram is impermissible (ghair ja'iz), meaning it is haram. He then lists the six miqats for different regions: Dhul-Hulayfah for Madinah, Juhfah (or Rabigh?) for Syria, Qarn al-Manazil for Najd, Yalamlam for Yemen, Dhatu 'Irq for Iraq, and Makkah itself for its residents. The commentator then cites two hadith proofs: the famous hadith of Ibn Abbas enumerating the miqats, and the hadith of Aisha adding Dhatu 'Irq for Iraq. The text underscores that it is obligatory to enter ihram before passing these points. According to the Hanafi school, entering ihram from the miqat is wajib (obligatory), not fard; crossing without ihram incurs a dam (sacrificial penalty) if one continues, but the Hajj is valid, but he must return to the miqat if possible. The authority of these rulings is derived from authentic Sunnah.

Key Terms
میقات (miqat): A boundary station beyond which one intending Hajj or Umrah cannot pass without being in ihram; it is the designated place to enter the state of consecration.
احرام (ihram): The state of consecration for Hajj or Umrah, consisting of intention (niyyah) and talbiyah, along with special restrictions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, what is the ruling for a person intending Hajj who passes the miqat without ihram?
A) His Hajj is invalid and he must repeat it.
B) He must return to the miqat and if unable, sacrifice a dam.
C) There is no problem; he can continue.
D) He must perform an extra tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Entering ihram from the miqat is a wajib act in Hanafi fiqh; omission requires a dam but does not invalidate the Hajj.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Obligation of Entering Ihram at the Miqat
Ruling with proof on miqat and obligated acts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on entering ihram at the miqat, list the six miqat boundaries, and explain the proof from the hadith of Ibn Abbas and Aisha.

Core Idea
Passing the miqat without ihram is prohibited; doing so requires a dam.

This lesson establishes the Hanafi position that entering ihram at the designated miqat is a wajib (obligatory) act. We will examine the miqat boundaries specified in the hadith and understand why Hanafi scholars deem crossing without ihram as requiring compensation. This ruling applies to every pilgrim who passes these boundaries, whether by land, sea, or air.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on entering ihram
Read the matn and commentary: 'When he intends to enter Hajj, he enters ihram from the miqat.' Identify that this is a command implying obligation (wajib) in Hanafi usul.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the proof is from ahad hadith.
2
Identify the miqat boundaries for each region
From the list provided: Dhul-Hulayfah (Madinah), Juhfah (Sham), Qarn al-Manazil (Najd), Yalamlam (Yemen), Dhat 'Irq (Iraq), and Makkah for its residents. Understand that each pilgrim must use the miqat on the route they travel.
Modern distances help but the legal point is the boundary itself.
3
Locate the proof from the hadith
The text cites two hadith: from Ibn Abbas (list of five miqats) and from Aisha (Dhat 'Irq for Iraq). These are ahad hadith, zanni al-thubut, hence the ruling is wajib not fard.
The hadith are found in Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
4
Explain how the Prophet's action indicates obligation
In Hanafi usul, when the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) fixes a boundary (waqt) for an act, it indicates a binding command (wujub). The hadith uses 'waqata' (he appointed), which implies obligation unless there is evidence to make it recommendatory.
Shafi'is interpret the same hadith as recommendatory, leading to a difference in ruling.
5
Analyze the Hanafi–Shafi'i difference and its thamarah
The practical consequence: if a pilgrim crosses the miqat without ihram, the Hanafi school requires a dam (penalty), while the Shafi'i school does not consider it obligatory and thus no penalty. However, both agree the ihram can be performed later.
This difference is based on the weight given to the prophetic command in usul.

ترجمه : (۱۲۹۰) جب حج میں داخل ہونے کا ارادہ کرے تو میقات سے احرام باندھے، مثلاً رابغ سے۔

وجه (۱) میقات کی تصریح اس حدیث میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال وقت رسول الله له لاهل المدينة ذا الحليفة، ولاهل الشام الجحفة ، ولاهل نجد قرن المنازل ، ولاهل اليمن يلملم من لهن ولمن اتى عليهن من غيرهن ممن اراد الحج والعمرة ومن كان دون ذلك فمن حيث انشاء حتى اهل مكة من مكة. (بخارى شریف ، باب محصل اہل مکتہ لحج والعمر ة ص ۲۰۶ نمبر ۱۵۲۴ر مسلم شریف ، باب مواقیت الحج ص ۱۳۷۴ نمبر ۲۸۰۳/۱۸) اس حدیث سے ثابت ہوا کہ یہ مقامات ان لوگوں کے لئے میقات ہیں۔ بغیر احرام کے ان سے آگے گزرنا جائز نہیں (۲) عن عائشة ان رسول الله لا لا لا لا وقت لاهل العراق ذات عرق (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب فی امواقیت ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۷۳۹ار بخاری شریف باب ذات عرق لاصل العراق ص ۲۰۷ نمبر ۱۵۳۱) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ اہل عراق کے لئے میقات مقام ذات عرق ہے۔

يلملم
اہل مکہ عمرے کا احترام متعیم سے باندھتے ہیں مکہ مکرمہ سے 7.5 کلومیٹر دور شمال مغرب کی جانب ہے لغت : میقات جس جگہ سے حاجی احرام باندھے اس کو میقات کہتے ہیں۔ حرم : بیت اللہ اور مکہ مکرمہ کے ارد گرد کچھ جگہیں ہیں جن پر آج کل نشانات لگا دئے گئے ہیں جن میں شکار کرنا حرام ہے اس کو حرم کہتے ہیں۔ حل : حرم سے باہر اور میقات کے اندر کی جگہ کو حل کہتے ہیں۔ مکہ مکرمہ سے مدینہ طیبہ 410 کلومیٹر ہے، اور ذوالحلیفہ مدینہ طیبہ سے 10 کلومیٹر کے فاصلے پر ہے۔ نوٹ: میقات اور حدود حرم کے نقشے آخیر میں دیکھیں۔
Chapter: On the arrangement of Hajj actions. (1290) When he intends to enter Hajj, he enters ihram from the miqat, e.g., Rabigh. Chapter: On the arrangement and quality of Hajj actions. Necessary note: In this chapter, it will be explained how to perform Hajj, which actions how, and when, and what their status is. Translation: (1290) When he intends to enter Hajj, he ties ihram from the miqat, e.g., from Rabigh. Explanation: When he intends Hajj, he ties ihram from the miqat; passing beyond the miqat without tying ihram is not permissible. Coming from Madinah to Makkah, before Juhfah is Rabigh, which is the miqat of the people of Sham. The miqats are: [1] For the people of Madinah, Dhul-Hulayfah; [2] For the people of Sham, Juhfah; [3] For the people of Najd, Qarn al-Manazil; [4] For the people of Yemen, Yalamlam; [5] Dhat 'Irq is the miqat of the people of Iraq; [6] And for the people of Makkah, Makkah. Proof (1): The specification of the miqat is in this hadith: From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed for the people of Madinah Dhul-Hulayfah, for the people of Sham Juhfah, for the people of Najd Qarn al-Manazil, and for the people of Yemen Yalamlam. These are for them and for those who come from other places intending Hajj and Umrah. And whoever is within these boundaries, then (he enters ihram) from where he starts, even the people of Makkah from Makkah. (Bukhari, Chapter on the ihram of the people of Makkah for Hajj and Umrah, p. 206, no. 1524; Muslim, Chapter on the miqats of Hajj, p. 1374, no. 2803/18) This hadith proves that these places are miqats for those people; passing beyond them without ihram is not permissible. (2) From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) appointed Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on miqats, p. 250, no. 1739; Bukhari, Chapter on Dhat 'Irq for the people of Iraq, p. 207, no. 1531) From this hadith it is known that for the people of Iraq, the miqat is Dhat 'Irq. Dhul-Hulayfah: Miqat at a glance. This place is the miqat of the people of Madinah, 410 km north of Makkah. Dhat 'Irq: This place is the miqat of the people of Iraq, 90 km east of Makkah. Juhfah: This place is the miqat of the people of Sham, 182 km northwest of Makkah. Qarn al-Manazil: This place is the miqat of the people of Najd, 80 km east of Makkah. Yalamlam: This place is the miqat of the people of Yemen, 130 km south of Makkah. The people of Makkah tie ihram for Umrah from Tan'im, 7.5 km northwest of Makkah. Lexicon: Miqat: The place from which the pilgrim ties ihram is called miqat. Haram: Some areas around the House of Allah and Makkah that are marked with signs today, in which hunting is forbidden, are called Haram. Hill: The area outside Haram and inside miqat is called Hill. The distance from Makkah to Madinah is 410 km, and Dhul-Hulayfah is 10 km from Madinah. Note: See the maps of miqat and Haram boundaries at the end.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil). The author states the ruling in the matn: when one intends to enter the state of Hajj, he must enter ihram from the miqat, giving Rabigh as an example. The commentary expands this, stressing that passing the miqat without ihram is impermissible. It then lists the six miqats for different regions: Dhul-Hulayfah for Madinah, Juhfah for Sham, Qarn al-Manazil for Najd, Yalamlam for Yemen, Dhat 'Irq for Iraq, and Makkah itself for its residents. The proof is two hadith: the first from Ibn Abbas (marfu') specifying the five miqats (excluding Iraq), and the second from Aisha specifying Dhat 'Irq for Iraq. This is based on the principle that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) fixed these boundaries, making them obligatory (wajib) crossing points. The typographical list and distances are for practical orientation, but the legal core is that ihram must be entered at the miqat designated for one's direction, not earlier (except by intention) and not later. The Hanafi position is that this is wajib (obligatory) due to the prophetic command; omitting it without a valid excuse necessitates a dam (sacrifice), though the ihram is valid. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah from the hadith and standard Hanafi works.

Key Terms
میقات (mīqāt): The specific place from which a pilgrim must enter ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
احرام (ihrām): The state of ritual consecration for Hajj or Umrah, beginning with the intention (niyyah) and talbiyah, and entailing prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the legal status (hukm) of entering ihram from the miqat according to the Hanafi school?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
It is wajib to enter ihram at the miqat; crossing without ihram requires a dam.

Ghusl Before Ihram: Recommended Purification for All
Ruling with proof on recommended purification before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on ghusl before ihram, explain its proof from hadith, and identify which individuals are included (including menstruating and postpartum women).

Core Idea
Ghusl before ihram is mustahabb for cleanliness, not ritual purity; even menstruating women perform it.

This passage addresses the recommended purification before entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah. The Hanafi school emphasizes that while ghusl is not obligatory, it is a stressed sunnah. Notably, this ruling extends to women who are menstruating or in postpartum, underscoring that the purpose is physical cleanliness, not ritual purification. The proofs from the Prophet's own practice and his instruction to Asma bint Umays establish this clearly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is performing ghusl (or wudu) before ihram. The Hanafi ruling is that it is mustahabb (sunnah muakkadah) – recommended and stressed, but not obligatory.
Ghusl is preferred over wudu.
2
Locate the dalil
Two ahadith are cited: (1) Ibn Abbas reports that the Prophet himself performed ghusl before ihram at Dhul-Hulayfah. (2) Aisha reports that the Prophet ordered Asma bint Umays, who was in postpartum, to perform ghusl and enter ihram.
Both are ahad (single-narrator) hadith, so zanni in transmission.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's own action indicates recommendation (sunnah). The explicit command to a postpartum woman proves the ghusl is for physical cleanliness, not ritual purity (since she was not ritually pure).
This distinguishes the ghusl from obligatory purification for prayer.
4
Note the scope and exceptions
The ruling includes all persons entering ihram: men, women, menstruating women, and postpartum women (as long as no harm results from washing).
Menstruating women perform ghusl even though they cannot pray.
5
Evaluate the authority
The ruling is based on ahad hadith, but it is consistent across the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah). There is no intra-Hanafi dispute; all three imams agree it is mustahabb.
The mufta bihi is that ghusl is mustahabb; wudu suffices if needed.

ترجمه : (۱۳۹۱) احرام کے لئے غسل کرے، یا وضو کرے، اور نظافت کے لئے غسل زیادہ پسندیدہ ہے، پس حیض والی عورت اور نقصان نہ ہو تو نفاس والی بھی غسل کرے۔
وجه : (۱) حدیث میں ہے آپ نے احرام کے لئے غسل فرمایا۔ عن ابن عباس قال اغتسل رسول الله ثم لبس ثيابه فلما اتى ذالحليفة صلى ركعتين ثم قعد على بعيره فلما استوى به على البيداء احرم بالحج ۔(دارقطنی ، کتاب الحج حج ثانی ص ۱۹۷ نمبر ۲۴۰۸ رسنن بیھقی ، باب الغسل للا هلال ج خامس ص ۱۴۹، نمبر ۸۹۴۵ / ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فی الاغتسال عند الاحرام ص ۷۱ انمبر ۸۳۰ ) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ احرام کے لئے غسل کرے یہ بہتر ہے۔(۲) (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نفاس والی عورت کو بھی غسل کرنے کے لئے فرمایا . . . عن عائشة قالت نفست أسماء بنت عميس بمحمد بن ابى بكر بالشجرة فأمر رسول الله الله أبا بكر يأمرها أن تغتسل و تهل - (مسلم شریف، باب صحۃ احرام النفساء و استباب التسالهالا حرام ، وكذا الى انفض ، ص ۱۵۰۴، نمبر ۱۲۰۹/ ۲۹۰۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نفاس والی عورت غسل کرے اور احرام باندھے، جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ غسل نظافت اور صفائی کے لئے ہے۔
Translation (1291): For ihram, he should perform ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is more beloved for cleanliness. Thus, a menstruating woman and a woman in postpartum (if no harm) should also perform ghusl. Proof (1): There is a hadith that the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed ghusl for ihram. From Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) performed ghusl, then put on his clothes, then when he came to Dhul-Hulayfah, he prayed two rak'ahs, then sat on his camel, and when he mounted the plain of al-Bayda', he entered ihram for Hajj. (Darqutni, Book of Hajj, second Hajj, p. 197, no. 2408; Bayhaqi, Chapter on ghusl for entering ihram, vol. 5, p. 149, no. 8945; Tirmidhi, Chapter on what is reported about ghusl at ihram, p. 71, no. 830) This hadith shows that one should perform ghusl for ihram; it is better. (2) This hadith shows that a woman in postpartum was also commanded to perform ghusl. From Aisha (may Allah be pleased with her) who said: Asma bint Umays gave birth to Muhammad ibn Abi Bakr at Shajarah, and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) ordered Abu Bakr to tell her to perform ghusl and begin the talbiyah. (Muslim, Chapter on the validity of ihram of a postpartum woman and that she is not prevented from ihram, and likewise until the end, p. 1504, no. 1209/2908) This hadith indicates that a postpartum woman should perform ghusl and enter ihram, proving that this ghusl is for cleanliness and purification.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof (hukm with dalil) on purification before ihram. The matn states the recommended acts: performing ghusl or wudu before entering ihram, with ghusl being more beloved. It explicitly includes menstruating women and postpartum women, as long as no harm (nags) occurs. The proofs are two hadith: first, that the Prophet himself performed ghusl before ihram at Dhul-Hulayfah, establishing it as a practice (sunnah); second, that Asma bint Umays, who was in postpartum, was ordered to perform ghusl and enter ihram, demonstrating that the ghusl is for cleanliness, not ritual purity (since postpartum women are not ritually pure for salah). The Hanafi ruling is that ghusl before ihram is mustahabb (recommended, not wajib). This is based on the fact that the Prophet performed it and commanded it for the postpartum woman, but did not reprimand those who omitted it. The authority weight is from hadith and standard Hanafi fiqh; it is Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): Full body washing with water, intended for cleanliness before ihram, not for ritual purity (since menstruating women also do it).
احرام (ihram): The sacred state entered before Hajj or Umrah, involving specific garments and prohibitions.
حائض (ha'id): Menstruating woman. In this context, she is still recommended to perform ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The Prophet ordered a postpartum woman (who is not ritually pure) to perform ghusl.
C) The hadith mentions 'cleanliness' explicitly.
D) The Qur'an commands ghusl before pilgrimage.

Key Takeaway
Ghusl before ihram is a recommended practice for all, including menstruating and postpartum women, emphasizing cleanliness over ritual purity.

Recommended Acts of Grooming Before Ihram
Ruling on mustahabb grooming before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended grooming acts before ihram and identify their legal status as mustahabb (sunnah ghayr muakkadah).

Core Idea
Complete cleanliness before ihram is mustahabb, not obligatory.

In preparing for the sacred state of ihram, the Hanafi school emphasizes physical cleanliness. This lesson clarifies that acts such as cutting nails, trimming the mustache, and removing armpit hair are recommended (mustahabb) rather than required. While these acts carry reward, their omission does not affect the validity of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling
The passage states 'complete cleanliness is mustahabb' (مستحب). Determine the legal category: mustahabb is equivalent to sunnah ghayr muakkadah in Hanafi fiqh.
2
Extract the specific recommendations
The text lists three acts: cutting nails (ناخن کاٹ لے), trimming the mustache (مونچھ تراش لے), and removing armpit hair (بغل کے بال صاف کرے).
These are part of the sunan al-fitrah.
3
Verify the legal consequence of omission
Since it is mustahabb, omitting these acts is not sinful and does not invalidate ihram or require compensation (like sajdah al-sahw or dam).
Contrast with wajib acts: omission of wajib before ihram does not invalidate ihram but is blameworthy.
4
Contrast with obligations in ihram
Note that these acts are pre-ihram recommendations. Once in ihram, cutting nails or removing hair becomes prohibited (haram) and requires fidya.
This boundary helps avoid confusion between pre-ihram sunan and ihram prohibitions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۹۲) اور کمال نظافت مستحب ہے (اس طور پر کہ ) ناخن کاٹ لے، مونچھ تراش لے، بغل کے بال صاف کرے،
Translation (1292): And complete cleanliness is mustahabb (in the sense that) he should cut his nails, trim his mustache, and remove armpit hair.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement (hukm without proof) on recommended acts before ihram. The author states that it is mustahabb (recommended) to achieve complete cleanliness by performing three specific grooming acts: cutting nails, trimming the mustache, and removing armpit hair. These acts are part of the sunan al-fitrah (natural practices) and are especially emphasized before entering the state of ihram to ensure physical purity and neatness. The Hanafi school considers these acts mustahabb; they are not wajib. If omitted, the ihram remains valid and no compensation is required. The authority weight is from general fiqh rulings (Zahir al-Riwayah basis from hadith on fitrah).

Key Terms
مستحب (mustahabb): An act that is recommended; doing it is rewarded, omitting it is not sinful. Here referring to grooming before ihram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Fard
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Cutting nails, trimming mustache, and removing armpit hair before ihram are mustahabb (recommended); omission does not invalidate ihram.

Sunnan Before Ihram: Ghusl, Cleanliness, and Garments
Explanation of recommended actions before entering ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four sunnan before ihram according to the Hanafi school and apply the ruling on ghusl for menstruating women.

Core Idea
Ghusl before ihram is sunnah, not wajib; wudu suffices.

Before entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, a pilgrim is encouraged to perform certain acts of cleanliness and preparation. These are not obligations but highly recommended sunnan that enhance the spiritual and physical state. In this lesson, we examine the four key sunnan as outlined in the Hanafi text, along with their evidences from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four sunnan
Read the passage and list the four recommended actions: (1) ghusl or wudu, (2) complete cleanliness (nail cutting, shaving, etc.), (3) wearing new/washed izaar and rida', (4) not knotting the izaar.
These are all sunnah muakkadah according to Hanafis.
2
Analyze the evidence for ghusl
The passage cites two hadith: the Prophet's own ghusl before ihram (Ibn Abbas) and his command to Asma bint Umays to perform ghusl despite postpartum bleeding (Aisha). Note that the command indicates recommendation, not obligation.
The ruling for a menstruating woman: she performs ghusl if it does not harm her.
3
Distinguish ghusl vs wudu
The text says 'he performs ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is more beloved.' This shows wudu is sufficient but ghusl is preferred. Understand the Hanafi position that ghusl is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
Omitting ghusl does not invalidate ihram.
4
Determine the ruling on knotting the izaar
The passage explicitly prohibits knotting, tying, or tearing the izaar to put around the neck. Doing so is makruh but there is no penalty. Recognize the distinction between makruh tahrimi and tanzihi here; this is makruh tanzihi.
The garment should be worn loosely, not sewn or knotted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل تركيب افعال الحج . (۱۲۹۱) فيغتسل او يتوضأ والغسل وهو احبّ للتنظيف فتغتسل المرأة الحائض والنفساء اذا لم يضرها (۱۲۹۲) ويستحب كمال النظافة بقص الظفر والشارب ونتف الابط وحلق العانة وجماع الاهل والدهن ولو مطيبا (۱۲۹۳ ) ويلبس الرجل ازارا ورداء جدیدین او غسيلين والجديد الابيض (۱۲۹۴) ولا يعقد الازار ولا يشد ولا يخرق فيجعل في عنقه وان فعل كره ولا جزاء فيه
Chapter: Composition of the actions of Hajj. (1291) He performs ghusl or wudu, and ghusl is more beloved for cleanliness. So the menstruating woman and the woman in postpartum bleeding perform ghusl if it does not harm her. (1292) Complete cleanliness is recommended: cutting the nail, mustache, plucking the armpit hair, shaving the pubic hair, intercourse with one's wife, and applying oil even if perfumed. (1293) The man wears an izaar and a rida', both new or both washed, and the new white (is better). (1294) He does not knot the izaar, nor tie it, nor tear it to put around his neck. If he does so, it is makruh but there is no penalty.
Source pages p. 342

Commentary
This passage from Thamaratun Najah is a commentary expanding on the rulings (sunnan) related to preparing for ihram. The author begins with the chapter heading 'Composition of the actions of Hajj' and then lists four recommended acts. First (1291): It is sunnah to perform ghusl before entering ihram; wudu suffices but ghusl is preferred for cleanliness. Even a woman in menstruation or postpartum bleeding should perform ghusl if it does not harm her, as the purpose is cleanliness. Second (1292): Complete personal hygiene is recommended, including trimming nails, mustache, plucking armpit hair, shaving pubic hair, marital intercourse, and applying oil or perfume. These are done because after ihram, such activities are prohibited. Third (1293): A man should wear an izaar (lower garment) and rida' (upper garment), both new or at least washed, and white is best. Fourth (1294): The izaar should not be knotted, tied, or torn to hang around the neck; doing so is makruh (disliked) but does not incur a penalty. The passage then provides hadith proofs for each ruling, establishing them as sunan from the Prophet.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full body wash before ihram for cleanliness.
الميقة (al-miqat): Place where ihram begins; defined geographically.
الازار والرداء (al-izar wa al-rida'): The two seamless garments worn by a male muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is wajib upon her.
B) She is excused and should not perform ghusl.
C) She should perform ghusl if it does not harm her, as it is sunnah.
D) She should perform tayammum instead.

Key Takeaway
Performing ghusl, personal hygiene, and wearing the ihram garments correctly are sunnah muakkadah; ihram remains valid even if omitted, but following them completes the Prophetic practice.

Recommendation of Cleanliness Before Ihram
Enumerates recommended acts of cleanliness and grooming before ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts of cleanliness before ihram and identify the evidence that establishes them as sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Cleanliness before ihram is recommended (sunnah), not obligatory, based on the Prophet's practice.

When preparing for the sacred state of ihram, the Prophet ﷺ engaged in grooming and applying perfume. This lesson examines that practice and clarifies that these acts are recommended, not required, in the Hanafi school. Understanding this distinction prevents the error of treating them as mandatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal ruling
The text uses 'yustahabb' meaning it is recommended. In Hanafi fiqh, this equates to sunnah. The acts are cleanliness practices before ihram.
2
Find the evidence (dalil) for this ruling
Two hadiths are cited: from Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet combing and oiling; from Aisha showing her perfuming the Prophet before ihram.
Dalil is from the Prophet's actions and tacit approval.
3
Determine how the evidence proves the ruling (wajh al-dalalah)
The Prophet's actions indicate permissibility and desirability. In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's fi'l (action) indicates nadb (recommendation) unless there is evidence of obligation. No command is present, so it is sunnah.
Also, the Prophet did not forbid others, implying approval.
4
Consider any differences of opinion (ikhtilaf)
Some schools may view some acts as obligatory, but the Hanafi school maintains they are sunnah. The evidence does not support wujub.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that these acts are sunnah. Omitting them does not invalidate ihram or require compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1292) ويستحب كمال النظافة بقص الظفر والشارب ونتف الابط وحلق العانة وجماع الاهل والدهن ولو مطيبا.

تشريح : احرام کے بعد کئی دن تک صفائی کا موقع نہیں ملے گا اس لئے صفائی کی ساری صورتیں اختیار کرلے تو بہتر ہے، مثلا ناخن کاٹ لے، مونچھ تراش لے ، بغل کے بال صاف کرلے، زیر ناف بال کاٹ لے، ہو سکے تو بیوی سے جماع کرلے تا کہ اس بھیٹر میں جس میں عورتیں بھی ہوتیں ہیں ان پر شہوت کی نگاہ نہ پڑے اور خوشبو وغیرہ لگالے۔

(1292) Complete cleanliness is recommended by cutting the nail and mustache, plucking the armpit, shaving the pubic area, intercourse with one's family, and oil even if perfumed. Explanation: After ihram, there will be no opportunity for cleanliness for several days, so it is better to adopt all forms of cleanliness, e.g., cut nails, trim mustache, clean armpit hair, cut pubic hair, if possible have intercourse with wife so that in this gathering where women are present they do not look with lust, and apply perfume etc. Evidence: (1) Combing and applying perfume – this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Abbas: the Prophet (peace be upon him) set out from Madinah after combing and oiling and wearing his izar and rida, he and his companions, and he did not forbid anything from the rida and izar. (Bukhari, book of what the muhrim wears, p.209 no.1545) (2) From Aisha: I used to perfume the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) for his ihram when he was about to enter ihram and for his hal after finishing ihram before he circumambulated the House. (Bukhari, book of perfume at ihram, p.208 no.1539, Abu Dawud, book of perfume at ihram, p.257 no.1745) This indicates applying perfume for ihram.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The author states that it is recommended (mustahabb) to perform all aspects of cleanliness before entering the state of ihram. The ruling is based on the fact that after ihram, many of these actions become prohibited or restricted. The commentary explains the wisdom: so that one does not miss cleanliness opportunities, and to avoid potential lustful glances. The evidence provided includes two hadiths: the first shows the Prophet’s practice of combing, oiling, and wearing ihram garments, implying these are recommended; the second proves that applying perfume before ihram is allowed (and recommended) as Aisha used to perfume the Prophet. In the Hanafi school, these acts are sunnah, not obligatory.

Key Terms
يستحب (yustahabb): It is recommended; a ruling between sunnah and mubah in Hanafi terminology.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Ihram Clothing: Izar and Rida – Sunnah or Obligation?
Ruling on recommended ihram garments with evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on ihram clothing (izar and rida), identify the evidences provided, and explain the preference for white and newness.

Core Idea
Ihram clothing is sunnah – two unsewn white wraps preferred, but not obligatory.

When a man enters ihram for Hajj or Umrah, what should he wear? This passage from a classical Hanafi text provides a clear recommendation: an izar (lower wrap) and rida (upper wrap), ideally new and white. But is this a requirement (wajib) or merely a strong sunnah? Let's examine the evidence and the school's ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The text states that a man in ihram should wear an izar and rida. Determine the hukm level: is it fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.?
The passage describes a recommendation, not an absolute requirement.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Two hadith are cited: one from Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet's practice, and one from Aisha about shrouding in white. Identify the type of evidence (Quran, Sunnah, etc.).
Both are ahad hadith.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (how the proof proves the ruling)
The Prophet's action of wearing izar and rida indicates it is a recommended practice (sunnah). The hadith on white shrouds is used qiyas to prefer white garments.
The Hanafi school uses the principle that the Prophet's habitual action indicates sunnah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may consider these garments obligatory (wajib) for ihram. The Hanafi school considers them sunnah.
The practical difference: if a man wears sewn clothes, his ihram is still valid according to Hanafis but may be invalid according to others.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred view)
The Hanafi reliance on the Prophet's practice and the lack of an explicit command leads to the conclusion that the clothing is sunnah, not wajib.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that izar and rida are recommended.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1293) ويلبس الرجل ازارا ورداء جدیدین او غسيلين والجديد الابيض.

تشريح : مرد احرام باندھنے کے لئے لنگی اور چادر پہنے، یہ دونوں نئے ہوں اور سفید ہوں تو زیادہ بہتر ہے، اور پرانے ہوں تو کم سے کم دھلے ہوئے ہوں تا کہ یہ معلوم ہو کہ صاف ستھرا ہیں اور پاک ہیں۔

وجه : (۱) لنگی اور چادر پہنے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عباس قال انطلق النبى صلى الله عليه وسلم من المدينة بعد ما ترجل وادهن ولبس ازاره ورداء هو واصحابه فلم ينه عن شيء من الاردية والازر. (بخارى شريف، باب ما يلبس المحرم من الثياب والا رديۃ والازار ص۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۵۴۵) (۲) سفید بہتر ہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم كفن في ثلاثة اثواب يمانية بيض سحولية من كرسف . ( بخاری شریف ، باب الثياب البيض للكفن ،ص ۲۰۲، نمبر ۱۲۶۴ رابوداود شریف ، باب فی الکفن ص ۴۶۱ نمبر ۳۱۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سفید کپڑا ہو۔
(1293) And the man wears an izar and rida, both new or washed, and the new white is better. Explanation: For tying ihram, a man should wear a lower garment (izar) and an upper wrap (rida). These should be new and white for preference; if old, at least washed so they are clean and pure. Evidence: (1) For wearing izar and rida, this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Abbas: the Prophet set out from Madinah after combing and oiling and wearing his izar and rida, he and his companions, and he did not forbid anything from the rida and izar. (Bukhari) (2) White is better: from Aisha: the Messenger of Allah was shrouded in three white Yemeni cotton garments. (Bukhari and Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates white cloth.
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This ruling with proof outlines the recommended attire for ihram. The man should wear two unsewn garments: an izar (lower wrap) and a rida (upper wrap). Preferably new and white, but if used, they must be washed to ensure cleanliness. The evidence from Ibn Abbas shows the Prophet’s practice of wearing izar and rida. The preference for white is deduced from the hadith of shrouding, as white garments are more virtuous. In the Hanafi school, these are sunnah; wearing other types of clothing is permissible but may be makruh if sewn.

Key Terms
إزار (izar): A lower garment wrapped around the waist, worn in ihram.
رداء (rida): An upper wrap worn over the shoulders, part of ihram clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred color for ihram garments according to the Hanafi school?
A) Black
B) Green
C) White
D) Any color

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that wearing izar and rida for ihram is a confirmed sunnah, with white being preferred; it is not obligatory, so the ihram remains valid with other clothing.

Prohibition of Tying and Buttoning the Izar
Ruling with proof on fastening the izar during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on tying the izar in ihram, identify the three pieces of evidence, and explain why it is makruh tanzihi rather than haram.

Core Idea
Any fastening resembling sewing is makruh; the izar must be worn untied unless necessity permits.

In ihram, the izar (lower garment) must be worn without buttons, ties, or pins. The Hanafi school rules that such fastening is makruh tanzihi — disliked but not sinful — because it resembles sewn garments. This lesson unpacks the ruling, its evidence, and a practical exception for those who fear exposure of the awrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific action is being ruled upon? Is it buttoning, tying, or pinning the izar? The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) but not haram or requiring expiation.
2
Locate the dalil
There are three pieces of evidence: a mursal hadith where the Prophet ordered a rope belt removed; the practice of Ibn Umar tucking rather than tying; and the general hadith prohibiting sewn garments.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does each proof connect to the ruling? The first shows direct disapproval of tying; the second shows the preferred method; the third provides an analogy: tying is like sewing in producing a fixed garment.
The Hanafi analogy (qiyas) treats tying as similar to sewing in terms of altering the garment's shape.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other madhhabs may consider such fastening haram (prohibitive) requiring a dam (penalty). The Hanafi school distinguishes between makruh tanzihi and haram.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Why does the Hanafi school choose the makruh ruling? Because the dalil are zanni in both transmission and meaning, and the analogy to sewing is not perfect.
The mufta bihi is that it is makruh tanzihi with no penalty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(1294) ولا يزرّه ولا يعقده ولا يخلّله فان فعل كره ولا شيء عليه.

تشريح : لنگی میں گھنڈی نہ لگائے اور نہ اس کو رسی سے باندھے ، اور نہ اس کو پھاڑ کر گلے میں لٹکائے ، اور اگر ایسا کر لیا تو مکروہ ہے لیکن چونکہ یہ سلے ہوئے کے درجے میں نہیں ہے اس لئے کوئی جز اواجب نہیں ہوگی۔ نوٹ : جولوگ ہمیشہ پائجامہ یا پینٹ پہنتے ہیں اور اندر میں انڈرویر پہننے کے عادی ہیں انکو ہر وقت لنگی کھلنے کا احساس ہوتا ہے، بلکہ سوتے میں کھل بھی جاتی ہے اس لئے ستر کھلنے کی مجبوری سے انکے لئے گانٹھ لگانا مکروہ نہیں ہوگا۔ اصول یہ ہے کہ سلے ہوئے کے درجے میں ہو جائے تو مکر وہ ہوگا۔

وجه : (۱) اس حدیث مرسل میں بھی ہے کہ رسی سے نہ باندھے۔ عن ابن جريج ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم رأى رجلا محتزما بحبل ابرق فقال انزع الحبل مرتين . هذا منقطع. (سن بيهقي، باب لا يعتقد الحمر م رداء عليه ولكن بيغر زطر في رداه ان شاء في ازاره ، ج خامس بص ۸۲، نمبر ۲ ۹۰۷) (۲) رسی سے باندھنا مکروہ ہے اس کے لئے یہ عمل صحابی ہے۔ ان ابن عمر لم يكن عقد الثوب عليه انما غرز طرفه على ازاره ( سنن بيقهي ، باب لا يعتقد المحرم رواہ علیہ ولکن یغفر زطرفی رداء ان شاء في ازاره، ج خامس ص ۸۲، نمبر ۹۰۷۱) (۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ سلا ہوا کپڑا جائز نہیں ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر قال قام رجل فقال يا رسول الله ماذا تأمرنا ان نلبس من الثياب في الاحرام؟ فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لا تلبسوا القميص ولا السراويلات ولا العمائم ولا البرانس الا ان يكون احد ليست له نعلان فليلبس الخفين وليقطع اسفل من الكعبين ولا تلبسوا شيئا مسه زعفران ولا الورس ولا تتنقب المرأة المحرمة ولا تلبس القفازين (بخاری شریف، باب ما نهى من الطيب للحرم والمحر م ص ۲۸ نمبر ۱۸۳۸ ر مسلم شریف ، باب ما يباح للمحرم بيج او عمر البسه ص ۳۷۲ نمبر ۲۷۹۱/۱۱۷۷)
(1294) And he should not button it, nor tie it, nor pin it. If he does, it is makruh and nothing is upon him. Explanation: He should not put a button in the izar, nor tie it with a rope, nor tear it and hang it around the neck. If he does so, it is makruh. But since it is not like sewing, no expiation is obligatory. Note: Those who always wear pajamas or pants and are accustomed to wearing underwear, they feel the izar opening all the time, even in sleep it opens; due to necessity of covering the awrah, tying a knot is not makruh for them. The principle is: if it reaches the level of sewing, then it is makruh. Evidence: (1) In this mursal hadith, do not tie with rope: from Ibn Jurayj that the Prophet saw a man tying a rope around his waist and said 'remove the rope' twice. This is disconnected. (Bayhaqi) (2) Tying with rope is makruh; this is a companion's practice: Ibn Umar did not tie the cloth, rather he tucked its end into his izar. (Bayhaqi) (3) This hadith states that sewn clothing is not allowed: from Abdullah ibn Umar: a man asked what garments to wear in ihram, the Prophet said: do not wear shirts, trousers, turbans, hooded cloaks, unless one has no sandals then wear khuffs cut below ankles, and do not wear anything touched by saffron or wars, and the muhrima woman should not wear niqab or gloves. (Bukhari and Muslim)
Source pages p. 343

Commentary
This ruling with proof addresses the method of wearing the izar in ihram. The izar should not be fastened by buttons, knots, or pins, as these imitate sewn garments. Doing so is makruh tanzihi, not makruh tahrimi, and does not require a dam (penalty). The commentary provides a practical note: for those unaccustomed to loose wraps, the necessity of covering the awrah may excuse tying, as long as it does not resemble sewing. The evidence includes a mursal hadith of the Prophet ordering removal of a rope belt, the practice of Ibn Umar who tucked rather than tied, and the famous hadith prohibiting sewn garments entirely. The Hanafi position is clear: the prohibition is on any fastening that resembles sewing; simple tucking or pinning to secure is allowed and not makruh.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): A disliked act; in Hanafi, it is not sinful but avoiding it is rewarded.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a muhrim ties his izar with a knot?
A) It is invalid (batil) and requires expiation
B) It is makruh but no penalty
C) It is allowed without any dislike
D) It is haram and requires a sacrifice

Key Takeaway
Tying the izar in ihram is makruh tanzihi, not haram, and no penalty is required.

Applying Perfume and Praying Two Rak'ahs Before Ihram
Recommending sunnah acts before ihram with hadith evidence for perfume.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended acts before ihram according to the Hanafi school and identify the evidence for applying perfume.

Core Idea
Perfume, two rak'ahs, and dua are sunnah before ihram — enhancing devotion, not obligation.

Before entering the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, the Hanafi school recommends a sequence of actions to prepare spiritually and physically. This passage from Thamaratun Najah outlines applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting a specific supplication. Understanding these sunan helps the pilgrim perform the rites with completeness and devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended acts
List the three actions mentioned: applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting the dua.
These are separate from the conditions of ihram itself.
2
Classify the legal ruling
Determine that these are sunnah muakkadah, not wajib. The Hanafi school emphasizes their recommendation.
Sunnah muakkadah means strongly recommended, but omission does not invalidate ihram.
3

The passage cites the hadith of Aisha (RA) who perfumed the Prophet (SAW) for ihram. This is found in Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
The prayer and dua have no explicit evidence cited here; they are based on general practice.
4

The order after wearing ihram garments is: perfume, then prayer, then supplication.
This sequence reflects the practice of the Prophet (SAW) and the early Muslims.

Knotting the Ihram Garment: Makruh, Not Haram
Ruling on not knotting or fastening the ihram garment with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on knotting the ihram garment and explain why no penalty is required, using the proofs cited.

Core Idea
Knotting the ihram garment is makruh, not haram — no fidyah because it does not turn into sewn clothing.

In his Thamaratun Najah, the author addresses a practical concern for those in ihram: how to fasten the lower garment without using sewn stitches. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the evidence, and the underlying principle that distinguishes makruh from haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act of knotting, buttoning, or tucking the ihram garment. The ruling is makruh (disliked) but no penalty (dam) is required.
The text says 'kareh wa la shay'a alayh' — disliked and nothing upon him.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites three proofs: (1) a mursal hadith about tying with a rope, (2) the practice of Ibn Umar who tucked instead of tying, and (3) the general hadith from Bukhari and Muslim listing prohibited sewn garments.
The mursal hadith is weak but supported by other evidence.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the general prohibition of sewn garments apply to knotting? The Hanafi position: the hadith prohibits actual sewing, not mere knotting. Knotting resembles sewing but is not equivalent, so it is only makruh.
The key distinction: knotting does not make the garment permanently sewn.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school and others may consider knotting as equivalent to sewing, making it haram and requiring fidyah. Hanafi distinguishes strongly.
This difference is a thamarah al-khilaf: practical consequence in penalty.
5
Evaluate the mufta bihi
The operative Hanafi ruling is makruh tanzihi; if necessity arises (e.g., covering awrah), it becomes permissible and not even makruh.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah from the matn.

The best: He should not put a button, nor tie it, nor tuck it. If he does so, it is disliked (makruh) and there is nothing upon him. (1295) And apply perfume... Explanation: In a lungi, do not put a knot, nor tie it with a rope, nor tear it and hang it around the neck. If done, it is makruh but since it is not like sewn garments, no penalty is required. Note: For those who always wear pajama or pants and are accustomed to wearing underwear, they often feel the lungi opening, so due to the compulsion of covering the awrah, tying a knot is not makruh for them. The principle is that if it reaches the level of sewn clothing, then it would be makruh. Evidence: (1) A mursal hadith from Ibn Jurayj that the Prophet saw a man with a rope and told him to remove it. (2) The practice of Ibn Umar that he did not tie the cloth but tucked its end into his izaar. (3) The hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar that the Prophet forbade wearing shirts, trousers, turbans, hooded cloaks, etc. for the muhrim.

Commentary
This lesson presents a ruling with proofs regarding the ihram garment. The author states that the best practice is not to attach buttons, tie knots, or tuck the garment. If one does so, it is makruh (disliked) but no penalty (dam) is required because it does not constitute wearing sewn clothing. The note clarifies that those who habitually wear pants/underwear may tie the lungi out of necessity to cover the awrah, and it is not makruh for them. The proofs include a mursal hadith (weak) about tying with a rope, the practice of Ibn Umar who tucked his garment instead of tying, and the well-known hadith from Bukhari and Muslim listing prohibited sewn garments. The underlying Hanafi principle is that actions which make the garment equivalent to sewn clothing are prohibited, but simple knotting does not reach that level, hence no fidyah is required.

Key Terms
يزر (yazurru): To put a button or knot the garment.
عقد ('aqada): To tie a knot using a rope or cloth.
خلل (khallala): To tuck the cloth into itself or pass it through a slit.

C) Permissible

Actions Before Ihram: Perfume, Two Rak'ahs, and Dua
Ruling with proof for sunnah acts before ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three recommended actions before ihram according to the Hanafi school and cite the hadith evidence for each.

Core Idea
Before entering ihram, apply perfume, pray two rak'ahs, and recite the dua for Hajj—these are Sunnah actions based on the Prophet's practice.

In this lesson, we study the recommended acts that precede the formal intention (niyyah) for Hajj. The matn instructs three steps: applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and supplicating for ease and acceptance. The commentary expands on each with hadith evidence from Aisha and Ibn Abbas. This lesson will help you understand the sunnah sequence and distinguish it from the prohibited use of perfume after ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions
State the three recommended actions before ihram as given in the matn: applying perfume, praying two rak'ahs, and reciting the dua.
The dua is 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajj...'
2
Understand the legal classification
Determine the hukm level: these are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized recommended), not wajib or fard. Omitting them is not sinful but loses the reward.
The Hanafi school holds that they are sunnah based on the hadith evidence.
3
Examine the evidence for perfume
Read the hadith of Aisha (ra) who said she applied perfume to the Prophet (peace be upon him) for his ihram and for his halal before tawaf.
Reference: Bukhari 1539, Abu Dawood 1745.
4
Examine the evidence for the prayer and dua
Read the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs at Dhu al-Hulayfah and then pronounced the talbiyah. The dua is derived from the Prophet's practice.
Reference: Abu Dawood 1770, Tirmidhi 819, Bukhari 1554.
5
Note the sequence and timing
After putting on the ihram garment, one applies perfume, then prays two rak'ahs, then recites the dua, and finally makes the niyyah for Hajj.
The perfume applied before ihram does not invalidate ihram; it is prohibited only after entering ihram.

ركعتين وقل اللهم انى اريد الحج فيسره لى وتقبله منى ترجمه : (۱۲۹۵) وخوشبولگا ، دورکعت نماز پڑھ ، اور کہہ "اے اللہ میں حج کا ارادہ کرتا ہوں میرے لئے اسے آسان کر دیجئے اور قبول فرمائیے۔ تشریح : کپڑا پہنے کے بعد خوشبو لگائے ، پھر دو رکعت نماز پڑھے، پھر یہ دعا پڑھے ( اللهم اني اريد الحج فيسره لي و تقبله منی ) اے اللہ میں حج کا ارادہ کرتا ہوں میرے لئے اسے آسان کر دیجئے اور قبول فرمائیے" وجه : (۱) خوشبو لگانے کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قالت كنت اطيب رسول الله لاحرامه حين يحرم و لحله قبل ان يطوف بالبيت - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الطیب عند الاحرام، ص ۲۰۸، نمبر ۱۵۳۹ را بوداود شریف ، باب الطيب عند الاحرام ، ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۱۷۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ احرام سے پہلے خوشبو لگائے (۲) دورکعت نماز پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قلت لعبد الله ابن عباس .... خرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاجا فلما صلى في مسجده بذي الحليفة ركعتيه أوجب في مجلسه فأهل بالحج حين فرغ من ركعتيه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی وقت الا حرام ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۷۰ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء متی احرم النبی ص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۸۱۹/ بخاری شریف ، باب الاهلال مستقبل القبلۃ ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۵۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے احرام باندھنے کے لئے دورکعت نماز پڑھی۔ اور اس حدیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ نماز کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھی۔
Two rak'ahs and say: O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me. Translation: (1295) And apply perfume, pray two rak'ahs, and say: O Allah, I intend Hajj... Explanation: After wearing the ihram garment, apply perfume, then pray two rak'ahs, then recite this dua. Evidence: (1) Hadith of Aisha that she used to apply perfume for the Prophet before ihram. (2) Hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs at Dhu al-Hulayfah and then recited talbiyah.
Source pages p. 344

Commentary
This lesson covers the Sunnah actions before entering ihram. The author instructs that after putting on the ihram garment, one should apply perfume, pray two rak'ahs, and then say the dua 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajj...'. The proofs are from the practice of the Prophet: Aisha applied perfume to him before ihram, and he prayed two rak'ahs at the miqat before pronouncing the talbiyah. Note that the perfume applied before ihram does not prevent the validity of ihram. The dua is a recommended supplication.

Key Terms
طيب (tib): Perfume; applying it before ihram is recommended.
ركعتين (rak'atayn): Two rak'ahs of prayer offered before ihram.

The Talbiyah: Its Wording and Permissible Additions
Ruling with proof on talbiyah wording and additions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum wording of the talbiyah and identify which additions are permissible according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The talbiyah is a sunnah that can be expanded upon; the Prophet's wording is sufficient, but adding the companion's additions is better.

In this lesson, we examine the ruling on reciting the talbiyah when entering ihram. The source text provides the exact wording from the Prophet and explicitly permits additional phrases. We will understand the legal status of the talbiyah and the scope of permissible additions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting the talbiyah after a prayer with intention of Hajj. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah).
The text says 'after your prayer' indicating a specific time.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Abdullah ibn Umar describing the Prophet's talbiyah and Ibn Umar's practice of adding words.
Hadith is from Muslim and Bukhari.
3
Analyse the wording
The minimum wording is: 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk, la sharika laka labbayk, inna al-hamda wa an-ni'mata wa al-mulka laka la sharika lak.' One may not decrease from this, but may add phrases like 'labbayka wa sa'dayka...'.
Additions are based on Ibn Umar's practice.
4
Note the practical application
After any prayer (e.g., sunnah of ihram or fard prayer), make the intention and recite the talbiyah. Adding is better.
The talbiyah can also be recited without a prayer, but the sunnah is after prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۲۹۶) ولبّ دُبُر صلوتک تنوى بها الحجّ وهی لبیک اللهم لبیک لا شریک لک لبیک ان الحمد والنعمة والملک لک لا شریک لک ولا تنقص من هذه الالفاظ شيئا وزڈفيها لبيك وسعديك والخیر کله بیدیک لبیک تشریح : نماز کے بعد حج کی نیت سے تلبیہ پڑھے تو احرام باندھا چلا جائے گا۔ تلبیہ کے جو الفاظ حضور کے ہیں اتنا پڑھے تب بھی کافی ہے، اور اس میں اضافہ کرے تو بہتر ہے۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں تلبیہ بھی ہے اور کیا اضافہ کرے وہ بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله له كان اذا استوت به راحلته قائمة عن ة عند مسجد ذو الحليفة اهل فقال : لبیک اللهم لبیک لبیک لا شریک لک لبیک ان الحمد والنعمة لك والملک لا شریک لک . قالوا وكان عبد الله بن عمر يقول هذه تلبية رسول الله الا الله قال قال نافع كان عبد الله يزيد مع هذا لبیک لبیک وسعدیک والخیر بیدیک لبیک والرغباء الیک و العمل (مسلم شریف، باب التلبية وصفتها و وقتها ص ۲۸۹، نمبر ۲۸۱۲/۱۱۸۴ / بخاری شریف، باب التلبية، ص ۲۵۱، نمبر ۱۵۴۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تلبیہ کس طرح پڑھے۔ اور عبد اللہ بن عمر کے عمل سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حضور کے تلبیہ کے علاوہ کچھ کلمات کی زیادتی بھی کی جاسکتی ہے۔
(1296) And say the talbiyah after your prayer, intending with it Hajj. It is: Labbayka Allahumma labbayk, la sharika laka labbayk, inna al-hamda wa an-ni'mata wa al-mulka laka la sharika lak. Do not decrease from these words, and add to them 'labbayka wa sa'dayka wa al-khayru kulluhu biyadayka labbayk'. Explanation: After the prayer, if he recites the talbiyah with the intention of Hajj, then he has entered ihram. Reciting just the words of the Prophet is sufficient, and adding to them is better. Evidence: Hadith of Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's talbiyah and the practice of Ibn Umar adding extra words.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This lesson explains the talbiyah, the declaration made when entering ihram. The author gives the exact wording from the Prophet: 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk...' and states that one should not decrease from these words but may add additional phrases such as 'labbayka wa sa'dayka...'. The proof is the hadith from Ibn Umar describing the Prophet's talbiyah and the practice of Ibn Umar adding extra words. The Hanafi position is that reciting the talbiyah is a recommended sunnah that formalizes the intention of ihram. The additional words are also sunnah, based on the companion's practice.

Key Terms
تلبيہ (talbiyah): The declaration recited to enter ihram, beginning with 'Labbayka Allahumma labbayk'.
لبيك (labbayk): 'Here I am' indicating response to Allah's call.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Entering Ihram: The Two Rak'ahs and Talbiyah
Explains the method of entering ihram with prayer and talbiyah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to perform the sunnah act of praying two rak'ahs before ihram and recite the talbiyah with the correct intention, distinguishing between the wajib element (talbiyah) and the sunnah addition.

Core Idea
Talbiyah with intention is wajib for ihram; adding extra words is sunnah.

This lesson explains the proper method of entering the state of ihram for Hajj. It covers the recommended two rak'ahs, the required talbiyah, and the evidence from the Prophet's practice that makes the talbiyah obligatory in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts
The passage prescribes two actions: praying two rak'ahs and then reciting the talbiyah with intention.
The two rak'ahs are sunnah; the talbiyah is wajib.
2
Understand the talbiyah wording
The minimum talbiyah is the Prophet's wording: 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk... la sharika lak.' Adding extra phrases like 'Labbayk wa sa'dayk...' is sunnah.
Do not reduce the words; additions are recommended.
3
Recognize the intention
The talbiyah must be recited with the explicit intention of entering ihram for Hajj (or Umrah).
The intention is what activates the ihram.
4
Note the evidence
Multiple hadith show the Prophet praying two rak'ahs and then reciting talbiyah. The term 'ahalla bi'l-hajj' is interpreted as both tying ihram and reciting talbiyah, proving wujub.
Hanafi school: talbiyah is wajib; Shafi'i school: sunnah.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل تركيب افعال الحج
ركعتين وقل اللهم انى اريد الحج فيسره لى وتقبله منى (۱۲۹۶) ولبّ دُبُر صلوتک تنوى بها الحجّ وهی لبیک اللهم لبیک لا شریک لک لبیک ان الحمد والنعمة والملک لک لا شریک لك ولا تنقص من هذه الالفاظ شيئا وزڈفيها لبیک وسعدیک والخیر کله بیدیک لبیک شریف ، باب الطيب عند الاحرام ، ص ۲۵۷، نمبر ۱۷۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ احرام سے پہلے خوشبو لگائے (۲) دورکعت نماز پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ قلت لعبد الله ابن عباس .... خرج رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حاجا فلما صلى في مسجده بذي الحليفة ركعتيه أوجب في مجلسه فأهل بالحج حين فرغ من ركعتيه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی وقت الا حرام ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۷۰ارترندی شریف ، باب ما جاء متی احرم النبی ص ۱۲۹ نمبر ۸۱۹/ بخاری شریف ، باب الاهلال مستقبل القبلۃ ص۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۵۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے احرام باندھنے کے لئے دورکعت نماز پڑھی۔ اور اس حدیث میں یہ بھی ہے کہ نماز کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھی۔
ترجمه : (۱۲۹۶) اور نماز کے بعد حج کی نیت سے تلبیہ پڑھ، تلبیہ یہ ہے لبیک اللهم لبیک لا شریک لک لبیک ان الحمد والنعمة والملک لک لا شریک لک ۔ حاضر ہوں اے اللہ حاضر ہوں ، کوئی آپ کا شریک نہیں حاضر ہوں ، بیشک حمد، نعمت، ملک آپ ہی کے لئے ہے، کوئی آپ کا شریک نہیں) ان الفاظ میں بھی کمی نہ کر، بلکہ اس میں لبیک و سعدیک و الـخـیـر کله بیدیک لبیک والرغبی الیک، ( حاضر ہوں آپ کی موافقت کرتا ہوں اور تمام قسم کی خیر آپ کے قبضہ میں ہے اور سب تمنا آپ کی طرف ہے ) کو بڑھا، اور زیادتی سنت ہے۔ تشریح : نماز کے بعد حج کی نیت سے تلبیہ پڑھے تو احرام باندھا چلا جائے گا۔ تلبیہ کے جو الفاظ حضور کے ہیں اتنا پڑھے تب بھی کافی ہے، اور اس میں اضافہ کرے تو بہتر ہے۔ وجه : (1) اس حدیث میں تلبیہ بھی ہے اور کیا اضافہ کرے وہ بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله له كان اذا استوت به راحلته قائمة عن ة عند مسجد ذو الحليفة اهل فقال : لبیک اللهم لبیک لبیک لا شریک لک لبیک ان الحمد والنعمة لك والملک لا شریک لک . قالوا وكان عبد الله بن عمر يقول هذه تلبية رسول الله الا الله قال قال نافع كان عبد الله يزيد مع هذا لبیک لبیک وسعدیک والخیر بیدیک لبیک والرغباء الیک و العمل (مسلم شریف، باب التلبية وصفتها و وقتها ص ۲۸۹، نمبر ۲۸۱۲/۱۱۸۴ / بخاری شریف، باب التلبية، ص ۲۵۱، نمبر ۱۵۴۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ تلبیہ کس طرح پڑھے۔ اور عبد اللہ بن عمر کے عمل سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ حضور کے تلبیہ کے علاوہ کچھ کلمات کی زیادتی بھی کی جاسکتی ہے۔
صلى الله
والرغبی الیک و الزيادة سنة (۱۲۹۷) فاذا لبيت ناويا فقد احرمت
ترجمه : (۱۲۹۷) جب تو نے نیت کے ساتھ تلبیہ پڑھا تو محرم ہو گیا۔
تشریح : احرام باندھنے کی نیت کے ساتھ تلبیہ پڑھے تو احرام باندھا چلا جائے گا اس لئے جب تلبیہ احرام کی نیت سے تلبیہ پڑھا تو محرم ہو گیا۔ وجه (۱) تلبیہ پڑھنے کو ہی احرام باندھنا کہتے ہیں۔ حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عائشة زوج النبي الله قالت خرجنا مع النبي الله في حجة الوداع ... واهلي بالحج ودعى العمرة . (بخاری شریف، باب کیف تھل الحائض والنفساء ص ۲۱۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۶) اس حدیث میں اصلی بالحج کا ترجمہ ہے کہ حج کا احرام باندھ لو اور یہ بھی ہے کہ حج کا تلبیہ پڑھو۔ اس لئے احرام باندھنے کے لئے تلبیہ پڑھنا واجب ہے۔ (۲) جابر بن عبد الله أنه حج مع رسول الله له يوم ساق البدن معه و قد أهلوا بالحج مفردا - ( بخاری شریف، باب استمع والقران والافراد با مج ص ۲۵۴ نمبر ۱۵۶۸) اس حدیث میں، کھلوا بالحج، ہے جس کا ترجمہ ہے حج کا احرام باندھو، اور اصل کا ترجمہ ہے تلبیہ پڑھو، اس لئے احرام باندھتے وقت تلبیہ پڑھناواجب ہے۔
Chapter: The composition of the actions of Hajj. Two rak'ahs and say: O Allah, I intend Hajj, so make it easy for me and accept it from me (1296). And recite the talbiyah after your prayer intending by it Hajj, and it is: Labbayk Allahumma labbayk, la sharika laka labbayk, inna al-hamda wa al-ni'mata wa al-mulka laka la sharika lak. And do not decrease anything from these words, and add in it: Labbayk wa sa'dayk wa al-khayru kulluhu bi-yadayka labbayk. Sharif, Bab al-Tib 'ind al-Ihram, p. 257, no. 1745. From this hadith it is known that before ihram one should apply perfume (2) and pray two rak'ahs; for this there is this hadith: I said to Abdullah ibn Abbas... The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, set out for Hajj, and when he prayed two rak'ahs in his mosque at Dhu al-Hulayfah, he made it obligatory in his sitting place and began the talbiyah for Hajj when he finished his two rak'ahs (Abu Dawud, Bab fi Waqt al-Ihram, p. 253, no. 1770; Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a Mata Ahrama al-Nabi, p. 129, no. 819; Bukhari, Bab al-Ihlal Mustaqbil al-Qibla, p. 252, no. 1554). In this hadith it is that the Prophet, peace be upon him, prayed two rak'ahs for tying the ihram. And in this hadith it is also that after prayer he recited the talbiyah. Translation: (1296) And after prayer recite the talbiyah with the intention of Hajj; the talbiyah is this: Labbayk Allahumma labbayk, la sharika laka labbayk, inna al-hamda wa al-ni'mata wa al-mulka laka la sharika lak. I am present, O Allah, I am present, no partner do You have, I am present. Indeed, all praise, blessing, and sovereignty are Yours; no partner do You have. Do not decrease in these words, rather add in it: Labbayk wa sa'dayk wa al-khayru kulluhu bi-yadayka labbayk wa al-raghba ilayk (I am present, complying with You, and all good is in Your hand, and all desire is towards You). And adding is Sunnah. Explanation: If one prays after prayer with the intention of Hajj and recites the talbiyah, then ihram is established. If one recites the words of the Prophet's talbiyah, that is sufficient, and if one adds to it, it is better. Evidence: (1) In this hadith there is the talbiyah and what addition to make is also there. From Abdullah ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, when his riding camel stood up with him at the mosque of Dhu al-Hulayfah, he began the talbiyah and said: Labbayk Allahumma labbayk, labbayk la sharika laka labbayk, inna al-hamda wa al-ni'mata laka wa al-mulka la sharika lak. They said: Abdullah ibn Umar used to say this is the talbiyah of the Messenger of Allah, and Naafi' said: Abdullah used to add to this: Labbayk labbayk wa sa'dayk wa al-khayru bi-yadayka labbayk wa al-raghba'u ilayka wa al-'amal (Muslim, Bab al-Talbiyah wa Sifatiha wa Waqtiha, p. 289, no. 2812/1184; Bukhari, Bab al-Talbiyah, p. 251, no. 1549). From this hadith it is known how to recite the talbiyah. And from the action of Abdullah ibn Umar it is also known that some words can be added beyond the talbiyah of the Prophet, peace be upon him. Peace be upon him. And al-raghba ilayk, and the addition is Sunnah (1297). So when you recite the talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. Translation: (1297) When you have recited the talbiyah with intention, you have become a muhrim. Explanation: If one recites the talbiyah with the intention of tying ihram, then ihram is tied; therefore when you recite the talbiyah with the intention of ihram, you have become a muhrim. Evidence: (1) Reciting the talbiyah is itself called tying ihram. There is a hadith: From Aisha, the wife of the Prophet, peace be upon him, she said: We set out with the Prophet, peace be upon him, for the Farewell Hajj... and he began the talbiyah for Hajj and called for Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab Kayfa Tuhill al-Ha'id wa al-Nufasa', p. 211, no. 1556). In this hadith, 'ahalla bi'l-hajj' is translated as 'tie the ihram of Hajj' and it also means 'recite the talbiyah for Hajj'. Therefore, for tying ihram, reciting the talbiyah is wajib. (2) Jabir ibn Abdullah that he performed Hajj with the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, the day he drove the sacrificial animals with him, and they had begun the talbiyah for Hajj alone (Bukhari, Bab al-Istimta' wa al-Qiran wa al-Ifrad bi'l-Hajj, p. 254, no. 1568). In this hadith, 'ahallu bi'l-hajj' is present, which is translated as 'tie the ihram of Hajj', and the original is translated as 'recite the talbiyah'. Therefore, at the time of tying ihram, reciting the talbiyah is wajib.
Source pages p. 345

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the method of entering ihram for Hajj. The author, Thamaratun Najah, presents the core text (matn) that prescribes two actions: praying two rak'ahs and then reciting the talbiyah with intention. The talbiyah wording is given as the well-known formula: 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' ending with 'la sharika lak'. It is then noted that one should not reduce these words but may add additional phrases like 'Labbayk wa sa'dayk wa al-khayru kulluhu bi-yadayka labbayk wa al-raghba ilayk'. The commentary (Tashrih) explains that reciting this talbiyah after prayer with the intention of Hajj establishes ihram, and that the minimum is the Prophet's words, while adding is better and considered Sunnah. The evidence (Wajh) cites multiple hadith: the hadith of Ibn Abbas showing the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs before ihram; the hadith of Ibn Umar detailing the talbiyah and the permissibility of addition; and the hadith of Aisha and Jabir establishing that 'ahalla bi'l-hajj' means both tying ihram and reciting talbiyah, making talbiyah wajib (obligatory) according to the Hanafi school. The author concludes that adding to the talbiyah is Sunnah, and that reciting it with intention is what actually enters one into ihram.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The specific phrase uttered by the pilgrim to declare intention for Hajj/Umrah, starting with 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk'.
احرام (ihram): The sacred state entered by the pilgrim for Hajj/Umrah, marked by intention and talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Fard
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
The talbiyah is the essential wajib act for entering ihram; the two rak'ahs are a sunnah preparation.

Prohibitions During Ihram: Refth, Fusooq, Jidal
Lists and explains the three prohibited acts for a muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three categories of prohibited acts for a muhrim and explain the Hanafi interpretation of rafath as including both the act and speech.

Core Idea
Three acts are absolutely prohibited during ihram: sexual talk/speech (rafath), sin (fusooq), and argumentation (jidal) — derived from Surah al-Baqarah 2:197.

This lesson examines the three specific prohibitions Allah has placed on a person in the state of ihram. Based on the clear text of the Quran, the muhrim must avoid rafath, fusooq, and jidal. We will explore the definitions, the scope of rafath, and the evidence that makes these acts forbidden.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibitions
List the three categories: rafath, fusooq, jidal. Note the primary definition of each: rafath as sexual intercourse, fusooq as sin/disobedience, jidal as argumentation.
The text gives both a primary and secondary definition for rafath.
2
Understand the scope of rafath
Examine the two opinions: some restrict rafath to the act of intercourse; others include speaking about it in front of women and any obscene speech.
The Hanafi mufta bihi follows the broader definition.
3
Locate the Quranic proof
Find the verse 2:197: 'So whoever intends Hajj therein, then [let there be] no rafath, nor fusooq, nor jidal during Hajj.' Note the word 'la' which is a prohibition particle.
The verse directly prohibits these three during Hajj, which extends to the entire state of ihram.
4
Apply the Hanafi usul principle
In Hanafi usul, the particle 'la' for prohibition (nahy) indicates tahrim (prohibition). Thus these acts are haram for the muhrim.
This is a zanni dalala, meaning the ruling is still subject to interpretation (e.g., definition of rafath).

Source Text

Translation: (1298) Now avoid rafath, and it is sexual intercourse, and some scholars have said mentioning it in front of women, and obscene speech, and avoid fusooq, and sins, and argumentation with friends and servants. Explanation: Allah has forbidden the muhrim from sexual intercourse, argumentation, and sinful talk; the muhrim should avoid these things in the state of ihram. Evidence: (1) 'So whoever intends (fard) Hajj therein, then [let there be] no rafath, nor fusooq, nor jidal during Hajj.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:197). From this verse it is known that whoever ties ihram should avoid talk of sexual intercourse, sinful talk, and argumentative speech. Lexicon: al-rafath: talk of sexual intercourse; al-fusooq: sinful talk; al-jidal: argumentative talk.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prohibitions incumbent upon a person in the state of ihram. The core text (matn) commands the muhrim to avoid three categories: rafath, fusooq, and jidal. The author provides the primary meaning of rafath as sexual intercourse, but also notes a secondary interpretation: speaking about it in front of women, as well as any obscene speech. Fusooq encompasses all sins and disobedience, while jidal refers to argumentation with fellow pilgrims and servants. The commentary (Tashrih) emphasizes that Allah has prohibited these acts for the muhrim. The evidence (Wajh) is the Quranic verse 2:197, which explicitly prohibits rafath, fusooq, and jidal during Hajj. The verse uses the general term 'rafath' which, in the Hanafi school, is understood to include both the act of sexual intercourse and speech related to it, as indicated by the alternative opinion cited. This prohibition applies throughout the state of ihram, and violation requires expiation (dam) as per other texts. The passage also includes a lexical note defining each term concisely.

Key Terms
رفث (rafath): Sexual intercourse or explicitly talking about it in the presence of women; also any obscene speech.
فسوق (fusooq): Disobedience, sin, or any act that is morally wrong.
جدال (jidal): Argumentation, quarreling, or disputation, especially with companions and servants.

Prohibition of Hunting Land Game During Ihram
States the prohibition of killing, pointing to, or directing towards land game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited actions related to land game during ihram and cite the Quranic evidence (5:95) for the prohibition.

Core Idea
Killing, pointing to, or directing towards land game is all haram for the muhrim — even indirect assistance is forbidden.

This passage from a Hanafi fiqh text clarifies the scope of the prohibition of hunting during ihram. While the Quran explicitly forbids killing land game, the Hanafi school extends this to any form of assistance, such as pointing to or guiding a hunter. Understanding this ruling helps the muhrim avoid actions that incur sin and potential penalty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited actions
Read the matn and commentary to list exactly what is forbidden: killing land game, pointing to it, and directing someone to it.
These three are explicitly mentioned.
2
Locate the primary evidence
The proof is the Quranic verse 5:95. Identify the key phrase 'la taqtulu' (do not kill) which indicates a clear prohibition.
The verse is quoted partially; the full verse is in Surah al-Ma'idah.
3
Analyze the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
In Hanafi usul, the imperative form of prohibition (la + verb) indicates haram. The penalty clause confirms the seriousness. The extension to pointing and directing is based on sadd al-dhara'i' (blocking the means to evil).
This is a common Hanafi principle.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
Consider: A muhrim sees a gazelle and gestures to a non-muhrim friend to hunt it. Determine the ruling.
The gesture counts as 'isharah' and is haram.
5
Distinguish from permissible acts
Note that sea game is permitted; the prohibition is specific to land game. Also, unintentional killing (without intent) does not incur sin but still requires expiation.
The verse mentions 'intentionally' for the penalty.

Source Text

وقتل صيد البر والاشارة اليه والدلالة عليه
ترجمه : (۱۲۹۹) اور خشکی کے شکار کے قتل سے، اس کی طرف اشارہ کرنے سے،اس کی طرف رہنمائی سے۔
تشریح : احرام کی حالت میں خشکی کے جانور کا شکار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، اس کی طرف اشارہ کرنا یا کسی شکار کرنے والے کی رہنمائی کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے

And the killing of land game, and pointing to it, and directing to it. Translation: (1299) And from killing land game, from pointing towards it, from guiding towards it. Explanation: In the state of ihram, it is not permissible to hunt land animals; pointing towards it or guiding a hunter is also not permissible. Evidence: (1) Hunting in the state of ihram is forbidden by this verse: 'O you who have believed, do not kill game while you are in the state of ihram. And whoever of you kills it intentionally - the penalty is an equivalent from livestock, judged by two just men among you as an offering reaching the Ka'bah.' (Surah al-Ma'idah, verse 95).
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prohibition of hunting land game during ihram. The core text (matn) prohibits three actions: killing land game, pointing towards it (to indicate its location to a hunter), and directing or guiding someone to it. The commentary (Tashrih) confirms that all these are impermissible for a muhrim. The evidence (Wajh) is the Quranic verse 5:95, which explicitly forbids killing game while in ihram and prescribes a penalty (jaza') of a livestock equivalent. The verse uses the general term 'la taqtulu' (do not kill), which by consensus includes prohibition. The Hanafi school extends this prohibition to indirect assistance like pointing and directing, as these are means to the prohibited act. The verse also mentions intentional killing, implying that unintentional killing does not incur sin but still requires expiation. The author cuts off the verse mid-ayat, but the ruling is clear. This prohibition is specific to land game; sea game is permitted as per other texts.

Key Terms
صيد البر (sayd al-barr): Land game, i.e., wild animals that inhabit the land.
اشارة (isharah): Pointing to the game to indicate its location to a hunter.
دلالة (dalalah): Directing or guiding someone to the game.

Key Terms from Source Passage
