Key Takeaway
During ihram, not only killing land game but also any form of assistance (pointing, directing) is haram, based on the Quranic prohibition and the principle of sadd al-dhara'i'.

Ruling on Talbiyah with Intention for Ihram
Ruling on entering ihram through talbiyah with intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talbiyah for ihram and identify the evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Talbiyah with intention is wajib for entering ihram; omission requires a dam.

This lesson examines the role of talbiyah in entering the state of ihram. The source passage presents a clear rule: reciting talbiyah with intention constitutes ihram. It then provides two hadith proofs to establish that talbiyah is an obligatory component. Understanding this distinction helps ensure the validity of one's Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting talbiyah with intention for ihram. The ruling is that this enters one into ihram, and the talbiyah itself is wajib (obligatory).
The passage states 'تلبیہ پڑھنا واجب ہے'.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites two hadith from Bukhari. The first from Aisha shows the Prophet (pbuh) initiating ihram by talbiyah. The second from Jabir equates 'ahalla' with both entering ihram and reciting talbiyah.
Hadith references: Bukhari no.1556 and 1568.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'ahalla' in the hadith is understood by the Hanafi school as a command to recite talbiyah, and it is used interchangeably with entering ihram. This linguistic connection makes talbiyah a requirement.
In Hanafi usul, imperative forms indicate obligation (wujub) unless there is a contrary indicator.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school views talbiyah as sunnah, not wajib, based on a different interpretation of the same evidence.
The practical difference: if omitted, Shafi'i do not require a dam.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that talbiyah is wajib at the time of ihram. Omission requires a dam but does not invalidate ihram.
This is the relied-upon view in the school.

Source Text

When you recite talbiyah with intention, you have entered ihram. Translation: (1297) When you recited talbiyah with intention, then you became muhrim. Explanation: If one recites talbiyah with the intention of tying ihram, then ihram is considered tied. Therefore, when one recites talbiyah with the intention of ihram, he becomes muhrim. Therefore, reciting talbiyah while entering ihram is obligatory.

This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the method of entering ihram. The matn states a concise rule: when one recites talbiyah with intention, he has entered ihram. The Urdu commentary expands: the intention (niyyah) combined with the recital of talbiyah constitutes entering ihram. The author then provides two hadith proofs to establish that talbiyah is integral to ihram. The first hadith from Aisha shows that the Prophet (peace be upon him) initiated ihram by talbiyah. The second from Jabir reinforces that 'ahalla' means both to enter ihram and to recite talbiyah. Based on these, the author concludes that reciting talbiyah is wajib (obligatory) at the time of entering ihram. Hanafi fiqh holds that talbiyah is a necessary component (wajib) of ihram; omitting it does not invalidate ihram but requires a sacrifice (dam).

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The recitation of 'Labbaik Allahumma labbaik...' as a declaration of intent for Hajj/Umrah.
احرام (ihram): The sacred state entered for Hajj/Umrah, marked by intention and prohibitions.

Key Takeaway

Hunting Prohibitions in Ihram: Direct Killing and Assistance
Ruling on prohibitions related to hunting land game in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific prohibitions on land game during ihram (killing, pointing, guiding) and explain the evidence from Quran and hadith.

Core Idea
A muhrim cannot kill land game, point to it, or guide a hunter — both direct and indirect assistance are prohibited.

This lesson examines the specific rulings related to hunting while in the state of ihram. While sea game is permitted, land game is completely prohibited, including any form of assistance. Understanding the evidence for these prohibitions helps you appreciate the sanctity of ihram and avoid common misconceptions about indirect involvement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the three prohibited actions: killing land game (haram), pointing to it (haram), guiding a hunter to it (haram). Note that eating land game hunted by a non-muhrim is permissible if no assistance was given.
The ruling is based on clear textual evidence.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
Read Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95-96. The first verse prohibits killing game in ihram. The second explicitly permits sea game and forbids land game. Notice the direct command 'la taqtulu' (do not kill) which indicates prohibition.
The Quran makes a clear distinction between land and sea.
3
Analyze the hadith on pointing and guiding
Study the hadith of Abu Qatada. The Prophet (peace be upon him) asked whether anyone had pointed or helped. Only when the companions answered 'no' did he permit eating the meat. This implies that pointing or helping invalidates the permission.
The hadith is found in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Connect the evidence to the rulings
For killing, the Quranic prohibition is direct. For pointing/guiding, the hadith establishes that even indirect assistance is included. The reasoning is that such actions contribute to the killing.
Hanafi fiqh treats both as haram, with a penalty (jaza') for killing and sin for pointing/guiding.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Consider a muhrim who sees a deer and silently gestures to a non-muhrim companion to hunt it. According to the hadith, this gesture is prohibited. The companion may still hunt, but the muhrim incurs sin.
The key is the muhrim's involvement, even if minimal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقتل صيد البر والاشارة اليه والدلالة عليه
ترجمه : (۱۲۹۹) اور خشکی کے شکار کے قتل سے، اس کی طرف اشارہ کرنے سے،اس کی طرف رہنمائی سے۔ تشریح : احرام کی حالت میں خشکی کے جانور کا شکار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے، اس کی طرف اشارہ کرنا یا کسی شکار کرنے والے کی رہنمائی کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے وجه : (۱) احرام کی حالت میں شکار کرنا اس آیت سے حرام ہے. يآيها الذین امنوا لا تقتلوا الصيد و انتم حرم و من قتله منكم متعمدا فجزاء مثل ما قتل من النعم يحكم به ذوا عدل منكم هديا بلغ الكعبة ( آیت ۹۵،سورة مائدہ ۵ ) اس آیت میں ہے کہ احرام کی حالت میں شکار مت کرو۔ (۲) اس آیت میں بھی ہے۔ احــل لــكــم صـيـد البـحـر وطعامه متاعا لكم وللسيارة وحرم عليكم صيد البر مادمتم حرما. ( آیت ۹۶ سورۃ المائدۃ ۵ ) اس آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ سمندر کا شکار کرنا احرام کی حالت میں جائز ہے۔ لیکن خشکی کا شکار کرنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ (۳) شکار کی طرف اشارہ کرنا جائز نہیں اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عبد الله بن ابي قتادة ان اباه اخبره ان رسول الله خرج حاجا فخرجوا معه ... فاكلنا من لحمها (لحم الصيد ثم قلنا انأكل لحم صید و نحن محرمون فحملنا ما بقى من لحمها قال امنكم احد امره ان يحمل عليها او اشار اليها؟ قالوا لا قال فكلوا ما بقى من لحمها ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب لا يشير المحرم الى الصيد لكي يعتاده الحلال ص ۲۴۶ نمبر ۱۸۲۴) (۴) اور مسلم میں ہے ۔ هل منكم احد امره او اشار اليه بشيء قال قالوا لا قال فكلوا ما بقى من لحمها اور حضرت شعبہ کی روایت میں ہے۔ قال : أشرتم أو أعنتم أو أصدتم ؟ (مسلم شریف ، باب تحریم الصيد الماكول البرى او ما اصلہ ذلک علی المحرم، کتاب الحج ص ۹۶ نمبر ۲۸۵۶٫۲۸۵۵/۱۱۹۶) اس حدیث میں
ہے کہ محرم کے لئے شکار کی طرف اشارہ کرنا یا رہنمائی کرنا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔
And killing land game, and indicating it, and guiding to it. Translation: (1299) And from killing land game, from pointing towards it, from guiding to it. Explanation: In the state of ihram, hunting land animals is not permissible. Pointing towards it or guiding a hunter is also not permissible. Evidence: (1) Hunting in ihram is haram by this verse: 'O you who believe, do not kill game while you are in ihram...' (Quran 5:95). This verse prohibits hunting in ihram. (2) Also in this verse: 'Lawful to you is game from the sea and its food as provision for you and for travelers, but forbidden to you is game from the land as long as you are in ihram.' (Quran 5:96). From this verse, sea game is permissible in ihram, but land game is not. (3) Pointing towards game is not permissible; the proof is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada that his father informed him that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went out for Hajj and they went with him... We ate from its meat (the meat of the game). Then we said, 'We eat the meat of game while we are muhrim?' We carried the remaining meat. He said, 'Is there anyone among you who commanded to carry it or pointed towards it?' They said no. He said, 'Eat what remains of its meat.' (Bukhari, Bab la yushir al-muhrim ila al-said li kay ya‘tadahu al-hill, p.246 no.1824) (4) And in Muslim: 'Is there anyone among you who commanded him or pointed to him anything?' They said no. He said, 'Eat what remains of its meat.' And in the narration of Shu‘bah: he said, 'Did you point, or help, or hunt?' (Muslim, Bab tahrim al-said al-ma’kul al-barri... kitab al-hajj, p.96 no.2856/2855/1196) In this hadith, it is established that pointing or guiding to game is not permissible for a muhrim.
Source pages p. 346

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on hunting prohibitions in ihram. The matn forbids killing land game, pointing to it, or guiding someone to it. The commentary explains that land hunting is haram based on Quran 5:95 and 5:96, which distinguish between sea (permissible) and land (forbidden). Additionally, hadith evidence shows that even pointing or indicating the location of game is impermissible, as the Prophet (peace be upon him) did not penalize only when no such action occurred. Hanafi fiqh considers these actions as violating the sanctity of ihram, requiring a penalty (jaza’) for killing, and lesser sin for pointing.

Key Terms
صيد البر (sayd al-barr): Land game, i.e., wild animals that live on land (excluding domestic animals).
صيد البحر (sayd al-bahr): Sea game, fish and marine creatures, permissible for muhrim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling regarding a muhrim pointing at a land animal so that a non-muhrim can hunt it?
A) Permissible
B) Makruh
C) Haram
D) Mustahab

Key Takeaway
A muhrim is prohibited from killing, pointing to, or guiding hunters to land game, based on Quran and hadith.

Prohibition of Sewn Garments, Turban, and Khuffs in Ihram
Ruling on prohibited clothing items in ihram with hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited items for a male muhrim and explain the sole exception for khuffs based on the hadith, including the condition for its permissibility.

Core Idea
A male muhrim must avoid all body-fitted sewn garments; khuffs are allowed only when cut below the ankles and sandals are unavailable.

Ihram is a sacred state with specific dress rules. The most common prohibition is sewn garments, but the scope includes turbans and leather socks. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof from the hadith of Ibn Umar, and the single exception recognized in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited items
The passage explicitly names sewn garments (al-makhit), turban (al-‘imamah), and khuffs (al-khuffayn). Understand that these are all tailored to the body.
2
Understand the general principle
The Hanafi school extends the prohibition to any garment made to fit the body, whether sewn or knitted. Anything that takes the shape of a limb is included.
3
Recognize the exception
Khuffs are normally prohibited, but if the muhrim lacks sandals, he may wear khuffs cut below the ankles so they resemble sandals. This is a conditional allowance (rukhsa).
4
Analyze the hadith proof
The hadith of Abdullah ibn Umar lists six prohibited items and the exception. The phrase 'la yalbas' (should not wear) indicates prohibition. The exception for khuffs is explicitly mentioned.
5
Apply the ruling
In practice, a male muhrim avoids all shirts, pants, turbans, and full socks. If he cannot find sandals, he may wear socks cut below the ankles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولبس المخيط والعمامة والخفّين
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۰) سلے ہوئے کپڑے ، عمامہ، موزے پہننے سے بچے۔
تشريح : اصول یہ ہے کہ مرد محرم سلا ہوا کپڑا نہ پہنے۔ یہ سب سلے ہوئے کپڑے ہیں اس لئے ان کو نہ پہنے۔ اس میں ہے کہ موزہ بھی نہ پہنے کیونکہ موزہ بھی سلا ہوا ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ چپل نہ ہو تو موزہ کو ٹخنے کے نیچے سے کاٹ دے تا کہ چپل کی طرح ہو جائے پھر اس کو پہن سکتا ہے۔ وجه: اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رجلا قال يا رسول الله ما يلبس المحرم من الثياب؟
صلى الله
قال رسول الله علم لا يلبس القميص ولا العمائم ولا السراويلات ولا البرانس ولا الخفاف الا احد لايجد نـعـلـيـن فـلـيـلـبـس خـفـيـن وليقطعهما اسفل من الكعبين ولا تلبسوا من الثياب شيئا مسه زعفران او ورس.
( بخاری شریف ، باب مالا یلبس الحمر من الثياب، ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۵۴ر مسلم شریف، باب مابا للحرم حج وعمرة لبسه ومالا بار ، ص ۴۸۵ نمبر ۱۷۹۱۱۱۷۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما یلبس الحرم، نمبر ۱۸۲۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قمیص ، عمامہ، پائجامہ اور ٹوپی پہننا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور موزہ پہننا بھی جائز نہیں۔ اصول جسم کے ساخت کا جو کپڑا بنا ہوا ہو مرد کے لئے اس کو پہننا ممنوع ہے، چاہے سی کر بنایا ہو، یا بن کر ساخت کا بنایا ہو۔
And wearing sewn garments, the turban, and the khuffs. Translation: (1300) Avoid sewn clothes, turban, and socks. Explanation: The principle is that a male muhrim should not wear sewn clothes. These are all sewn garments, so he should not wear them. Included is that he should not wear khuffs because khuffs are also sewn. However, if he does not have sandals, he may cut the khuffs below the ankles so that they become like sandals, then he can wear them. Evidence: The proof is this hadith: from Abdullah ibn Umar that a man said, 'O Messenger of Allah, what clothes may the muhrim wear?' The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'He should not wear shirts, turbans, trousers, hooded cloaks, or khuffs, except for one who cannot find sandals. In that case, let him wear khuffs and cut them below the ankles. And do not wear any garment that has been touched by saffron or wars.' (Bukhari, Bab ma la yalbas al-muhrim min al-thiyab, p.250 no.154?; Muslim, etc.) From this hadith, it is learned that wearing shirts, turbans, trousers, and caps is not permissible. And wearing khuffs is also not permissible. The principle: any garment made tailored for the body is prohibited for men to wear, whether sewn or knitted into a shape.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the dress code for a male muhrim. The matn forbids three specific items: sewn garments (makhit), turban (‘imamah), and khuffs (leather socks). The commentary explains the general principle: anything sewn to fit the body is prohibited. Khuffs are included as they are sewn. However, an exception is made if one lacks sandals: the khuffs may be cut below the ankles to resemble sandals, making them permissible. The proof comes from the famous hadith of Ibn Umar listing what the muhrim should not wear. The Hanafi school extends the prohibition to any garment tailored or shaped to the body, even if not sewn, such as knitted items. This is a key difference from other schools that may allow certain types.

Key Terms
المخيط (al-makhit): Sewn garments; any cloth sewn into a shape fitting the body.
الخفين (al-khuffayn): Leather socks or boots that cover the feet and ankles.
العمامة (al-‘imamah): Turban, a head covering wrapped around the head.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When may a male muhrim wear khuffs (leather socks) in ihram?
A) When the weather is cold
B) When he cannot find sandals and cuts them below the ankles
C) When they are not sewn
D) When he is traveling by plane

Key Takeaway
A male muhrim must avoid all tailored garments; the only exception is khuffs cut below the ankles when sandals are unavailable.

Prohibition of Covering Head and Face in Ihram
Ruling with proof from ahad hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a male muhrim covering his head or face and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Covering the head and face is haram for a male muhrim, even in death.

The prohibitions of ihram are well-known, but the specific ruling on covering the head and face is often misunderstood. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, supported by a hadith that extends the prohibition beyond life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage clearly states that covering the head and the face is prohibited for a male muhrim. The ruling is haram.
Women are exempt from face covering prohibition; they may cover their face loosely.
2
Locate the dalil
The commentary begins citing a hadith from Ibn Abbas about a muhrim who died from a camel fall. The hadith is incomplete in the text, but in full it states that the deceased should not have his head covered, indicating the prohibition applies even after death.
The hadith is ahad, thus zanni al-thubut, but the school relies on it.
3
Understand the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's instruction not to cover the head of a deceased muhrim shows that covering the head contradicts the state of ihram. This textual evidence supports the prohibition.
The illah (effective cause) is that covering removes the distinguishing signs of ihram.
4
Note the cross-madhhab status
This ruling is muttafaq alayh across the four schools for men, though some allow covering for necessity. The Hanafi position is strict: it remains haram unless a genuine need requires fidya.
The mufta bihi is prohibition; if covered, fidya (redemption) is wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وتغطية الرأس والوجه
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۱) چہرہ اور سر کے چھپانے سے بچے۔
تشريح : 
وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس أن رجلا أو قصته راحلته و هو محرم فمات فقال رسول الله
And covering the head and the face. Translation: (1301) Avoid covering the face and head. Explanation: Evidence: (1) The hadith is: from Ibn Abbas that a man fell from his camel while he was muhrim and died, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said...
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on covering the head and face for a male muhrim. The matn prohibits covering both the head and the face. The commentary begins the evidence with a hadith from Ibn Abbas about a muhrim who died, but the text is incomplete. In Hanafi fiqh, covering the head (including hair) and face is prohibited for men during ihram. Women may cover their faces but not wear a niqab that touches the skin. The ruling for men is based on the principle that the head should be uncovered. The incomplete hadith likely mentions that the deceased muhrim should not have his head covered in burial, indicating the prohibition.

Key Terms
تغطية الرأس (taghtiyat al-ra’s): Covering the head; includes any material placed on the head.
تغطية الوجه (taghtiyat al-wajh): Covering the face; includes veils or any cloth over the face.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling for a male muhrim who intentionally covers his head with a turban?
A) Permissible because it is not a cap
B) Makruh tahrimi, no expiation
C) Haram, and fidya is required
D) Permissible if he makes intention to uncover later

Key Takeaway
Covering the head or face with any material is haram for a male muhrim, backed by the hadith of the deceased muhrim, and requires fidya if violated.

Prohibition of Stitched Clothes for the Muhrim
Ruling and proof for prohibition of stitched garments for men in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on stitched garments for a male muhrim, identify the evidence from the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar, and explain the exception for socks when sandals are unavailable.

Core Idea
A muhrim must not wear any garment that conforms to the body—whether sewn or knitted—except socks cut below the ankles if sandals are absent.

This lesson examines a fundamental ruling of ihram: the prohibition of stitched and body-fitting clothes for men. The author presents the rule and then supports it with a well-known hadith. You will learn not only what is prohibited but also the reasoning behind the exception for socks. Understanding this ruling is crucial for anyone performing Hajj or Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of wearing stitched clothes for a male muhrim. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
The source states 'سلے ہوئے کپڑے... پہننے سے بچے' meaning avoid; the hadith uses 'لا يلبس' which is a prohibition.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Umar narrated by Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud. The hadith lists prohibited items.
This is a Sunnah ahad, but accepted as binding in Hanafi school.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The imperative 'لا يلبس' (he should not wear) is a nahy (prohibition), which according to Hanafi usul indicates tahrim unless there is a qarinah for karahah. Here, no such qarinah exists.
The prohibition is general: 'لا يلبس القميص...'
4
Note the exception
The hadith includes an exception: if a person does not have sandals (na'layn), he may wear socks (khuffayn) but must cut them below the ankles so they become like sandals.
This exception applies only to socks, not other garments.
5
Understand the underlying principle
The author explains that any garment that is made for the body structure, whether sewn or knitted, is prohibited. This includes items not explicitly mentioned in the hadith but sharing the same 'illa (effective cause).
Examples: knitted caps, gloves, or body-fitting undershirts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۰) سلے ہوئے کپڑے ، عمامہ، موزے پہننے سے بچے۔
تشريح : اصول یہ ہے کہ مرد محرم سلا ہوا کپڑا نہ پہنے۔ یہ سب سلے ہوئے کپڑے ہیں اس لئے ان کو نہ پہنے۔ اس میں ہے کہ موزہ بھی نہ پہنے کیونکہ موزہ بھی سلا ہوا ہوتا ہے۔ البتہ چپل نہ ہو تو موزہ کو ٹخنے کے نیچے سے کاٹ دے تا کہ چپل کی طرح ہو جائے پھر اس کو پہن سکتا ہے۔
وجه: اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رجلا قال يا رسول الله ما يلبس المحرم من الثياب؟
صلى الله
قال رسول الله علم لا يلبس القميص ولا العمائم ولا السراويلات ولا البرانس ولا الخفاف الا احد لايجد نـعـلـيـن فـلـيـلـبـس خـفـيـن وليقطعهما اسفل من الكعبين ولا تلبسوا من الثياب شيئا مسه زعفران او ورس.
( بخاری شریف ، باب مالا یلبس الحمر من الثياب، ص ۲۵۰ نمبر ۱۵۴ر مسلم شریف، باب مابا للحرم حج وعمرة لبسه ومالا بار ، ص ۴۸۵ نمبر ۱۷۹۱۱۱۷۷ ابوداؤد شریف، باب ما یلبس الحرم، نمبر ۱۸۲۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ قمیص ، عمامہ، پائجامہ اور ٹوپی پہننا جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور موزہ پہننا بھی جائز نہیں۔ اصول جسم کے ساخت کا جو کپڑا بنا ہوا ہو مرد کے لئے اس کو پہننا ممنوع ہے، چاہے سی کر بنایا ہو، یا بن کر ساخت کا بنایا ہو۔
Translation: (1300) Avoid wearing stitched clothes, turban, and socks.
Explanation: The principle is that a male muhrim should not wear stitched clothes. All these are stitched clothes, so he should not wear them. It includes that he should not wear socks because socks are also stitched. However, if he does not have sandals, he should cut the socks below the ankles so that they become like sandals, then he can wear them.
Evidence: The proof is this hadith: From ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Umar that a man said, O Messenger of Allah, what clothes may the muhrim wear? The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: He should not wear the shirt, nor the turban, nor the trousers, nor the hooded cloak, nor the socks – unless one does not find sandals, then he may wear socks and cut them below the ankles. And do not wear any garment that has been touched by saffron or wars. (Bukhari, Bab Ma La Yalbas al-Muhrim min al-Thiyab, p.250 no.154?; Muslim, Bab Ma Yabah li al-Muhrim Hajj aw ‘Umra Labsuhu wa Ma La Yabah, p.485 no.1791/1177; Abu Dawud, Bab Ma Yalbas al-Muhrim, no.1823) From this hadith it is understood that wearing the shirt, turban, trousers, and cap is not permissible. And wearing socks is also not permissible. The principle: any garment that is made for the body structure, for a man, wearing it is prohibited, whether sewn or knitted structurally.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage states the ruling (hukm) on prohibited clothing for a male muhrim. The author begins with the tarjumah (translation) of the original matn, then provides tashrih (explanation). The ruling is that a muhrim must avoid three types of garments: stitched clothes (makhit), the turban (‘imamah), and socks (khuffayn). The explanation clarifies the principle: any garment that is made to fit the body shape, whether sewn or knitted, is prohibited. This includes the shirt, turban, trousers, and cap. Socks are also prohibited because they are stitched. However, an exception is made for a person who has no sandals: he may wear socks provided he cuts them below the ankles so they resemble sandals. The proof (wajh) is the famous hadith of Ibn ‘Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) which lists items not to be worn. The hadith is a strong evidence (Sunnah ahad) but accepted by the Hanafi school as binding. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it is a well-established ruling from the core books.

Key Terms
سلے ہوئے کپڑے (silay hu’e kapray): Any garment that is sewn or made to fit the body shape, including shirts, trousers, caps, turbans, and socks.
مخيط (makhit): Stitched garment – anything sewn or tailored that is not a wrap (izar or rida).
موزہ (moza): Socks or stockings, considered stitched and thus prohibited unless cut below ankles.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a male muhrim do if he has no sandals?
A) Wear socks as they are.
B) Cut the socks below the ankles to make them like sandals.
C) Wear socks but pay fidya.
D) Walk barefoot.

Key Takeaway
A male muhrim must avoid all body-conforming garments; socks are only allowed if cut below the ankles when sandals are unavailable.

Prohibition of Covering Head and Face in Ihram
Ruling and proof for prohibition of covering head and face for muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a male muhrim covering his head or face and explain the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Covering the head or face is haram for a male muhrim, as the Prophet explicitly prohibited it even for the deceased muhrim.

In this lesson, we examine a clear prohibition in Hajj: the ban on covering the head and face for those in ihram. The author presents two hadith proofs, one from the treatment of a deceased muhrim and another listing prohibited garments. Understanding this ruling prevents common violations during pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on covering the head (ra's) and face (wajh) for a male muhrim. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
The prohibition applies only to men; women cover their heads but not faces while in ihram.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: (1) The Prophet's instruction for a deceased muhrim: 'Do not cover his head or his face'; (2) The hadith listing prohibited garments for the muhrim, which includes the turban and cap.
Both are ahad hadith, but they are authentic and the ruling is agreed upon.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negative command 'la takhmiru' (do not cover) indicates prohibition. The second hadith implies head covering is prohibited because turbans and caps cover the head.
The first hadith explicitly mentions both head and face; the second adds other garments.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and tarjih
There is no significant ikhtilaf among the Hanafi school; the ruling is established in the zahir al-riwayah. The prohibition is clear from the texts.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that covering is haram for men and requires fidyah if done intentionally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۱) چہرہ اور سر کے چھپانے سے بچے۔
صلى الله وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے ۔ عن ابن عباس أن رجلا أو قصته راحلته و هو محرم فمات فقال رسول الله اغسلوه بماء وسدر وكفنوه في ثوبيه و لا تخمروا رأسه و لا وجهه فانه يبعث يوم القيامة ملبيا ۔ (مسلم شريف ، باب ما يفعل بالمحرم اذامات ،ص ۵۰۲ نمبر ۲۸۹۶/۱۲۰٦ رابن ماجہ شریف ، باب الحرم یموت ،ص ۴۴۹، نمبر۳۰۸۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ محرم کا سر اور چہرہ مت ڈھانکو۔ (۲) عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رجلا قال يا رسول الله مايلبس المحرم من الثياب؟ قال رسول الله الله لا يلبس القميص ولا العمائم ولا السراويلات ولا البرانس . (بخارى شریف، باب ما لا يلبس المحرم من الثياب ، ص۲۵۰، نمبر ۱۵۴۲ر مسلم شریف ، باب ما يباح للمحرم حج او عمرة البسه ومالا يباح ، ص ۴۸۵، نمبر ۲۷۹۱/۱۱۷۷/ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب ما یلبس المحرم نمبر ۱۸۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پگڑی نہ پہنے اور ٹوپی نہ پہنے۔ کیونکہ ان سے سر ڈھنگ جاتا ہے۔
Translation: (1301) Avoid covering the face and head.
Evidence: (1) The hadith is from Ibn ‘Abbas that a man fell from his camel while in ihram and died. So the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Wash him with water and sidr, shroud him in his two garments, and do not cover his head or his face, for he will be raised on the Day of Judgment saying the talbiyah. (Muslim, Bab Ma Yuf‘al bi al-Muhrim Idha Mata, p.502 no.2896/1206; Ibn Majah, Bab al-Muhrim Yamut, p.449 no.3084) In this hadith it is stated: Do not cover the head or face of the muhrim. (2) From ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Umar that a man said, O Messenger of Allah, what clothes may the muhrim wear? The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: He should not wear the shirt, nor the turban, nor the trousers, nor the hooded cloak. (Bukhari, Bab Ma La Yalbas al-Muhrim min al-Thiyab, p.250 no.1542; Muslim, Bab Ma Yabah li al-Muhrim Hajj aw ‘Umra Labsuhu wa Ma La Yabah, p.485 no.2791/1177; Abu Dawud, Bab Ma Yalbas al-Muhrim, no.1823) In this hadith it is stated: Do not wear the turban and do not wear the cap, because they cover the head.
Source pages p. 347

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling (hukm) that a muhrim must avoid covering the head (ra’s) and face (wajh). The author presents two proofs. The first proof is the hadith of Ibn ‘Abbas regarding a muhrim who died: the Prophet (peace be upon him) instructed not to cover his head or face, indicating that during life in ihram, covering them is also prohibited. The second proof is the same hadith of Ibn ‘Umar mentioned earlier, which prohibits the turban (‘imamah) and other head coverings, implying the prohibition of covering the head. The commentary explains that turbans and caps cover the head, hence they are prohibited. The face is also explicitly mentioned in the first hadith. Note that for women, the face covering (niqab) is prohibited but they may cover the head (hijab).

Key Terms
تخمروا (tukhmiru): Do not cover – specifically referring to covering the head or face entirely.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet instruct regarding the head and face of a muhrim who died?
A) Cover them out of respect.
B) Leave them uncovered.
C) Cover only the head.
D) Cover only the face.

Key Takeaway
Covering the head or face is haram for a male muhrim, as proven by explicit prophetic command not to cover even a deceased muhrim's head or face.

Prohibition of Applying Perfume in Ihram
Ruling and proof for prohibition of perfume for muhrim

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on applying perfume in ihram and cite the primary hadith proofs.

Core Idea
A muhrim must abstain from all perfume, on body and clothes, as commanded by the Prophet.

This lesson examines the prohibition of perfume (tib) during ihram. The Hanafi school bases this on clear prophetic directives, including the command to wash off perfume before entering ihram and the prohibition of wearing scented garments. Understanding these proofs reinforces the sacred nature of ihram as a state of simplicity and devotion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is applying perfume while in ihram. The ruling is haram.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The key hadith from Ibn Umar: 'Wash off the perfume that is on you three times and remove the cloak.'
Found in Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Analyse the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'wash off' indicates prohibition because it commands removal, implying the presence of perfume is impermissible.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub.
4
Note the scope of prohibition
Both body and clothing are covered; the hadith about saffron and wars extends to garments.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The Hanafi position is that perfume is absolutely prohibited; remnants from before ihram must be washed off.
Any intentional application requires fidyah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۲) خوشبولگانے سے۔
تشريح : احرام کی حالت میں خوشبو نہ لگائے۔
صل الله وجه : (۱) حدیث یہ ہے . عن ابن عمر قال قام رجل الى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فقال يا رسول الله ! ما يوجب الحج ؟ قال الزاد والراحلة قال يا رسول الله ! فما الحج ؟ قال الشعث و التفل . (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب فضل دعاء الحاج، ص ۴۱۹، نمبر ۲۸۹۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حاجی کو پراگندہ ہونا چاہئے (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر .... فقال اين الذي سأل عن العمرة ؟ فاتي برجل فقال اغسل الطيب الذي بک ثلاث مرات و انزع عنک الجبة و اصنع في عمرتك ما تصنع في حجتک ( بخاری شریف، باب غسل الخلوف ثلث مرات من الثياب ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۱۵۳۶ر مسلم شریف ، باب ما یباح للمحرم و بیان تحریم الطبیب علیه، ص ۲۸۶، نمبر ۱۱۸۰/ ۲۷۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم کے لئے خوشبو لگانا جائز نہیں ہے ۔ (۳) عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رجلا قال يا رسول الله ما يلبس المحرم من الثياب؟ قال رسول الله الله الله .... ولا تلبسوا من الثياب شيئا مسه زعفران او ورس. (بخاری شریف، باب مالا يلبس المحرم من الثياب، ص ۲۰۹ نمبر ۱۵۴۲ر مسلم شریف ، باب ما یباح للحرم حج اوعمرة لبسه ومالا يباح ص ۳۷۲ /۳۷۳ نمبر ۲۷۹۱/۱۱۷۷ /ابو داؤد شریف ، باب ما یلبس المحرم نمبر ۱۸۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایسے کپڑے کو نہ پہنو جس میں زعفران اور ورس کی خوشبو ہو۔
Translation: (1302) Avoid applying perfume.
Explanation: Do not apply perfume in the state of ihram.
Evidence: (1) The hadith is from Ibn ‘Umar: A man stood up to the Prophet (peace be upon him) and asked, O Messenger of Allah! What makes hajj obligatory? He said: Provision and mount. He said: O Messenger of Allah! What is hajj? He said: Disheveled hair and unwashed appearance. (Ibn Majah, Bab Fadl Du‘a al-Hajj, p.419 no.2896) In this hadith it is stated that the pilgrim should be unkempt. (2) Also in this hadith from ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Umar: He said, Where is the one who asked about ‘umrah? So a man was brought. He said: Wash off the perfume that is on you three times, remove the cloak, and do in your ‘umrah what you do in your hajj. (Bukhari, Bab Ghasl al-Khuluf Thalath Marrat min al-Thiyab, p.249 no.1536; Muslim, Bab Ma Yabah li al-Muhrim wa Bayan Tahrim al-Tib ‘alayh, p.286 no.1180/2798) From this hadith it is understood that applying perfume is not permissible for the muhrim. (3) From ‘Abdullah ibn ‘Umar that a man said, O Messenger of Allah, what clothes may the muhrim wear? The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: ...and do not wear any garment that has been touched by saffron or wars. (Bukhari, Bab Ma La Yalbas al-Muhrim min al-Thiyab, p.209 no.1542; Muslim, Bab Ma Yabah li al-Muhrim Hajj aw ‘Umra Labsuhu wa Ma La Yabah, p.372/373 no.2791/1177; Abu Dawud, Bab Ma Yalbas al-Muhrim, no.1823) In this hadith it is stated: Do not wear clothes that have saffron or wars perfume.
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage prohibits applying perfume (tib) in the state of ihram. The author provides three proofs. The first hadith from Ibn Majah describes that hajj involves being disheveled (sha‘th) and not using perfume (tafl). The second hadith directly commands a man to wash off the perfume he had applied and remove the cloak, indicating that perfume is prohibited. The third hadith from the commonly cited clothing prohibition specifically forbids wearing clothes touched by saffron (za‘faran) or wars (a type of fragrant plant), showing that even indirect perfume on clothing is not allowed. The ruling is clear: muhrim must avoid any scented substances.

Key Terms
طيب (tib): Perfume or any fragrant substance applied to the body or clothing.
شعث و تفل (sha‘th wa tafil): Disheveled hair and an unkempt, unperfumed state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did the Prophet command a man to do regarding the perfume on his body when beginning ‘umrah?
A) Leave it as it is.
B) Add more perfume.
C) Wash it off three times.
D) Cover it with a cloth.

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's command to wash off perfume and avoid scented clothes establishes that a muhrim must remain free of any fragrance.

Prohibition of Shaving the Head and Cutting Hair in Ihram
Ruling and proof for prohibition of shaving head or cutting hair in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shaving the head or cutting hair during ihram, identify the Quranic evidence, and explain the consequence (dam or fidyah) based on the circumstance.

Core Idea
Shaving the head during ihram is prohibited by the Quran; violation requires a dam unless due to illness then fidyah.

This lesson addresses one of the key prohibitions of ihram: removing hair from the head. The Quran explicitly forbids it and prescribes a compensation. We will examine the verse, its implications, and the Hanafi ruling that a deliberate violation necessitates a sacrificial animal (dam), while an illness-related shaving requires a fidyah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited act and its ruling
The passage clearly states that shaving the head (halq) and cutting hair (qat‘ al-sha‘r) are not permissible during ihram. In Hanafi fiqh, this is a prohibition (tahrim), making the act haram.
The prohibition applies to both deliberate and accidental acts, but the consequence differs (dam vs. no compensation).
2
Locate the dalil and analyse its indication
The evidence is Quran 2:196: 'And do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place...'. The imperative negative 'لا تحلقوا' indicates a binding prohibition. The exception for illness confirms the general rule.
In Hanafi usul, the apparent meaning of the verse is clear (zahir) and the prohibition is established (haram).
3
Determine the consequence (dam or fidyah)
If a muhrim shaves or cuts hair without a valid excuse, the Hanafi position is that a dam (one sheep or goat) is wajib. If done due to illness or ailment, the verse allows a fidyah: fasting three days, feeding six poor persons, or offering a sacrifice.
The specific number of hairs that trigger dam is discussed; the relied view is that cutting three or more hairs requires dam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۳) سرکے حلق سے اور بال کے کاٹنے سے بچے۔
تشريح : احرام کی حالت میں سرمونڈوانا، یا بال کٹوانا جائز نہیں ہے،اگر ایسا کیا تو دم لازم ہوگا۔
وجه : (۱) آیت یہ ہے۔ ولا تحلقوا رؤوسكم حتى يبلغ الهدى محله فمن كان منكم مريضا او به اذى من
Translation: (1303) Avoid shaving the head and cutting the hair.
Explanation: It is not permissible to shave the head or cut the hair during ihram. If one does so, a dam (sacrificial animal) will be obligatory.
Evidence: (1) The verse is: "And do not shave your heads until the sacrificial animal reaches its place. But if any of you is ill or has an ailment in his scalp..." (Al-Baqarah 2:196)
Source pages p. 348

Commentary
This passage prohibits shaving the head (halq) and cutting hair (qat‘ al-sha‘r) during ihram. The explanation adds that if a muhrim commits this violation, he must offer a dam (one sheep or goat) as expiation. The evidence cited is part of verse 2:196 from Surah Al-Baqarah, which prohibits shaving the head until the sacrifice reaches its place. The verse also provides a concession for those who are ill or have a scalp ailment, allowing them to shave with a fidyah (fasting, charity, or sacrifice). The passage is incomplete but conveys the essential prohibition and consequence.

Key Terms
حلق (halq): Shaving the head completely.
دم (dam): A sacrificial animal (one sheep or goat) required as expiation for violating an ihram prohibition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if a muhrim deliberately shaves his head without a valid excuse?
A) Nothing, it is allowed.
B) He must offer a dam (sacrificial animal).
C) He must fast for three days.
D) He must give charity.

Key Takeaway
The Quranic prohibition against shaving the head in ihram is unequivocal; deliberate violation necessitates a sacrificial animal (dam), while illness permits a fidyah.

Permissible Acts for a Muhrim: Ghusl, Shade, and Waistband
Ruling on permissible acts for muhrim with detailed proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bathing, seeking shade, and tying a hamian for a muhrim, and cite the textual evidence from Quran and hadith that support these rulings.

Core Idea
A muhrim may bathe, seek shade, and carry money in a waist pouch, as these do not violate the prohibitions of ihram.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah clarifies three actions that are permissible for a person in the state of ihram: bathing (ghusl), seeking shade under a tent or howdah, and tying a hamian (a money belt). Although the state of ihram has restrictions, these acts are lawful because they do not involve covering the head, cutting hair, or using perfume. The author provides proofs from the Quran, authentic hadith, and practices of the Companions to support these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three acts and their ruling
From the matn, identify that ghusl, istizlal (seeking shade), and tying the hamian are all ruled mubah (permissible) for the muhrim. Note that no compensation is required for these acts unless they lead to a prohibited action.
2
Locate the dalil for each act
For ghusl: Quranic verse 2:222 on purification, hadith of Abu Ayyub washing his head, and practice of 'Umar and Ibn 'Abbas. For shade: hadith of Umm al-Husayn about the Prophet being shaded. For hamian: statement of the Tabi'i and the general principle of permissibility.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah for each proof
For each evidence, explain how it directly supports permissibility. E.g., the verse shows love for those who purify themselves—ghusl is a form of purification. The hadith shows the Prophet (peace be upon him) seeking shade, proving it is allowed. The athar on hamian shows that a muhrim can carry money in a sewn pouch.
4
Note the ikhtilaf on shading
The passage indicates that some schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may have stricter views on seeking shade under permanent structures. The Hanafi response is that the act does not involve covering the head with a sewn garment, and the prophetic practice confirms its permissibility.
This ikhtilaf is legitimate and does not affect the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
5
Evaluate the authority level
The ruling from the later Hanafi authorities (fatawa mutakhkhirin) is that these acts are permissible. The zahir al-riwayah position from the earlier corpus also supports this. The mufta bihi is the permissibility of all three acts.

Source Text

غسل المحرم بدنه وراس ص ۱۳۸۳ نمبر ۱۲۰۵ ۲۸۸۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم غسل کر سکتا ہے۔ (۳) اس قول صحابی میں ہے . عن ابن عباس قال قال لي عمر : تعال معى حتى أنافس في الماء أين اصبر و نحن محرمون۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ، باب في الحرم يغتسل أو يغسل رأسه ، ج ثالث ، ص ۱۳۸ نمبر ۱۲۸۴۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ حضرت عمر اور حضرت ابن عباس نے غسل فرمایا۔ (۴) گھر یا کجاوہ سے سایہ حاصل کر سکتا ہے اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ام الـحـصـيـن حـدثـتـه قـالـت حججنا مع النبي الله حجة الوداع فرأيت اسامة وبلالا واحدهما اخذ بخطام ناقة النبى الله والآخر رافع ثوبه يستره من الحر حتى رمى جمرة العقبة ۔ (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الحرم يظلل ص ۲۶۲/۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۸۳۴ مسلم شریف، باب استحباب رمی جمرة العقبة يوم النحر ص ۵۴۶، نمبر ۳۱۳۸/۱۲۹۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم سایہ حاصل کر سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ حضور نے کپڑے سے سایہ حاصل کیا۔ (۵) ہمیانی باندھ سکتا ہے اس کے لئے یہ قول تابعی ہے ۔ سالت ابا جعفر وعطاء عن الهميان للمحرم فقال لا۔ (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ۴۳۴ فی الهميان للحرم، ج ثالث ص ۱۳۹۳ نمبر ۱۵۴۴۴ر بخاری شریف، باب الطيب عند الاحرام ص ۲۴۹ نمبر ۱۵۳۷) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ محرم ہمیانی باندھ سکتا ہے۔ لغت : استظلال بظل سے مشتق ہے، سایہ حاصل کرنا۔ مکمل : کجاوہ شد: باندھنا۔ الھمیان: لمبی سی سلی ہوئی تھیلی جس میں درہم وغیرہ رقم رکھتے ہیں۔ وسط : درمیان ، مراد ہے کمر ۔
Chapter: Composition of Hajj Actions. (1304) It is permissible to bathe, seek shade under a tent, a howdah, and others, and to tie the hamian in the waist. Then fidyah from fasting or charity or sacrifice. (Verse 196 of Surah al-Baqarah) From this verse it is understood that a muhrim should not cut the hair of the head or body. (2) In this hadith: From Abdullah bin Ma'qil who said: I sat with Ka'b bin 'Ujra and asked him about fidyah. He said: It was revealed specifically for me and is general for you. I was carried to the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) with lice falling on my face. He said: I did not think that the harm had reached you as I see, or I did not think the difficulty had reached you as I see. Do you have a sheep? I said no. He said: Then fast three days or feed six poor people, each with half a sa'. And in another narration: Or sacrifice a sheep. (Bukhari, Muslim) This hadith indicates that one should not shave, otherwise one must offer a blood sacrifice.

Translation: (1304) Bathing, seeking shade under a tent, a howdah, and others, and tying the hamian around the waist are permissible. Explanation: Bathing is permissible during ihram; it is not against dishevelment. Seeking shade under a howdah or tent is permissible because it does not involve placing cloth on the head. Tying the hamian around the waist is also permissible. Proofs: (1) Bathing is permissible, and the indication for this is the verse: Indeed Allah loves those who repent and loves those who purify themselves. (al-Baqarah 2:222) Allah loves purity greatly, so it is also beloved and permissible for the muhrim. (2) From Abdullah bin Abbas and al-Miswar bin Makhrama who differed at al-Abwa. Ibn Abbas said: The muhrim may wash his head... He poured water on his head, then Abu Ayyub moved his head with his hands, moving it forwards and backwards, then said: This is how I saw him do. (Abu Dawud, Muslim) This hadith shows that the muhrim can bathe. (3) In the saying of a Companion: From Ibn Abbas who said: 'Umar said to me: Come with me to compete in the water, I will wring [my hair] while we are in ihram. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) This effect shows that 'Umar and Ibn Abbas performed ghusl. (4) One can seek shade from a house or howdah, and the proof is the hadith of Umm al-Husayn: We performed Hajj with the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the Farewell Pilgrimage. I saw Usamah and Bilal, one holding the nose-string of the Prophet's she-camel, and the other raising his garment to shade him from the heat until he stoned the Jamrat al-Aqabah. (Abu Dawud, Muslim) From this hadith it is known that a muhrim can seek shade because the Prophet (peace be upon him) sought shade from a cloth. (5) He can tie a hamian, and for this there is the saying of a Tabi'i: I asked Abu Ja'far and 'Ata' about the hamian for a muhrim, and they said no. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Bukhari) From this effect it is known that a muhrim can tie a hamian. Lexicon: استظلال is derived from ظل, meaning to seek shade. المكمل: howdah. الشد: to tie. الهميان: a long sewn pouch in which dirhams and other money are kept. الوسط: the middle, meaning the waist.
Source pages p. 349

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Thamaratun Najah regarding permissible acts during ihram. The author first states the ruling: it is permissible to bathe, seek shade under a tent or howdah, and tie a hamian (a money belt) around the waist. He then quotes the Quranic verse (2:196) about fidyah for shaving the head, using it to derive the prohibition of cutting hair. He then provides multiple proofs: (1) the Quranic verse on purification for ghusl; (2) a hadith where Abu Ayyub is seen washing his head; (3) the practice of 'Umar and Ibn 'Abbas; (4) the hadith of Umm al-Husayn about shade; and (5) the statement of a Tabi'i about the hamian. The commentary explains that these acts are permissible because they do not conflict with the state of ihram. The fidyah verse is used to show that cutting hair requires compensation. Lexicon clarifies terms.

Key Terms
الهميان (al-hamyān): A long sewn pouch used to carry money, tied around the waist.
الاستظلال (al-istizlāl): Seeking shade under a structure like a tent or howdah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following acts is permissible for a muhrim?
A) Cutting the hair of the head
B) Seeking shade under a howdah
C) Covering the head with a cloth
D) Wearing perfume

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may bathe, seek shade, and tie a money belt, as these are permissible practices supported by the Quran, Sunnah, and Companions’ actions.

Reciting Talbiyah Loudly and Frequently: Sunnah and Its Occasions
Ruling on times and manner of talbiyah recitation with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah occasions for reciting talbiyah and identify the Hanafi proof that it is sunnah, not wajib.

Core Idea
The Prophet defined 'ajj (raising the voice with talbiyah) as the best Hajj — making it a sunnah, not an obligation.

Reciting the talbiyah (Labbayk Allahumma labbayk) is a cherished act during Hajj and Umrah. But when and how should it be recited? This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling that it is sunnah to increase talbiyah after prayers, on high ground, in valleys, at dawn, and when meeting riders — and why it remains sunnah, not wajib, despite strong proofs. We will trace the evidence from the Prophet's practice and the hadith defining 'ajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What act is being discussed? It is the recitation of talbiyah (التلبية). The ruling is sunnah — recommended, not obligatory. Locate this in the text: the word 'سنت' appears in the explanation.
Sunnah here means a confirmed practice of the Prophet, but not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary hadith cited: from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq that the Prophet said 'العج و الثج' (raising the voice and sacrificing). The text explains 'العج' as raising the voice with talbiyah. Note the source: Tirmidhi.
Hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut), which supports the sunnah classification.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet explicitly called 'ajj the best Hajj, indicating its high virtue. Since it is described as 'best' rather than obligatory, it becomes sunnah. The text also cites Jibril's command to raise voices, but command (amr) in Hanafi usul can indicate recommended status when context shows it is not obligatory.
Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub unless qarinah indicates nadb.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Are there differing views? The text notes that some schools may consider raising the voice as mandatory. Hanafi holds it as sunnah. Be aware that the cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi based on fatawa mutakhkhirin.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi position relies on the hadith being ahad and the absence of a clear obligation. The text also mentions the Prophet's practice of reciting after prayer, on heights, etc., which reinforces sunnah rather than wajib.
The preferred view is that talbiyah loudly is sunnah, practiced by the Prophet and Companions.

(۱۳۰۵) واكثر التلبية متى صليت او علوتَ شرفا او هبطت واديا او لقيت ركبا وبالاسحار بأس به.
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۵) - نماز کے بعد بلندی پر چڑھتے ہوئے ، پستی کی طرف اترتے ہوئے ، مسافر سے ملاقات پر صبح کے وقت، تلبیہ کو اتنے بلند آواز سے پڑھ کہ کوئی مشقت ونقصان نہ ہو
تشریح : احرام باندھنے کے بعد کثرت سے تلبیہ پڑھنا سنت ہے، پھر زور زور آواز سے پڑھے، پہاڑی پر چڑھتے ،اتر تے ، سواری سے ملتے تلبیہ پڑھے، اور اتنا پڑھے کی کسی دوسرے کو بھی نقصان نہ ہو اور اپنے کو بھی نقصان نہ ہو۔

( ترمذی شریف، باب ما جاء فضل التلبية والخر ص ۲۰۶، نمبر ۸۲۷ ) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ افضل حج ، حج ، ہے جس کا ترجمہ راوی نے کیا، کہ تلبیہ کو بلند آواز سے پڑھنا۔ اور، مج ، ہے جسکا ترجمہ راوی نے کیا ، ھدی کے جانور کو زیادہ سے زیادہ ذبح کرنا. (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عـن خـلاد بن السائب عن ابيه قال قال رسول الله الله : أتاني جبريل فأمرني أن أمر أصحابي أن يرفعوا أصواتهم بالاهلال أو التلبية . ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فى رفع الصوت بالتلبية ، ص ۲۰۷، نمبر ۸۲۹/ ابو داود شریف ، باب کیف التلبية ،ص ۲۶۷، نمبر ۱۸۱۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضرت جبریل علیہ السلام نے فرمایا کہ اللہ کا حکم یہ ہے کہ بلند آواز سے تلبیہ پڑھے۔ (۳) نماز کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھنے کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ قلت لعبد الله ابن عباس .... خرج رسول الله الله حاجا فلما صلى في مسجده بذي الحليفة ركعتيه أوجب في مجلسه فأهل بالحج حين فرغ من ركعتيه (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی وقت الاحرام ص ۲۵۳ نمبر ۱۷۷۰/ ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جامعتی احرم النبی یا ا ن ص ۱۶۹ نمبر ۸/۱۹/ بخاری شریف، باب الاحلال مستقبل القبلة ، ص ۲۵۲، نمبر ۱۵۵۴) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ نماز کے بعد حضور نے تلبیہ پڑھا۔ (۴) سواری سے ملتے وقت تلبیہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله الا الله كان اذا استوت به راحلته قائمة عند مسجد ذو الحليفة اهل فقال لبیک اللهم لبیک، الخ. (مسلم شریف، باب التلبية وصفتها ووقتها ص ۳۷۵ نمبر ۲۸۱۲/۱۱۸۴ / بخاری شریف، باب الاهلال مستقبل القبلة ،ص ۲۵۱ نمبر ۱۵۵۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے سواری پر سوار ہونے کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھا۔ (۵) بار بار پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے
(1305) And increase talbiyah: when you pray, or ascend a height, or descend a valley, or meet a rider, and at dawn, without causing harm. 
Translation: (1305) - After prayer, while ascending a height, descending a valley, when meeting a rider, at dawn, recite talbiyah so loudly that there is no hardship or harm. 
Explanation: After donning ihram, it is sunnah to recite talbiyah frequently, then loudly; on climbing a mountain, descending, meeting a rider, recite talbiyah; recite so that no harm comes to others or oneself. 
Proofs: (1) The hadith about reciting talbiyah loudly and after prayer: From Abu Bakr al-Siddiq that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) was asked which Hajj is best? He said: 'ajj and thajj... and 'ajj is raising the voice with talbiyah, and thajj is sacrificing the animals. (Tirmidhi) This hadith means that the best Hajj is the one where talbiyah is recited loudly and many sacrifices are made. (2) Another hadith: From Khallad bin al-Sa'ib from his father that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: Jibril came to me and ordered me to command my companions to raise their voices with ihilal or talbiyah. (Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud) This hadith indicates that Jibril commanded raising voices with talbiyah. (3) Hadith about talbiyah after prayer: I said to Abdullah bin Abbas... The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) went for Hajj, and when he prayed two rak'ahs in his mosque at Dhu al-Hulayfah, he made the intention in his sitting place, and began talbiyah for Hajj when he finished the two rak'ahs. (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Bukhari) This hadith shows that the Prophet recited talbiyah after prayer. (4) Hadith about talbiyah when meeting a rider: From Abdullah bin Umar that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) would, when his riding camel stood up at the mosque of Dhu al-Hulayfah, begin talbiyah saying 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' (Muslim, Bukhari) This hadith shows that the Prophet recited talbiyah after mounting his camel. (5) For reciting frequently, the hadith is... (incomplete)
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage discusses the sunnah of reciting talbiyah (labbayk) loudly and at specific times. The ruling is that increasing talbiyah after prayers, on heights, in valleys, when meeting riders, and at dawn is sunnah. The commentary explains that it is sunnah to recite frequently and loudly without causing harm. Proofs include: (1) the hadith that the best Hajj is 'ajj and thajj, where 'ajj is raising the voice with talbiyah; (2) Jibril commanding to raise voices; (3) the Prophet reciting talbiyah after praying; (4) the Prophet reciting after mounting his camel; and (5) an incomplete proof about reciting frequently.

Key Terms
التلبية (al-talbiyah): The invocation 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited by a pilgrim.
العج (al-'ajj): Raising the voice with talbiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Reciting talbiyah loudly and frequently at specific occasions (after prayer, on heights, in valleys, when meeting others, and at dawn) is sunnah in the Hanafi school, confirmed by the Prophet's statement that the best Hajj includes 'ajj (raising the voice).

Recommended Manners of Reciting Talbiyah
Rulings on the recommended times and manner of talbiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended times and manner of reciting talbiyah according to the Hanafi school and identify the prophetic proofs for each.

Core Idea
Recite talbiyah frequently, raise your voice, but avoid causing harm.

This passage details the multiple occasions when a pilgrim should recite talbiyah—after prayer, on heights, in valleys, meeting riders, and at dawn. It also emphasizes raising the voice without harm. These are all based on specific hadiths, strengthening their recommendation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
First, understand that talbiyah in the Hanafi school is sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah), not fard or wajib. Note the overall hukm from the text: 'reciting talbiyah frequently is sunnah.'
2
List the recommended occasions
From the text, enumerate the six occasions: after prayer, ascending a height, descending a valley, meeting a rider, at dawn, and in general frequently. Write these down.
The text uses 'mata salayta' (whenever you pray), 'alawta sharafan' (ascend a height), etc.
3
Analyze each prophetic proof
For each occasion, find the hadith cited. For example, raising the voice is proven by the hadith of Jibril commanding the Prophet to order raising voices. Connect each occasion to its proof.
There are six hadiths; match them to the occasions.
4
Note the condition of avoiding harm
The text explicitly adds 'without causing harm to oneself or others.' This qualifies the recommendation—a loud voice should not disturb others.
This condition is important for proper adab.
5
Summarize the Hanafi position
Combine all the above: talbiyah is a sunnah act, to be recited at specific times, with a raised voice but without harm. This is the mufta bihi view.
The Hanafi school follows the practice of the Prophet and his companions.

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
الوسط (۱۳۰۵) واكثر التلبية متى صليت او علوتَ شرفا او هبطت واديا او لقيت ركبا وبالاسحار بأس به.
تشریح : احرام باندھنے کے بعد کثرت سے تلبیہ پڑھنا سنت ہے، پھر زور زور آواز سے پڑھے، پہاڑی پر چڑھتے ،اتر تے ، سواری سے ملتے تلبیہ پڑھے، اور اتنا پڑھے کی کسی دوسرے کو بھی نقصان نہ ہو اور اپنے کو بھی نقصان نہ ہو۔

(۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ عن خـلاد بن السائب عن ابيه قال قال رسول الله : أتاني جبريل فأمرني أن أمر أصحابي أن يرفعوا أصواتهم بالاهلال أو التلبية . (۵) بار بار پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس ان اسامة كان ردف رسول الله من عرفة الى المزدلفة ثم ردف الفضل من المزدلفة الى منى قال فكلاهما قال لم يزل النبى الله يلبي حتى رمي الجمرة العقبة۔ (۶) وادی میں اتر تے چڑھتے تلبیہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فقال ابن عباس لم اسمعه و لكنه قال اما موسی کانی انظر اليه اذا انحدر في الوادي یلبی

(۱۳۰۶ ) واذا وصلت الى مكة يستحب ان تغتسل
وجه : (ا) كان ابن عمر اذا دخل ادنى الحرم امسك عن التلبية ثم يبيت بذى طوى ثم يصلى به الصبح ويغتسل ويحدث ان النبى كان يفعل ذالک ۔ (۲) عن ابن عمر قال اغتسل النبي لدخول مكة بفخ

(۱۳۰۷ ) وتدخلها مـن بـاب الـمـعـلـى لتكون مستقبلا في دخولک باب البيت الشريف تعظيما
تشریح : باب معلی سے داخل ہوگا تو بیت اللہ کا استقبال ہوگا، اور اس کی تعظیم بھی ہوگی ، اس لئے باب معلی سے مکہ مکرمہ داخل ہو حضور اسی دروازے سے داخل ہوئے تھے۔
وجه : (۱) عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله لا يدخل مكة من الثنية العليا و يخرج من الثنية السفلى ۔

(۱۳۰۸ ) ويستحب ان ... رافعا صوتک بلا جهد مضر
ترجمه : (۱۳۰۸) اور داخل ہوتے وقت برابر تلبیہ پڑھنا بھی مستحب ہے، یہاں تک کہ باب سلام پر آجائے، تشریح : مکہ مکرمہ میں داخل ہوتے وقت تلبیہ پڑھتے رہنا مستحب ہے جب تک کہ باب سلام کے پاس نہ آجائے ، باب سلام سے آگے بڑھے گا تو بیت اللہ نظر آئے گا وجه (۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ بدھ کے دن تک حج کا تلبیہ پڑھتے رہے ، حضور حجتہ الوداع میں بدھ کے دن بیت اللہ داخل
Chapter on the Composition of Hajj Actions. (1305) Increase talbiyah: whenever you pray, ascend a height, descend a valley, meet a rider, and at dawn - there is no harm in it. Explanation: After donning ihram, reciting talbiyah frequently is sunnah; then recite it loudly while climbing a mountain, descending, meeting a rider, and recite it such that no one else is harmed nor oneself harmed. Proof: (1) Hadith from Abu Bakr al-Siddiq: the Prophet was asked which Hajj is best? He said: 'al-Ajj wa al-Thaj' - raising voice in talbiyah and sacrificing animals. (2) Hadith from Khalid ibn al-Sa'ib: Jibril came to me and ordered me to command my companions to raise their voices with talbiyah. (3) Hadith about talbiyah after prayer: Ibn Abbas said the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs in Dhul-Hulayfah then began talbiyah. (4) Hadith from Ibn Umar: when the Prophet's mount stood, he said 'Labbayk...' (5) Hadith from Ibn Abbas: Usama rode behind the Prophet from Arafat to Muzdalifah, then Fadl rode behind him to Mina; both said the Prophet continued talbiyah until stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah. (6) Hadith: when descending into a valley he would recite talbiyah. (1306) When you reach Mecca, it is recommended to perform ghusl. Proof: Ibn Umar would do so, and the Prophet did so. (1307) Enter Mecca from Bab al-Mu'alla so that upon entry you face the door of the Sacred House as an act of veneration. Explanation: Entering from Bab al-Mu'alla allows facing the Kaaba; the Prophet entered from that door. Proof: Ibn Umar said the Prophet entered from the upper pass and exited from the lower. (1308) It is recommended to continue reciting talbiyah while entering until you reach Bab al-Salam. Explanation: It is recommended to recite talbiyah until you reach Bab al-Salam; beyond that you will see the Kaaba. Proof: Hadith that he recited talbiyah until Wednesday, and he entered Mecca on Wednesday during his farewell pilgrimage.
Source pages p. 350

Commentary
This passage presents a series of recommended actions (mustahabbat) related to talbiyah and entering Mecca for the Hajj pilgrimage. The author begins by stating the general principle: talbiyah should be recited frequently after entering ihram, especially after prayers, upon ascending or descending terrain, meeting fellow travelers, and at dawn. The voice should be raised without causing harm to oneself or others. Multiple hadith are cited to support each occasion. Next, the text rules that performing ghusl (ritual bath) before entering Mecca is recommended (mustahabb), based on the practice of Ibn Umar and the Prophet. Then, it is recommended to enter Mecca from Bab al-Mu'alla so that one faces the Kaaba upon entry, as an act of veneration; the Prophet entered from that gate. Finally, talbiyah should be continued until one reaches Bab al-Salam, after which the Kaaba becomes visible. All these are mustahabb (recommended) actions, not obligatory. The Hanafi school consistently holds that talbiyah is a sunnah of Hajj, and these specific timings and manners enhance the spiritual experience.

Key Terms
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The phrase 'Labbayk, Allahumma labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim upon assuming ihram.
مستحب (mustahabb): An action that is recommended but not obligatory; omission is not sinful but performing it brings reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, reciting talbiyah frequently is:
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah muakkadah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
Reciting talbiyah frequently and with a raised voice is a sunnah act of Hajj, practiced by the Prophet on various occasions.

Recommended Actions Upon Entering Mecca
Rulings on recommended actions when entering Mecca

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three recommended actions when entering Mecca according to the Hanafi school and the prophetic proofs for each.

Core Idea
Ghusl, entering from Bab al-Mu'alla, and continuing talbiyah until Bab al-Salam are recommended sunnahs.

This passage covers three recommended acts for a pilgrim entering Mecca: performing ghusl, entering from Bab al-Mu'alla to face the Kaaba, and continuing talbiyah until reaching Bab al-Salam. Each is supported by the practice of the Prophet and his companions, making them sunnah acts that enhance the sacredness of entry.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three recommendations
From the text, list the three distinct recommendations: (1) performing ghusl before entering, (2) entering from Bab al-Mu'alla, and (3) continuing talbiyah until Bab al-Salam.
These are separate sunan, each with its own proof.
2
Analyze the proof for ghusl
The text cites two proofs: the practice of Ibn Umar and that the Prophet performed ghusl for entering Mecca. Understand that this makes ghusl mustahabb.
The hadith: 'اغتسل النبي لدخول مكة بفخ'
3
Analyze the proof for entering from Bab al-Mu'alla
The text cites Ibn Umar saying the Prophet entered from the upper pass (الثنية العليا) which is Bab al-Mu'alla. This is to face the Kaaba upon entry.
Bab al-Mu'alla is also known as Bab al-Hazwarah.
4
Analyze the proof for continuing talbiyah
The text mentions that the Prophet continued talbiyah until Wednesday, the day he entered Mecca. This indicates talbiyah should not stop until reaching Bab al-Salam.
Bab al-Salam is the gate after which the Kaaba becomes visible.
5
Explain the wisdom
These actions are done to venerate the Sacred House and follow the Prophet's example. Facing the Kaaba upon entry shows respect, and continuing talbiyah prolongs the state of worship.

الوسط (۱۳۰۵) واكثر التلبية متى صليت او علوتَ شرفا او هبطت واديا او لقيت ركبا وبالاسحار بأس به.
تشریح : احرام باندھنے کے بعد کثرت سے تلبیہ پڑھنا سنت ہے، پھر زور زور آواز سے پڑھے، پہاڑی پر چڑھتے ،اتر تے ، سواری سے ملتے تلبیہ پڑھے، اور اتنا پڑھے کی کسی دوسرے کو بھی نقصان نہ ہو اور اپنے کو بھی نقصان نہ ہو۔
وجه : (۱) زور زور سے تلبیہ پڑھنے کی اور نماز کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھنے کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابي بكر الصديق أن رسول الله سئل أى الحج أفضل ؟ قال العج و الثج ... (۳) نماز کے بعد تلبیہ پڑھنے کی حدیث یہ ہے۔ قلت لعبد الله ابن عباس .... خرج رسول الله حاجا فلما صلى في مسجده بذي الحليفة ركعتيه أوجب في مجلسه فأهل بالحج حين فرغ من ركعتيه (۴) سواری سے ملتے وقت تلبیہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن عمر ان رسول الله كان اذا استوت به راحلته قائمة عند مسجد ذو الحليفة اهل فقال لبیک اللهم لبیک... (۵) بار بار پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے عن ابن عباس ان اسامة كان ردف رسول الله من عرفة الى المزدلفة ثم ردف الفضل من المزدلفة الى منى قال فكلاهما قال لم يزل النبى الله يلبي حتى رمي الجمرة العقبة۔ (۶) وادی میں اتر تے چڑھتے تلبیہ پڑھے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ فقال ابن عباس لم اسمعه و لكنه قال اما موسی کانی انظر اليه اذا انحدر في الوادي یلبی

(۱۳۰۶ ) واذا وصلت الى مكة يستحب ان تغتسل
وجه : (ا) كان ابن عمر اذا دخل ادنى الحرم امسك عن التلبية ثم يبيت بذى طوى ثم يصلى به الصبح ويغتسل ويحدث ان النبى كان يفعل ذالک ۔ (۲) عن ابن عمر قال اغتسل النبي لدخول مكة بفخ

Commentary
This passage presents a series of recommended actions (mustahabbat) related to talbiyah and entering Mecca for the Hajj pilgrimage. The author begins by stating the general principle: talbiyah should be recited frequently after entering ihram, especially after prayers, upon ascending or descending terrain, meeting fellow travelers, and at dawn. Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): The ritual washing of the entire body with the intention of purification.
باب معلی (Bab al-Mu'alla): One of the gates of Mecca, also known as Bab al-Hazwarah, from which the Prophet entered.
باب سلام (Bab al-Salam): A gate of the Sacred Mosque (Masjid al-Haram) near the Kaaba.

Recommended Acts When Entering Makkah and the Haram
Describes mustahabbat with proofs from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four mustahabbat when entering Makkah and identify the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Entering Makkah and the Haram follows a sunnah protocol of ghusl, specific gate entry, talbiyah, and humble approach.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah details the recommended acts (mustahabbat) that a pilgrim performs upon reaching Makkah. These acts are not obligatory but perfect the experience of entering the sacred precincts. Each is backed by the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as recorded in authentic hadith. By learning these sunan, the student can enhance their own or others' Hajj journey with adherence to Prophetic guidance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four mustahabbat
Scan the Arabic and translation to list the four recommended acts: ghusl, entering from Bab al-Mu'alla, continuous talbiyah until Bab al-Salam, and entering Masjid al-Haram with humility, takbir, tahlil, and salawat.
The text numbers them (1306-1309).
2
Extract the hadith evidence for each
For each act, note the primary hadith cited. Ghusl: hadith of Ibn Umar (Bukhari, Tirmidhi). Gate: hadith of Ibn Umar on entering from upper pass. Talbiya: hadith of Ibn Abbas on Prophet's talbiyah. Humility: multiple hadith on raising hands, supplication, and salawat upon seeing the House.
Use the Arabic text of the hadith where provided.
3
Understand the hikmah (wisdom)
The text explains why each act is done: ghusl for cleanliness, Bab al-Mu'alla to face the Kaaba, talbiyah until sighting the House, and humility to venerate Allah's House.
The hikmah reinforces the sunnah aspect.
4
Apply to a modern pilgrim's journey
Consider how a pilgrim today would implement these acts: perform ghusl at the hotel or before entering the Haram boundary, use GPS to locate Bab al-Mu'alla, recite talbiyah aloud or softly until approaching the Masjid, then enter with prescribed adhkar.
Ensure understanding that these are recommended, not obligatory.

Source Text
