Seven Circuits of Tawaf and the Hateem Boundary
Instructions for seven circuits and Hateem boundary in tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the number of tawaf circuits (seven) and the requirement to perform tawaf outside the Hateem, and cite the two hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Seven circuits are fard; tawaf must encompass the Hateem because it is part of the Kaaba.

This passage establishes two fundamental rulings of tawaf: the required number of circuits (seven) and the boundary that must be encompassed (outside the Hateem). These are not mere recommendations but obligatory elements rooted in the Prophet's practice and the physical structure of the Kaaba. The text provides clear hadith proofs from Ibn 'Umar and 'A'isha, which are the basis for the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
From the matn: tawaf is seven circuits and must be performed from outside the Hateem.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For seven circuits: hadith of Ibn ‘Umar. For Hateem boundary: hadith of ‘A’isha.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action in Ibn ‘Umar’s hadith directly shows seven circuits. In ‘A’isha’s hadith, the Prophet confirms the Hateem is part of the Kaaba, so tawaf must enclose it.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement among schools on these two points; it is muttafaq alayh.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The ruling is based on authentic ahadith and accepted by all; the Hanafi position follows the zahir al-riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمه : (۱۳۱۶) طواف سات چکر ہے، اس میں جو چاہے دعا کرئے ۔ اور حطیم کے باہر سے طواف کرے۔ تشريح طواف سات چکر کرے، اور چونکہ حطیم بیت اللہ کا حصہ ہے اس لئے اس کے باہر سے طواف کرے، اس کو چھوڑے نہیں وجه : (۱) سات شوط طواف کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال سعى النبي ام ثلثة اشواط ومشى اربعة في الحج والعمرة ـ ( بخاری شریف، باب الرمل في الحج والعمرة ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۳ رابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف میں سات مرتبہ بیت اللہ کے چاروں طرف چکر لگائے جس کو سات شوط کہتے ہیں۔ (۲) اور حطیم کے پیچھے سے طواف کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت سألت رسول الله عن الجدر ؟ أمن البيت هو ؟ قال : نعم قلت فلم لم يدخلوه البيت ؟ قال ان قومک قصرت بهم النفقة قلت فما شأن بابه مــرتـفـع ؟ قال فعل ذالک قومک لیدخلوا من شآؤا و يمنعوا من شآؤا و لولا أن قومك حديث عهدهم في الجاهلية فأخاف أن تنكر قلوبهم لنظرت أن ادخل الجدر في البيت ، و ان الزق بابه بالارض (مسلم شریف، باب جدر الکعبه و با بها، ص ۵۶۳، نمبر ۳۲۴۹/۱۳۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خرچ کی کمی کی وجہ سے قریش نے حطیم کو بیت اللہ میں داخل نہیں کیا اور نہ وہ بیت اللہ میں داخل ہے، اس لئے اس کے پیچھے سے طواف کرے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔
Translation: (1316) Tawaf is seven circuits; in it supplicate with whatever you wish. And perform tawaf from outside the Hateem. Elaboration: Perform seven circuits of tawaf, and since the Hateem is part of the House of Allah, perform tawaf from outside it; do not leave it out. Proof: (1) The evidence for performing seven circuits is this hadith: From Ibn ‘Umar: The Prophet (peace be upon him) did three circuits quickly and walked four in Hajj and ‘Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab al-Raml fi al-Hajj wa al-‘Umrah, p.218, no.1603; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Raml, p.266, no.1886) From this hadith it is known that in tawaf one circles around the House seven times, which is called seven circuits. (2) The evidence for tawaf behind the Hateem is this hadith: From ‘A’isha: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the wall (al-Jidr): Is it part of the House? He said: Yes. I said: Then why did they not include it in the House? He said: Your people’s funds fell short. I said: What is the matter with its door being raised? He said: Your people did that so that they could admit whomever they wished and prevent whomever they wished. Were it not that your people are new in Islam and I fear their hearts would change, I would consider including the wall in the House and making its door level with the ground. (Muslim, Bab Jidr al-Ka‘ba wa Babiha, p.563, no.3249/1333) In this hadith, due to shortage of funds, the Quraysh did not include the Hateem in the House, and it is not inside the House, so perform tawaf behind it.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, establishing two key aspects of tawaf: the number of circuits (seven) and the requirement to stay outside the Hateem (the semicircular wall). The matn states that tawaf consists of seven circuits, and one should make tawaf from outside the Hateem. The commentary explains that the Hateem is part of the Kaaba’s original foundation but was not included due to Quraysh’s financial constraints; thus tawaf must be performed outside it. The proof for seven circuits is the hadith of Ibn ‘Umar describing the Prophet’s ramal and walking. The proof for the Hateem is the hadith of ‘A’isha in which the Prophet confirms that the wall (al-Jidr) is from the House, but it was left out by Quraysh. Therefore, the Hanafi position is that tawaf must be performed around the Hateem from outside, as it is effectively part of the Kaaba. Seven circuits are obligatory (fard) in tawaf; the number is established by the Prophet’s practice and consensus.

Key Terms
حطیم (Hateem): The semicircular wall opposite the Kaaba’s corner, considered part of the original structure of the Kaaba
شوط (shaut): One complete circuit around the Kaaba

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why must tawaf be performed from outside the Hateem?
A) Because the Hateem is a sacred area but not part of the Kaaba
B) Because the Hateem is considered part of the Kaaba's original structure
C) To avoid overcrowding
D) Because it is a sunnah but not obligatory

Key Takeaway
Tawaf must consist of seven circuits, all performed outside the Hateem because it is part of the Kaaba.

The Sunnah of Idtiba' in Tawaf al-Qudum
Ruling with proof on idtiba'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of idtiba', identify when it is performed as a sunnah according to the Hanafi school, and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Idtiba' is sunnah only for the arrival tawaf that includes raml, not for all tawaf.

This passage from the chapter on Hajj clarifies the specific ruling and method of idtiba' (exposing the right shoulder) during tawaf. It distinguishes between the general practice and the proper timing, showing that it is a sunnah linked to the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) when raml (jogging) is also performed. The proof is taken from the Prophet's action, as narrated by Ibn Abbas.

Guided Path
1
Define idtiba'
Read the first lines: 'Idtiba' is that you place the cloth under the right armpit and throw its ends over the left shoulder.' Understand the physical action—exposing the right shoulder.
The term comes from the root ض ب ع (armpit).
2
Identify the context
Notice the phrase 'This is the tawaf of arrival; in it raml is performed, so in it one makes idtiba'.' The Hanafi ruling ties idtiba' specifically to tawaf al-qudum (the arrival tawaf) when raml is done.
Tawaf al-qudum is a sunnah for those performing Hajj ifrad or qiran.
3
Locate the proof
The author cites the hadith: 'From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah and his companions performed Umrah from Ji'ranah, and they did raml around the House, and they placed their cloaks under their armpits and threw them over their left shoulders.' This is from Sunan Abi Dawud.
The hadith shows the Prophet doing both raml and idtiba' together.
4
Determine the ruling level
The hadith reports an action, not a command. Hanafi usul holds that the Prophet's action indicates recommendation (sunnah), not obligation (wajib). Hence idtiba' is sunnah muakkadah in this context.
If it were wajib, the Prophet would have commanded it explicitly.
5
Scope of application
Idtiba' is not for all tawaf; it is only for the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum when raml is performed. After completing raml, the pilgrim may cover both shoulders.
Shafi'i school extends it to all tawaf; this is a legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مضطجعا وهو ان تجعل الرداء تحت الابط الايمن وتلقى طرفيه على الايسر (١٣١٥) ترجمه : (۱۳۱۵) اضطباع کے ساتھ ، اور وہ یہ ہے کہ چادر کو دائیں بغل کے نیچے کرے اور دونوں کناروں کو بائیں مونڈھے پر تشریح : یہ طواف قدوم ہے، اس میں رمل کرنا ہے، اس لئے اس میں اضطباع کرے، اور اضطباع یہ ہے کہ احرام کی چادر کو دائیں بغل کے نیچے سے نکالے اور دونوں کناروں کو بائیں مونڈھے پر ڈال دے، یہ اضطباع ہے۔ وجه :(۲) اضطباع کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس ان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم واصحابه اعتمروا من الجعرانة فرملوا بالبيت وجعلوا ارديتهم تحت ابا طهم قد قذفوها على عواتقهم اليسرى . (ابودا ادشریف، باب الاضطباع في الطواف ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف شروع کرنے سے پہلے اپنی چادر کا اضطباع کرے۔۔ابط : بغل۔
He said: 'Idtiba' is that you place the cloth under the right armpit and throw its ends over the left shoulder.' Translation: (1315) With idtiba', and it is that you place the cloth under the right armpit and its two ends on the left shoulder. Explanation: This is the tawaf of arrival; in it raml is performed, so in it one makes idtiba'. And idtiba' is that you take the ihram cloth from under the right armpit and put both ends on the left shoulder, this is idtiba'. Proof: (2) The evidence for performing idtiba' is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah and his companions performed Umrah from Ji'ranah, and they did raml around the House, and they placed their cloaks under their right armpits and threw them over their left shoulders. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Idtiba' in Tawaf, p. 266 no. 1884) From this hadith it is understood that before starting tawaf one should make idtiba' of his cloth. 'Ibt': armpit.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the chapter on the composition of Hajj actions. It defines idtiba' as wrapping the ihram cloth under the right armpit and throwing its ends over the left shoulder. The author explains that this is done during the tawaf of arrival (tawaf al-qudum), which also includes raml (jogging). The idtiba' is specific to this tawaf because it demonstrates vigor. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas that the Prophet and his Companions performed umrah from Ji'ranah and made raml and idtiba'. The moral: the ruling is sunnah, not wajib.

Key Terms
اضطباع (idtiba'): Wrapping the ihram cloth under the right armpit and throwing the ends over the left shoulder, exposing the right shoulder.
رمل (raml): Jogging with short steps while shaking the shoulders, like a warrior strutting between two ranks.
طواف قدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Mecca before standing at Arafat; it is sunnah for those performing Hajj ifrad or qiran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the meaning of 'idtiba'' as described in the text?
A) Placing the cloth under the left armpit and over the right shoulder
B) Placing the cloth under the right armpit and over the left shoulder
C) Jogging with shoulder shaking
D) Walking slowly

Key Takeaway
Idtiba' is sunnah only for the arrival tawaf (with raml), not wajib and not for all tawaf.

Rulings on Tawaf: Seven Circuits, Supplication, and Hatim
Ruling with proof on number of circuits, supplication, and place of tawaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of tawaf circuits, the recommended supplication, and the condition of performing tawaf outside the Hatim, and cite the primary hadith proofs.

Core Idea
Tawaf requires seven complete circuits outside the Hatim with supplication; missing the Hatim invalidates the circuit.

This lesson covers three essential rulings of tawaf from the Hanafi school: the number of circuits (seven), the recommended supplication during tawaf, and the critical requirement to perform tawaf outside the Hatim (also called Hijr Ismail). Each ruling is supported by authentic hadith. Understanding these ensures the validity of tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three rulings
From the passage, extract the three distinct rulings: (1) tawaf has seven circuits, (2) one may supplicate as desired, (3) tawaf must be performed behind the Hatim.
These are the core points of the passage.
2
Examine the hadith for seven circuits
Read the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet performed three circuits with jogging and four walking. This establishes the number seven.
The hadith is from Bukhari and Abu Dawud.
3
Examine the hadith for Hatim's status
Read the two hadith from Aisha. The first explains that Quraysh excluded the Hatim due to lack of funds. The second confirms the Hatim is a piece of the Kaaba.
These hadith prove that tawaf must encompass the Hatim.
4
Note the recommended supplication
The passage mentions a specific supplication between the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone: 'Rabbana atina...' (Quran 2:102). This is sunnah.
Supplication during tawaf is recommended, not wajib.
5
Recognize the cross-madhhab difference
The Hanafi school requires tawaf outside the Hatim. The Shafi'i school holds that cutting through does not invalidate the circuit but requires repetition. Understand the practical impact.
Both schools require repeating the circuit if one walks inside the Hatim, but the Hanafi view is stricter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۱۶) سبعة اشواط داعيا فيها بما شئت وطف وراء الحطيم ترجمه : (۱۳۱۶) طواف سات چکر ہے، اس میں جو چاہے دعا کرئے ۔ اور حطیم کے باہر سے طواف کرے۔ تشريح طواف سات چکر کرے، اور چونکہ حطیم بیت اللہ کا حصہ ہے اس لئے اس کے باہر سے طواف کرے، اس کو چھوڑے نہیں وجه : (۱) سات شوط طواف کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال سعى النبي ام ثلثة اشواط ومشى صلى الله اربعة في الحج والعمرة ـ ( بخاری شریف، باب الرمل في الحج والعمرة ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۳ رابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف میں سات مرتبہ بیت اللہ کے چاروں طرف چکر لگائے جس کو سات شوط کہتے ہیں۔ (۲) اور حطیم کے پیچھے سے طواف کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت سألت رسول الله عن الجدر ؟ أمن البيت هو ؟ قال : نعم قلت فلم لم يدخلوه البيت ؟ قال ان قومک قصرت بهم النفقة قلت فما شأن بابه مــرتـفـع ؟ قال فعل ذالک قومک لیدخلوا من شآؤا و يمنعوا من شآؤا و لولا أن قومك حديث عهدهم في الجاهلية فأخاف أن تنكر قلوبهم لنظرت أن ادخل الجدر في البيت ، و ان الزق بابه بالارض (مسلم شریف، باب جدر الکعبه و با بها، ص ۵۶۳، نمبر ۳۲۴۹/۱۳۳۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ خرچ کی کمی کی وجہ سے قریش نے حطیم کو بیت اللہ میں داخل نہیں کیا اور نہ وہ بیت اللہ میں داخل ہے، اس لئے اس کے پیچھے سے طواف کرے۔ (۲) اس حدیث میں بھی ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت كنت احب ان ادخل البيت فاصلى فيه فاخذ رسول الله الله بیدی فادخلني الحجر وقال صلى في الحجر ان اردت دخول البيت فانما هو قطعة من البيت ولكن قومك استقصروه حين بنوا الكعبة فاخرجوه من البيت. ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ فی المجر ص ۷۷ے انمبر ۱/۸۷۶ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ فی الحجرص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۲۰۲۸ مسلم شریف ، باب جدر الکعبه و با بها، ص ۵۶۳، نمبر ۳۲۴۹/۱۳۳۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حطیم جس کو حجر بھی کہتے ہیں بیت اللہ کا حصہ ہے۔ (۳) طواف میں یہ دعا پڑھے تو اچھا ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن السائب قال سمعت رسول الله علة يقول بين الركنين ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة و في الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار (آیت ۱۰۲ سورة البقرۃ ۲)۔(ابود ودشریف، باب الدعا فی الطواف ، ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۹۲)
(1316) Seven circuits, supplicating in them as you wish, and perform tawaf behind the Hatim. Translation: Tawaf is seven circuits, in it supplicate as you wish, and perform tawaf from outside the Hatim. Explanation: He should make seven circuits of tawaf, and because the Hatim is part of the House of Allah, he should perform tawaf from outside it, not leaving it. Proof: (1) The evidence for seven circuits is this hadith: From Ibn Umar: The Prophet performed three circuits with jogging and walked four in Hajj and Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab al-Raml fi al-Hajj wa al-Umrah, p. 218 no. 1603; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Raml, p. 266 no. 1886) From this hadith it is understood that in tawaf one goes around the Kaaba seven times, which are called seven circuits. (2) The evidence for performing tawaf behind the Hatim is this hadith: From Aisha: I asked the Messenger of Allah about the wall: 'Is it part of the House?' He said: 'Yes.' I said: 'Then why did they not include it in the House?' He said: 'Your people lacked funds.' I said: 'Why is its door raised?' He said: 'Your people did that so they could let in whomever they wished and prevent whomever they wished. Were it not that your people are near to the time of Jahiliyyah and I fear their hearts would deny, I would have included the wall in the House and made its door level with the ground.' (Muslim, Bab Jidr al-Ka'bah wa Babiha, p. 563 no. 3249/1333) In this hadith it is that due to lack of funds, Quraysh did not include the Hatim in the Kaaba and it is not inside the Kaaba, so perform tawaf behind it. (2) There is also this hadith: From Aisha: I used to love to enter the House and pray in it. So the Messenger of Allah took my hand and made me enter the Hijr and said: 'Pray in the Hijr if you wish to enter the House, for it is a piece of the House, but your people shortened it when building the Kaaba and took it out of the House.' (Tirmidhi, Bab ma Ja'a fi al-Salah fi al-Hijr, p. 77 no. 876; Abu Dawud, Bab al-Salah fi al-Hijr, p. 284 no. 2028; Muslim, Bab Jidr al-Ka'bah wa Babiha, p. 563 no. 3249/1333) From this hadith it is understood that the Hatim, also called Hijr, is part of the House of Allah. (3) It is good to recite this supplication during tawaf: From Abdullah ibn al-Sa'ib: I heard the Messenger of Allah between the two corners saying: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good and protect us from the punishment of the Fire.' (Quran 2:102) (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Du'a fi al-Tawaf, p. 276 no. 1892)
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the essential aspects of tawaf. First, tawaf consists of seven circuits, as proven by the hadith of Ibn Umar where the Prophet performed three circuits with raml and four walking. Second, one should supplicate freely during tawaf; a recommended supplication is the Quranic verse 'Rabbana atina...' between the Yemeni corner and the Black Stone. Third, tawaf must be performed outside the Hatim (also called Hijr), because the Hatim is part of the original Kaaba but was excluded by Quraysh due to funding. The hadith from Aisha confirms that the Prophet wished to include it but refrained. Therefore, walking through the Hatim invalidates that part of tawaf.

Key Terms
حطيم (Hatim): The semi-circular wall opposite the corner of the Kaaba, also called Hijr Ismail; it is part of the original Kaaba.
شوط (shawt): One complete circuit around the Kaaba. Seven shawt make one tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They forgot
B) They lacked sufficient funds
C) They wanted to reduce the size for security
D) The Prophet forbade them

Key Takeaway
Tawaf must consist of seven circuits, with supplication, and must be performed outside the Hatim to be valid.

The Ruling of Raml (Jogging) in the First Three Circuits of Tawaf
Ruling with proof on jogging with shoulder shaking during the first three circuits of tawaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of raml, describe its manner, and cite the prophetic proofs establishing it as a sunnah muakkadah.

Core Idea
Raml is a sunnah muakkadah for men in the first three circuits of arrival tawaf, symbolizing strength.

This lesson examines the practice of raml — walking quickly with shoulder shaking — during the first three circuits of tawaf after which sa'i is performed. We will explore its definition, its ruling as a confirmed sunnah, and the primary hadith evidence from the Prophet's practice. Understanding raml helps us appreciate the historical context and the continuity of prophetic tradition in Hajj and Umrah rituals.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what raml is and its legal status in the Hanafi school. Is it fard, wajib, sunnah, or mubah? From the passage, we see it is a sunnah muakkadah for men.
The passage explicitly states it is sunnah, not wajib.
2
Describe the manner of raml
Examine the description: walking quickly with short steps while shaking the shoulders, resembling a warrior strutting between ranks. Note that this applies only to men; women do not perform raml.
The analogy to a warrior shows the symbolic purpose.
3
Locate the dalil
Identify the primary hadith evidence cited. The passage provides three hadith: the origin story from Ibn Abbas, the practice of Ibn Umar, and the observation of Salim from his father.
All three are from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
4
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the hadith prove the ruling. The Prophet's command and his own practice indicate that raml is a recommended act. The reason (showing strength) is a wisdom, not a cause that changes the ruling to wajib.
The Prophet's order to the Companions was in response to the polytheists' taunt.
5
Note the inter-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Hanafi school restricts raml to the first three circuits of the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) only when sa'i follows. The Shafi'i school applies raml to any tawaf that includes sa'i. Both agree it is sunnah.
The practical difference is the scope of application.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۱۳۱۷) وان اردت ان تسعى بين الصفا والمروة عقب الطواف فارمل في الثلاثة الاشواط الاول وهو المشى بسرعة مع هزّ الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفّين ترجمه : (۱۳۱۷) اگر طواف کے بعد صفا و مروہ کی سعی کا ارادہ ہو تو طواف کے پہلے تین چکر میں رمل کر ، اور ریل یہ ہے کہ تیزی کے ساتھ مونڈھے ہلاتے ہوئے چلنا، جیسا کہ جنگ کے میدان میں ) صفوں کے درمیان اکڑ کر چلتا ہے۔ تشریح : جس طواف کے بعد سعی کرنی ہے، چاہے حج میں ہو یا عمرے میں تو اس کے پہلے تین شوط میں رمل کرے، رمل کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مونڈھے ہلاتے ہوئے تیزی کے ساتھ اکڑ کر چلے جس طرح جنگ کے صفوں کے درمیان بہادر مجاہدا کٹڑ کر چلتا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) مشرکین مکہ نے صحابہ کے بارے میں کہا تھا کہ یہ لوگ مدینے میں کمزور ہو گئے تو حضور نے طاقت دکھلانے کے لئے اکٹر کر چلنے کے لئے فرمایا تھا، وہ حکم آج بھی باقی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قدم رسول الله واصحابه فقال المشركون انه يقدم عـلـيـكـم وفـد وهنهم حمى يثرب فامرهم النبي الله ان يرملوا الاشواط الثلثة وان يمشوا ما بين الر کنین. (بخاری شریف، باب کیف كان بدء الرسل ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۲ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کس طرح رمل کی ابتدا ہوئی۔ (۲) رمل کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال سعى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثلثة اشواط ومشى اربعة في الحج والعمرة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الرحل في الحج والعمرة ، ص ۲۱۸، نمبر ۱۶۰۳ ارابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے پہلے تین شوط میں رمل کرے (۳) عن سالم عن ابيه قال رأيت رسول الله الا الله حين يقدم مكة اذا استلم الركن الاسود أول ما يطوف يخب ثلاثة أطواف من السبع ( بخاری شریف ، باب استلام الحجر الاسود حين يقدم مكتة أول ما يطوف و ریل خلا نا ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۱۶۰۳ر مسلم شریف، باب استحباب الرمل في الطواف في العمرة وفي الطواف الاول في المج، ص ۵۳۳ نمبر ۳۰۴۹/۱۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلی مرتبہ کے طواف میں پہلے تین چکر میں اکڑ کر چلے اور باقی چار میں اپنی ہیئت پر چلے۔
(1317) And if you intend to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah after the tawaf, then make raml in the first three circuits, and raml is walking quickly with shaking of the shoulders, like a warrior strutting between two ranks. Translation: If after tawaf you intend sa'i between Safa and Marwah, then in the first three circuits of tawaf perform raml, and raml is walking quickly while shaking the shoulders, like a brave mujahid strutting between ranks in the battlefield. Explanation: The tawaf after which sa'i is to be performed, whether in Hajj or Umrah, in its first three circuits he should perform raml. Raml means walking quickly with shoulder shaking and strutting like a brave warrior between the ranks of battle. Proof: (1) The polytheists of Mecca said about the Companions that these people have become weak in Madinah, so the Prophet ordered them to walk with strutting to show strength, and that command remains today. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah and his Companions arrived, and the polytheists said, 'A delegation has come to you whom the fever of Yathrib has weakened.' So the Prophet ordered them to do raml for three circuits and to walk between the two corners. (Bukhari, Bab Kayfa kana bad' al-raml, p. 218 no. 1602; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Raml, p. 266 no. 1886) From this hadith it is understood how raml began. (2) The evidence for performing raml is this hadith: From Ibn Umar: The Prophet performed three circuits with jogging and walked four in Hajj and Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab al-Raml fi al-Hajj wa al-Umrah, p. 218 no. 1603; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-Raml, p. 266 no. 1886) From this hadith it is understood that in the first three circuits of tawaf, one should do raml. (3) From Salim from his father: I saw the Messenger of Allah when he arrived in Mecca, when he kissed the Black Stone at the beginning of his tawaf, he jogged three circuits out of seven. (Bukhari, Bab Istilam al-Hajar al-Aswad, p. 260 no. 1603; Muslim, Bab Istihbab al-Raml, p. 533 no. 3049/126) In this hadith it is that in the first tawaf, he walked with strutting in the first three circuits and walked normally in the remaining four.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling of raml (jogging with shoulder shaking) during the first three circuits of tawaf. It is specific to the tawaf after which sa'i is performed, i.e., the arrival tawaf (tawaf al-qudum) for those performing Hajj or Umrah. The description of raml is walking quickly with movement of the shoulders, like a warrior strutting. The author provides three hadith proofs: (1) The origin of raml: when the polytheists claimed the Muslims were weak from Madinah's fever, the Prophet ordered them to show vigor by jogging. This command remains a sunnah. (2) The hadith of Ibn Umar confirms three circuits of raml and four of normal walking. (3) The hadith of Ibn Umar (from Salim) confirms the practice of the Prophet doing three circuits of jogging in the first tawaf. Hence, raml is a confirmed sunnah for the first three circuits.

Key Terms
رمل (raml): Walking quickly with short steps while shaking the shoulders, like a warrior strutting between two ranks.
اضطباع (idtiba'): Exposing the right shoulder by wrapping the cloth under the right armpit and over the left shoulder.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Raml is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for men in the first three circuits of the arrival tawaf, based on explicit prophetic command and practice.

Raml in Tawaf: Ruling, Definition, and Evidence
Ruling with proof: raml definition and hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raml, define it, explain its historical origin, and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah in the first three circuits of a tawaf followed by sa'i, proven by the Prophet's command and practice.

The lesson begins with the ruling that if you intend to perform sa'i after tawaf, you should do raml in the first three circuits. Raml is a brisk walk with shoulder shaking, reminiscent of a warrior's stride. The passage provides the reason—to counter polytheist claims of weakness—and cites multiple hadiths from Ibn Abbas, Ibn Umar, and Salim to establish the practice as sunnah. Understanding this ruling requires examining the proof structure and the Hanafi classification of raml as sunnah mu'akkadah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Locate in the text the command to do raml and determine its fiqh classification (fard, wajib, sunnah, etc.). The text says 'do raml' and later calls it 'necessary' but clarifies it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
Note the translation of 'daruri' as 'necessary'—in context it means strongly recommended, not obligatory.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the hadith proofs cited. The text gives three hadiths: from Ibn Abbas on the origin, from Ibn Umar on the Prophet's practice, and from Salim on the three circuits of raml.
All hadith are from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how each hadith proves the ruling. The imperative 'irramlu' in Ibn Abbas's hadith indicates a command. In Hanafi usul, a command from the Prophet for a non-obligatory act indicates sunnah. The descriptive hadith show the Prophet's consistent practice (fi'l), also a proof for sunnah.
The historical reason (showing strength) does not change the ruling; the command remains.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text includes an alternative view from Ibn Abbas that raml is not sunnah but mustahabb. This is a legitimate early ikhtilaf. The Hanafi school follows the majority view that it is sunnah mu'akkadah.
The author presents this view as a concession for extreme crowding.
5
State the mufta bihi
The operative position: raml is sunnah mu'akkadah in the first three circuits of a tawaf followed by sa'i in Hajj or Umrah. Abandoning it without excuse is makruh tanzihi.
No compensation (dam) is required for omission.

فصل تركيب افعال الحج (۱۳۱۷) وان اردت ان تسعى بين الصفا والمروة عقب الطواف فارمل في الثلاثة الاشواط الاول وهو المشى بسرعة مع هزّ الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفّين قالت كنت احب ان ادخل البيت فاصلى فيه فاخذ رسول الله الله بيدي فادخلني الحجر وقال صلى في الحجر ان اردت دخول البيت فانما هو قطعة من البيت ولكن قومك استقصروه حين بنوا الكعبة فاخرجوه من البيت. ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ فی المجر ص ۷۷ے انمبر ۱/۸۷۶ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ فی الحجرص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۲۰۲۸ مسلم شریف ، باب جدر الکعبه و با بها، ص ۵۶۳، نمبر ۳۲۴۹/۱۳۳۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حطیم جس کو حجر بھی کہتے ہیں بیت اللہ کا حصہ ہے۔ (۳) طواف میں یہ دعا پڑھے تو اچھا ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن السائب قال سمعت رسول الله علة يقول بين الركنين ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة و في الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار (آیت ۱۰۲ سورة البقرۃ ۲)۔(ابود ودشریف، باب الدعا فی الطواف ، ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۹۲) ترجمه : (۱۳۱۷) اگر طواف کے بعد صفا و مروہ کی سعی کا ارادہ ہو تو طواف کے پہلے تین چکر میں رمل کر ، اور ریل یہ ہے کہ تیزی کے ساتھ مونڈھے ہلاتے ہوئے چلنا، جیسا کہ جنگ کے میدان میں صفوں کے درمیان اکڑ کر چلتا ہے۔ تشریح : جس طواف کے بعد سعی کرنی ہے، چاہے حج میں ہو یا عمرے میں تو اس کے پہلے تین شوط میں رمل کرے، رمل کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مونڈھے ہلاتے ہوئے تیزی کے ساتھ اکڑ کر چلے جس طرح جنگ کے صفوں کے درمیان بہادر مجاہدا کٹڑ کر چلتا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) مشرکین مکہ نے صحابہ کے بارے میں کہا تھا کہ یہ لوگ مدینے میں کمزور ہو گئے تو حضور نے طاقت دکھلانے کے لئے اکٹر کر چلنے کے لئے فرمایا تھا، وہ حکم آج بھی باقی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قدم رسول الله واصحابه فقال المشركون انه يقدم عـلـيـكـم وفـد وهنهم حمى يثرب فامرهم النبي الله ان يرملوا الاشواط الثلثة وان يمشوا ما بين الر کنین. (بخاری شریف، باب کیف كان بدء الرسل ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۲ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کس طرح رمل کی ابتدا ہوئی۔ (۲) رمل کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال سعى النبي صلى الله ثلثة اشواط ومشى اربعة في الحج والعمرة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الرحل في الحج والعمرة ، ص ۲۱۸، نمبر ۱۶۰۳ ارابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے پہلے تین شوط میں رمل کرے (۳) عن سالم عن ابيه قال رأيت رسول الله الا الله حين يقدم مكة اذا استلم الركن الاسود أول ما يطوف يخب ثلاثة أطواف من السبع ( بخاری شریف ، باب استلام الحجر الاسود حين يقدم مكتة أول ما يطوف و ریل خلا نا ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۱۶۰۳ر مسلم شریف، باب استحباب الرمل في الطواف في العمرة وفي الطواف الاول في المج، ص ۵۳۳ نمبر ۳۰۴۹/۱۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلی مرتبہ کے طواف میں پہلے تین چکر میں اکڑ کر چلے اور باقی چار میں اپنی ہیئت پر چلے۔ (۱۳۱۸ ) فان زحمه الناس وقف فاذا وجد فرجة رمل لا بد له منه فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون بخلاف استلام الحجر الاسود لان له بدلا وهو استقباله (۱۳۱۹) ويستلم الحجر كلّما مرّ لغت : رل اکڑ کر چلنا ۔ اشواط : شوط کی جمع ہے ، طواف کے ایک چکر کو ایک شوط کہتے ہیں۔ ھر : حرکت دینا۔ مبارز : برز سے مشتق ہے، باہر نکلنا، جنگ میں مقابلے کے لئے دعوت دینے والا ۔ تینتر : بختر سے مشتق ہے، متکبرانہ چال سے چلنا۔ زحم : بھیڑ فرجہ : کشادگی، راستہ۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۱۸) اگر لوگوں کا ہجوم ہو تو رک جائے پس جب کشادگی ملے تو رمل کرے جو اس کے لئے ضروری ہے،اس لئے ٹھہر جائے تاکہ مسنون طریقے پر ادا کر سکے، بخلاف حجر اسود چومنے کے اس لئے کہ اس کا بدل استقبال کرنا موجود ہے۔ تشریح : رمل کر رہا تھا کہ بھیڑ آ گئی تو وہیں ٹھہر جائے تا کہ بھیڑ کم ہو جائے تو مسنون طریقے پر رمل کرے، مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ بغیر ریل کے آگے نہ بڑھے ، کیونکہ رمل ضروری ہے اور اس کا کوئی بدل بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے ابھی رکے اور بھیڑ کم ہونے پر مسنون طریقے پر رمل کرتے ہوئے طواف پورا کرے۔ اس کے برخلاف حجر اسود کو بوسہ نہ دے سکے تو آگے بڑھتا چلا جائے کیونکہ اس کا بدل یہ ہے کہ دور سے حجر اسود کا استقبال کرے اور ہاتھ سے اشارہ کرے اور اس کو چوم لے ۔ آج کل حج کے موقع پر بہت بھیڑ ہوتی ہے اور دن رات بھیٹر رہتی ہے، اس لئے جتنا کٹر کر چل سکے چلے باقی میں اپنی ہیئت پر چل کر طواف پورا کرلے۔ وجه : (ا) وقال عطاء فيمن يطوف فتقام الصلاة او يدفع عن مكانه اذا سلم يرجع الى حيث قطع عليه فيبني . ويذكر نحوه عن ابن عمر و عبد الرحمن بن ابی بکر ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اوقف فی الطواف ، ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۶۲۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ درمیان میں کوئی انقطاع پیش آجائے تو دوبارہ بنا کرے۔(۲) ایسی بھیٹر ہو کہ ختم ہی نہیں ہو پا رہی ہو تو حضرت عبداللہ ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کر لے، انہوں نے فرمایا کہ رمل سنت نہیں ہے مستحب ہے اس لئے مجبوری کے وقت اس پر عمل کر لے۔ اثریہ ہے عن ابی طفيل قال قلت لابن عباس یزعم قومك أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قد رمل بالبيت و أن ذالك سنة ؟ قال صدقو ا و كذبوا قلت و ما صدقوا و ما كذبوا ؟ قال صدقوا قد رمل رسول الله الله و كذبوا، ليس بسنة - (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل، ص ۲۷۵، نمبر ۱۸۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ریل سنت نہیں ہے۔ (۲) ان ابن عباس و على بن حسين كانا لا يرملان . مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب من رخص فی ترک الرمل ، ج ثالث ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۴۱۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ریل واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے گنجائش نہ ہو تو اس پر عمل کر لے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۱۹) اور حجر اسود کا استلام کرے جب بھی اس کے پاس سے گزرے۔ اور استلام کے ساتھ ہی طواف پورا کرے،۔ تشریح : ہر طواف میں جب جب بھی حجر اسود کے سامنے سے گزرے اور موقع ملے تو اس کو چھوئے ، اور بھیٹر کی وجہ سے چھونے کا موقع نہ ہو تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کرے اور ہاتھ کو چوم لے۔ اور حجر اسود پر ہی آکر آخری طواف ختم کرے، تو گویا کہ حجر
Section on the composition of the actions of Hajj. (1317) If you intend to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then do raml in the first three circuits, which is walking quickly with shaking of the shoulders, like a champion strutting between the two rows. She said: I loved to enter the House and pray in it, so the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, took my hand and entered me into the Hijr and said: Pray in the Hijr if you intend to enter the House, for it is a part of the House, but your people shortened it when they built the Ka'bah and removed it from the House. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-salah fi al-Hijr, p. 77, no. 876; Abu Dawud, Bab al-salah fi al-Hijr, p. 284, no. 2028; Muslim, Bab jidr al-Ka'bah wa babuha, p. 563, no. 3249/1333). From this hadith it is known that the Hatim, which is also called Hijr, is part of the House of Allah. (3) It is good to recite this supplication during tawaf: From Abdullah ibn al-Sa'ib, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, say between the two corners: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the Fire' (verse 102 of Surah al-Baqarah). (Abu Dawud, Bab al-du'a fi al-tawaf, p. 276, no. 1892). Translation: (1317) If you intend to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then do raml in the first three circuits, and raml is to walk quickly while shaking the shoulders, like one who strides arrogantly between the rows in the battlefield. Commentary: In the tawaf after which sa'i is to be performed, whether in Hajj or Umrah, he should do raml in the first three circuits. The meaning of raml is to walk quickly with a proud gait, shaking the shoulders, like a brave warrior walks between the rows in battle. Reason: (1) The polytheists of Mecca said about the Companions that they had become weak in Madinah, so the Prophet ordered them to walk with a proud gait to show strength, and that command remains today. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah and his Companions arrived, and the polytheists said: 'There comes to you a delegation weakened by the fever of Yathrib.' So the Prophet ordered them to do raml in the first three circuits and to walk between the two corners. (Bukhari, Bab kayf kana bad' al-raml, p. 218, no. 1602; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-raml, p. 266, no. 1886). From this hadith it is known how raml began. (2) The evidence for doing raml is this hadith: From Ibn Umar: The Prophet performed raml in three circuits and walked four in Hajj and Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab al-raml fi al-hajj wa al-umrah, p. 218, no. 1603; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-raml, p. 266, no. 1886). From this hadith it is known that one should do raml in the first three circuits. (3) From Salim from his father: I saw the Messenger of Allah when he arrived in Mecca, when he kissed the Black Stone as the first thing of tawaf, he hastened three circuits out of seven. (Bukhari, Bab istilam al-hajar al-aswad hina yaqdamu Makkata awwal ma yatufu wa al-raml, p. 260, no. 1603?; Muslim, Bab istihbab al-raml fi al-tawaf fi al-umrah wa fi al-tawaf al-awwal fi al-hajj, p. 533, no. 3049/126). This hadith states that in the first tawaf, one should walk with a proud gait in the first three circuits and walk normally in the remaining four. (1318) If people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds an opening, he does raml, which is necessary for him. So he stops so that he can perform it in the prescribed manner (al-wajh al-masnun), unlike kissing the Black Stone, because it has an alternative, which is to face it. (1319) And he touches the Stone every time he passes. Glossary: raml: walking with a proud gait. ashwat: plural of shawt, one circuit of tawaf. harr: to move. mubariz: derived from baraza, to come out, one who challenges in battle. yatabakhtar: derived from bakhtar, to walk arrogantly. ziham: crowding. farjah: opening, path. Translation: (1318) If there is a crowd of people, he stops. Then when he finds an opening, he does raml, which is necessary for him. So he stops so that he can perform it in the prescribed manner, unlike kissing the Black Stone because it has an alternative, which is to face it. Commentary: While doing raml, if a crowd came, he stops there until the crowd reduces, then he does raml in the prescribed manner. The author says that he should not proceed without raml, because raml is necessary and has no alternative, so he stops and when the crowd lessens, he completes the tawaf doing raml in the prescribed manner. In contrast, if he cannot kiss the Black Stone, he moves forward because its alternative is to face the Black Stone from a distance and gesture with the hand and then kiss the hand. Nowadays, during Hajj, there is a lot of crowding day and night, so he should walk with a proud gait as much as he can, and for the rest, he walks normally to complete the tawaf. Reason: (1) Ata said concerning one who is doing tawaf and the prayer is established or he is pushed from his place: when he finishes the prayer, he returns to where he was interrupted and builds upon it. Similar is narrated from Ibn Umar and Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr. (Bukhari, Bab idha uqifa fi al-tawaf, p. 263, no. 1623). This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that if an interruption occurs in between, he builds upon it from where he left off. (2) If the crowd is such that it never ends, then act upon the saying of Abdullah ibn Abbas, who said that raml is not sunnah but mustahabb, so in times of necessity, act upon it. There is an athar from Abu al-Tufayl: I said to Ibn Abbas: 'Your people claim that the Messenger of Allah did raml around the House and that it is a sunnah.' He said: 'They spoke truly and they lied.' I said: 'What did they speak truly and what did they lie?' He said: 'They spoke truly that the Messenger of Allah did raml, and they lied that it is a sunnah.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-raml, p. 275, no. 1885). This hadith states that raml is not a sunnah. (2) Ibn Abbas and Ali ibn Husayn did not do raml. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab man rakhkhasa fi tark al-raml, vol. 3, p. 265, no. 1416). This athar indicates that raml is not obligatory, so if there is no room, act upon it. Translation: (1319) And he does istilam of the Black Stone every time he passes by. And with istilam, he completes the tawaf. Commentary: In every tawaf, whenever he passes in front of the Black Stone and gets a chance, he touches it. If due to crowding he cannot touch it, he gestures towards it with his hand and then kisses his hand. And he ends the last circuit at the Black Stone, so that he completes the tawaf at it.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi fiqh work discussing the rulings of raml and istilam during tawaf. The author begins by stating the ruling (point 1317): if one intends to perform sa'i after tawaf, he should perform raml in the first three circuits. Raml is defined as walking briskly with shaking of the shoulders, like a warrior striding between ranks. The reason given is that the polytheists had said the Companions were weakened by the fever of Madinah, so the Prophet ordered them to show vigor. The author then provides several hadith proofs: Ibn Abbas narrates the origin; Ibn Umar confirms the Prophet did raml in three circuits; and a hadith from Salim indicates the Prophet did raml in the first three circuits of his first tawaf upon entering Mecca. An additional hadith about the Hijr being part of the Kaaba is included, as well as a recommended supplication between the Yemeni Corner and the Black Stone. Point 1318 addresses the scenario of crowding: if one is doing raml and is blocked by people, he should stop until there is an opening, then resume raml. This is because raml has no substitute, unlike kissing the Black Stone, which has the alternative of facing it and gesturing. The author cites Ata and Ibn Umar for the principle of building upon interrupted tawaf. An alternative view from Ibn Abbas is noted: he considered raml mustahabb, not sunnah, so in persistent crowding, one may act on that. Point 1319 rules that one should touch (istilam) the Black Stone every circuit, and if unable, gesture and kiss the hand. The tawaf should end at the Stone. The presentation follows the matn-commentary style, with the original numbered rulings followed by detailed explanation and evidence.

Key Terms
رمل (raml): Walking briskly with a proud gait and shaking of the shoulders during the first three circuits of tawaf
اشواط (ashwat): Plural of shawt, meaning the circuits of tawaf (one full circle around the Kaaba)
استلام (istilam): Touching or kissing the Black Stone (Hajar al-Aswad) during tawaf
حجر (hijr): The semicircular wall opposite the Kaaba, also called Hatim; considered part of the Kaaba's foundation

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Ibn Abbas, why did the Prophet order raml?
A) To make tawaf physically demanding as a form of worship.
B) To show strength and disprove the polytheists' claim that the Companions were weak.
C) To distinguish Muslims from non-Muslims during tawaf.
D) To prepare the Companions for battle.

Key Takeaway
Raml is an emphasized sunnah in the first three circuits of a tawaf followed by sa'i, proven by multiple authentic hadith, and omitting it without excuse is makruh tanzihi.

Raml When Crowded and Istilam of the Black Stone
Ruling with proof on crowding and istilam alternatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on raml when crowded and distinguish between raml and istilam regarding alternatives.

Core Idea
Raml has no substitute, so one must stop and wait if crowded; istilam has the alternative of facing the Black Stone and gesturing.

The previous lesson established that raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah. This lesson tackles practical challenges: what to do if a crowd prevents raml? The text (1318) rules that you should stop and wait for an opening, because raml has no substitute. In contrast, if you cannot touch the Black Stone (istilam), you may proceed and gesture, since it has an alternative. The lesson also presents the view of Ibn Abbas who considered raml mustahabb, which may be followed in persistent crowding. Understanding these distinctions helps pilgrims navigate actual Hajj conditions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling for raml when crowded
Read point (1318): if people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds an opening, he does raml. The text says 'raml is necessary for him' — meaning it is important to perform it in the correct manner.
'La budda lahu' means 'no alternative for him' in this context.
2
Understand the rationale: raml has no alternative
The text explicitly contrasts raml with istilam: raml has no substitute (badal), so you must wait and perform it; istilam has a substitute (facing the stone and gesturing), so you may move on.
This is a key fiqh principle: if an act has no substitute, one should delay to perform it; if it has a substitute, the substitute suffices.
3
Analyze the alternative view from Ibn Abbas
The commentator presents Ibn Abbas's view that raml is mustahabb, not sunnah. This provides a concession: if crowding is continuous and never ends, one may omit raml and follow Ibn Abbas's opinion.
This is an example of acting on a weaker view in cases of hardship (istihsan).
4
Apply the ruling for istilam
Point (1319) says to touch the Black Stone every time you pass. If unable, face it and gesture (isharah) and then kiss the hand. This is the alternative (badal).
The tawaf ends at the Stone, so the last circuit should conclude at the Stone.
5
Distinguish between the two rulings
Raml: must be performed when possible; if obstructed, stop and resume. Istilam: if obstructed, substitute with gesture and moving on. The difference is due to the nature of the act: raml is a mode of walking, istilam is a specific action at a fixed point.
This distinction shows the importance of understanding the legal nature (mahiyyah) of each act.

فصل تركيب افعال الحج (۱۳۱۷) وان اردت ان تسعى بين الصفا والمروة عقب الطواف فارمل في الثلاثة الاشواط الاول وهو المشى بسرعة مع هزّ الكتفين كالمبارز يتبختر بين الصفّين قالت كنت احب ان ادخل البيت فاصلى فيه فاخذ رسول الله الله بيدي فادخلني الحجر وقال صلى في الحجر ان اردت دخول البيت فانما هو قطعة من البيت ولكن قومك استقصروه حين بنوا الكعبة فاخرجوه من البيت. ترندی شریف، باب ماجاء فی الصلوۃ فی المجر ص ۷۷ے انمبر ۱/۸۷۶ ابو داؤد شریف ، باب الصلوۃ فی الحجرص ۲۸۴ نمبر ۲۰۲۸ مسلم شریف ، باب جدر الکعبه و با بها، ص ۵۶۳، نمبر ۳۲۴۹/۱۳۳۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حطیم جس کو حجر بھی کہتے ہیں بیت اللہ کا حصہ ہے۔ (۳) طواف میں یہ دعا پڑھے تو اچھا ہے۔ عن عبد الله بن السائب قال سمعت رسول الله علة يقول بين الركنين ربنا آتنا في الدنيا حسنة و في الآخرة حسنة وقنا عذاب النار (آیت ۱۰۲ سورة البقرۃ ۲)۔(ابود ودشریف، باب الدعا فی الطواف ، ص ۲۷۶ نمبر ۱۸۹۲) ترجمه : (۱۳۱۷) اگر طواف کے بعد صفا و مروہ کی سعی کا ارادہ ہو تو طواف کے پہلے تین چکر میں رمل کر ، اور ریل یہ ہے کہ تیزی کے ساتھ مونڈھے ہلاتے ہوئے چلنا، جیسا کہ جنگ کے میدان میں صفوں کے درمیان اکڑ کر چلتا ہے۔ تشریح : جس طواف کے بعد سعی کرنی ہے، چاہے حج میں ہو یا عمرے میں تو اس کے پہلے تین شوط میں رمل کرے، رمل کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ مونڈھے ہلاتے ہوئے تیزی کے ساتھ اکڑ کر چلے جس طرح جنگ کے صفوں کے درمیان بہادر مجاہدا کٹڑ کر چلتا ہے۔ وجه : (۱) مشرکین مکہ نے صحابہ کے بارے میں کہا تھا کہ یہ لوگ مدینے میں کمزور ہو گئے تو حضور نے طاقت دکھلانے کے لئے اکٹر کر چلنے کے لئے فرمایا تھا، وہ حکم آج بھی باقی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قدم رسول الله واصحابه فقال المشركون انه يقدم عـلـيـكـم وفـد وهنهم حمى يثرب فامرهم النبي الله ان يرملوا الاشواط الثلثة وان يمشوا ما بين الر کنین. (بخاری شریف، باب کیف كان بدء الرسل ص ۲۱۸ نمبر ۱۶۰۲ / ابو داؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ کس طرح رمل کی ابتدا ہوئی۔ (۲) رمل کرنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال سعى النبي صلى الله ثلثة اشواط ومشى اربعة في الحج والعمرة - ( بخاری شریف ، باب الرحل في الحج والعمرة ، ص ۲۱۸، نمبر ۱۶۰۳ ارابو داؤد شریف ، باب فی الرمل ص ۲۶۶ نمبر ۱۸۸۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے پہلے يطوف و ریل خلا نا ص ۲۶۰ نمبر ۱۶۰۳ر مسلم شریف، باب استحباب الرمل في الطواف في العمرة وفي الطواف الاول في المج، ص ۵۳۳ نمبر ۳۰۴۹/۱۲۶) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ پہلی مرتبہ کے طواف میں پہلے تین چکر میں اکڑ کر چلے اور باقی چار میں اپنی ہیئت پر چلے۔ (۱۳۱۸ ) فان زحمه الناس وقف فاذا وجد فرجة رمل لا بد له منه فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون بخلاف استلام الحجر الاسود لان له بدلا وهو استقباله (۱۳۱۹) ويستلم الحجر كلّما مرّ لغت : رل اکڑ کر چلنا ۔ اشواط : شوط کی جمع ہے ، طواف کے ایک چکر کو ایک شوط کہتے ہیں۔ ھر : حرکت دینا۔ مبارز : برز سے مشتق ہے، باہر نکلنا، جنگ میں مقابلے کے لئے دعوت دینے والا ۔ تینتر : بختر سے مشتق ہے، متکبرانہ چال سے چلنا۔ زحم : بھیڑ فرجہ : کشادگی، راستہ۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۱۸) اگر لوگوں کا ہجوم ہو تو رک جائے پس جب کشادگی ملے تو رمل کرے جو اس کے لئے ضروری ہے،اس لئے ٹھہر جائے تاکہ مسنون طریقے پر ادا کر سکے، بخلاف حجر اسود چومنے کے اس لئے کہ اس کا بدل استقبال کرنا موجود ہے۔ تشریح : رمل کر رہا تھا کہ بھیڑ آ گئی تو وہیں ٹھہر جائے تا کہ بھیڑ کم ہو جائے تو مسنون طریقے پر رمل کرے، مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ بغیر ریل کے آگے نہ بڑھے ، کیونکہ رمل ضروری ہے اور اس کا کوئی بدل بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے ابھی رکے اور بھیڑ کم ہونے پر مسنون طریقے پر رمل کرتے ہوئے طواف پورا کرے۔ اس کے برخلاف حجر اسود کو بوسہ نہ دے سکے تو آگے بڑھتا چلا جائے کیونکہ اس کا بدل یہ ہے کہ دور سے حجر اسود کا استقبال کرے اور ہاتھ سے اشارہ کرے اور اس کو چوم لے ۔ آج کل حج کے موقع پر بہت بھیڑ ہوتی ہے اور دن رات بھیٹر رہتی ہے، اس لئے جتنا کٹر کر چل سکے چلے باقی میں اپنی ہیئت پر چل کر طواف پورا کرلے۔ وجه : (ا) وقال عطاء فيمن يطوف فتقام الصلاة او يدفع عن مكانه اذا سلم يرجع الى حيث قطع عليه فيبني . ويذكر نحوه عن ابن عمر و عبد الرحمن بن ابی بکر ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اوقف فی الطواف ، ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۶۲۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ درمیان میں کوئی انقطاع پیش آجائے تو دوبارہ بنا کرے۔(۲) ایسی بھیٹر ہو کہ ختم ہی نہیں ہو پا رہی ہو تو حضرت عبداللہ ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کر لے، انہوں نے فرمایا کہ رمل سنت نہیں ہے مستحب ہے اس لئے مجبوری کے وقت اس پر عمل کر لے۔ اثریہ ہے عن ابی طفيل قال قلت لابن عباس یزعم قومك أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قد رمل بالبيت و أن ذالك سنة ؟ قال صدقو ا و كذبوا قلت و ما صدقوا و ما كذبوا ؟ قال صدقوا قد رمل رسول الله الله و كذبوا، ليس بسنة - (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل، ص ۲۷۵، نمبر ۱۸۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ریل سنت نہیں ہے۔ (۲) ان ابن عباس و على بن حسين كانا لا يرملان . مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب من رخص فی ترک الرمل ، ج ثالث ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۴۱۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ریل واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے گنجائش نہ ہو تو اس پر عمل کر لے۔ ترجمه : (۱۳۱۹) اور حجر اسود کا استلام کرے جب بھی اس کے پاس سے گزرے۔ اور استلام کے ساتھ ہی طواف پورا کرے،۔ تشریح : ہر طواف میں جب جب بھی حجر اسود کے سامنے سے گزرے اور موقع ملے تو اس کو چھوئے ، اور بھیٹر کی وجہ سے چھونے کا موقع نہ ہو تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کرے اور ہاتھ کو چوم لے۔ اور حجر اسود پر ہی آکر آخری طواف ختم کرے، تو گویا کہ حجر
Section on the composition of the actions of Hajj. (1317) If you intend to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then do raml in the first three circuits, which is walking quickly with shaking of the shoulders, like a champion strutting between the two rows. She said: I loved to enter the House and pray in it, so the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, took my hand and entered me into the Hijr and said: Pray in the Hijr if you intend to enter the House, for it is a part of the House, but your people shortened it when they built the Ka'bah and removed it from the House. (Tirmidhi, Bab ma ja'a fi al-salah fi al-Hijr, p. 77, no. 876; Abu Dawud, Bab al-salah fi al-Hijr, p. 284, no. 2028; Muslim, Bab jidr al-Ka'bah wa babuha, p. 563, no. 3249/1333). From this hadith it is known that the Hatim, which is also called Hijr, is part of the House of Allah. (3) It is good to recite this supplication during tawaf: From Abdullah ibn al-Sa'ib, he said: I heard the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, say between the two corners: 'Our Lord, give us in this world good and in the Hereafter good, and protect us from the punishment of the Fire' (verse 102 of Surah al-Baqarah). (Abu Dawud, Bab al-du'a fi al-tawaf, p. 276, no. 1892). Translation: (1317) If you intend to perform sa'i between Safa and Marwah after tawaf, then do raml in the first three circuits, and raml is to walk quickly while shaking the shoulders, like one who strides arrogantly between the rows in the battlefield. Commentary: In the tawaf after which sa'i is to be performed, whether in Hajj or Umrah, he should do raml in the first three circuits. The meaning of raml is to walk quickly with a proud gait, shaking the shoulders, like a brave warrior walks between the rows in battle. Reason: (1) The polytheists of Mecca said about the Companions that they had become weak in Madinah, so the Prophet ordered them to walk with a proud gait to show strength, and that command remains today. From Ibn Abbas: The Messenger of Allah and his Companions arrived, and the polytheists said: 'There comes to you a delegation weakened by the fever of Yathrib.' So the Prophet ordered them to do raml in the first three circuits and to walk between the two corners. (Bukhari, Bab kayf kana bad' al-raml, p. 218, no. 1602; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-raml, p. 266, no. 1886). From this hadith it is known how raml began. (2) The evidence for doing raml is this hadith: From Ibn Umar: The Prophet performed raml in three circuits and walked four in Hajj and Umrah. (Bukhari, Bab al-raml fi al-hajj wa al-umrah, p. 218, no. 1603; Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-raml, p. 266, no. 1886). From this hadith it is known that one should do raml in the first three circuits. (3) From Salim from his father: I saw the Messenger of Allah when he arrived in Mecca, when he kissed the Black Stone as the first thing of tawaf, he hastened three circuits out of seven. (Bukhari, Bab istilam al-hajar al-aswad hina yaqdamu Makkata awwal ma yatufu wa al-raml, p. 260, no. 1603?; Muslim, Bab istihbab al-raml fi al-tawaf fi al-umrah wa fi al-tawaf al-awwal fi al-hajj, p. 533, no. 3049/126). This hadith states that in the first tawaf, one should walk with a proud gait in the first three circuits and walk normally in the remaining four. (1318) If people crowd him, he stops, and when he finds an opening, he does raml, which is necessary for him. So he stops so that he can perform it in the prescribed manner (al-wajh al-masnun), unlike kissing the Black Stone, because it has an alternative, which is to face it. (1319) And he touches the Stone every time he passes. Glossary: raml: walking with a proud gait. ashwat: plural of shawt, one circuit of tawaf. harr: to move. mubariz: derived from baraza, to come out, one who challenges in battle. yatabakhtar: derived from bakhtar, to walk arrogantly. ziham: crowding. farjah: opening, path. Translation: (1318) If there is a crowd of people, he stops. Then when he finds an opening, he does raml, which is necessary for him. So he stops so that he can perform it in the prescribed manner, unlike kissing the Black Stone because it has an alternative, which is to face it. Commentary: While doing raml, if a crowd came, he stops there until the crowd reduces, then he does raml in the prescribed manner. The author says that he should not proceed without raml, because raml is necessary and has no alternative, so he stops and when the crowd lessens, he completes the tawaf doing raml in the prescribed manner. In contrast, if he cannot kiss the Black Stone, he moves forward because its alternative is to face the Black Stone from a distance and gesture with the hand and then kiss the hand. Nowadays, during Hajj, there is a lot of crowding day and night, so he should walk with a proud gait as much as he can, and for the rest, he walks normally to complete the tawaf. Reason: (1) Ata said concerning one who is doing tawaf and the prayer is established or he is pushed from his place: when he finishes the prayer, he returns to where he was interrupted and builds upon it. Similar is narrated from Ibn Umar and Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr. (Bukhari, Bab idha uqifa fi al-tawaf, p. 263, no. 1623). This saying of a Tabi'i indicates that if an interruption occurs in between, he builds upon it from where he left off. (2) If the crowd is such that it never ends, then act upon the saying of Abdullah ibn Abbas, who said that raml is not sunnah but mustahabb, so in times of necessity, act upon it. There is an athar from Abu al-Tufayl: I said to Ibn Abbas: 'Your people claim that the Messenger of Allah did raml around the House and that it is a sunnah.' He said: 'They spoke truly and they lied.' I said: 'What did they speak truly and what did they lie?' He said: 'They spoke truly that the Messenger of Allah did raml, and they lied that it is a sunnah.' (Abu Dawud, Bab fi al-raml, p. 275, no. 1885). This hadith states that raml is not a sunnah. (2) Ibn Abbas and Ali ibn Husayn did not do raml. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, Bab man rakhkhasa fi tark al-raml, vol. 3, p. 265, no. 1416). This athar indicates that raml is not obligatory, so if there is no room, act upon it. Translation: (1319) And he does istilam of the Black Stone every time he passes by. And with istilam, he completes the tawaf. Commentary: In every tawaf, whenever he passes in front of the Black Stone and gets a chance, he touches it. If due to crowding he cannot touch it, he gestures towards it with his hand and then kisses his hand. And he ends the last circuit at the Black Stone, so that he completes the tawaf at it.
Source pages p. 357

Commentary
This passage is from a Hanafi fiqh work discussing the rulings of raml and istilam during tawaf. The author begins by stating the ruling (point 1317): if one intends to perform sa'i after tawaf, he should perform raml in the first three circuits. Raml is defined as walking briskly with shaking of the shoulders, like a warrior striding between ranks. The reason given is that the polytheists had said the Companions were weakened by the fever of Madinah, so the Prophet ordered them to show vigor. The author then provides several hadith proofs: Ibn Abbas narrates the origin; Ibn Umar confirms the Prophet did raml in three circuits; and a hadith from Salim indicates the Prophet did raml in the first three circuits of his first tawaf upon entering Mecca. An additional hadith about the Hijr being part of the Kaaba is included, as well as a recommended supplication between the Yemeni Corner and the Black Stone. Point 1318 addresses the scenario of crowding: if one is doing raml and is blocked by people, he should stop until there is an opening, then resume raml. This is because raml has no substitute, unlike kissing the Black Stone, which has the alternative of facing it and gesturing. The author cites Ata and Ibn Umar for the principle of building upon interrupted tawaf. An alternative view from Ibn Abbas is noted: he considered raml mustahabb, not sunnah, so in persistent crowding, one may act on that. Point 1319 rules that one should touch (istilam) the Black Stone every circuit, and if unable, gesture and kiss the hand. The tawaf should end at the Stone. The presentation follows the matn-commentary style, with the original numbered rulings followed by detailed explanation and evidence.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute; an alternative action that replaces the original when it is not possible.
زحام (ziham): Crowding, pushing of people; a common situation during Hajj.
استقبال (istiqbal): Facing; here, facing the Black Stone from a distance as a substitute for touching it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why should a pilgrim stop and wait when crowded during raml rather than substitute it?
A) Because raml is wajib.
B) Because raml has no alternative (badal).
C) Because stopping is a sunnah itself.
D) Because the crowd is a test of patience.

Key Takeaway
Raml has no substitute, so one must stop and wait if crowded; istilam has a substitute (gesture), so one may proceed.

Raml When Crowded During Tawaf
Ruling on stopping raml during crowd and resuming, with contrast to kissing Black Stone.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raml when crowded during tawaf and explain the difference between raml and kissing the Black Stone regarding the availability of a substitute.

Core Idea
Raml must be performed in its sunnah manner; if crowded, stop and resume—unlike kissing the Black Stone which has a substitute.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hajj manual: what should a pilgrim do if a crowd prevents them from performing raml (quick walking) during tawaf? The Hanafi school provides a clear directive: stop and wait for an opening, then resume raml in the sunnah manner. This ruling is contrasted with kissing the Black Stone, which can be substituted by facing it from a distance. The passage also presents evidence from the Companions to support this view, including a narration from Ibn 'Abbas that is used to justify omitting raml in extreme necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Raml is a sunnah mu'akkadah (or wajib) act for men in the first three circuits of tawaf al-qudum. The text says 'la budda lahu minhu' (unavoidable), indicating its necessity.
2
Understand the condition and response
If a crowd prevents raml, stop and wait for an opening. Do not proceed without raml because it has no substitute (la badal lahu).
3
Contrast with kissing the Black Stone
Kissing the Black Stone can be substituted by facing it and pointing; thus you may proceed without stopping.
4
Examine the evidence
The text cites narrations: 'Ata's saying about resumption after interruption, Ibn 'Abbas's statement that raml is not sunnah (i.e., not wajib), and the practice of Ibn 'Abbas and 'Ali ibn Husayn leaving raml. These support the ruling and allow omission in constant crowd.
5
Apply the concession for constant crowd
If the crowd is unending, one may act on Ibn 'Abbas's view and skip raml, as per the commentary.

(۱۳۱۸ ) فان زحمه الناس وقف فاذا وجد فرجة رمل لا بد له منه فيقف حتى يقيمه على الوجه المسنون بخلاف استلام الحجر الاسود لان له بدلا وهو استقباله ... ترجمه : (۱۳۱۸) اگر لوگوں کا ہجوم ہو تو رک جائے پس جب کشادگی ملے تو رمل کرے جو اس کے لئے ضروری ہے،اس لئے ٹھہر جائے تاکہ مسنون طریقے پر ادا کر سکے، بخلاف حجر اسود چومنے کے اس لئے کہ اس کا بدل استقبال کرنا موجود ہے۔ تشریح : رمل کر رہا تھا کہ بھیڑ آ گئی تو وہیں ٹھہر جائے تا کہ بھیڑ کم ہو جائے تو مسنون طریقے پر رمل کرے، مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ بغیر ریل کے آگے نہ بڑھے ، کیونکہ رمل ضروری ہے اور اس کا کوئی بدل بھی نہیں ہے اس لئے ابھی رکے اور بھیڑ کم ہونے پر مسنون طریقے پر رمل کرتے ہوئے طواف پورا کرے۔ اس کے برخلاف حجر اسود کو بوسہ نہ دے سکے تو آگے بڑھتا چلا جائے کیونکہ اس کا بدل یہ ہے کہ دور سے حجر اسود کا استقبال کرے اور ہاتھ سے اشارہ کرے اور اس کو چوم لے ۔ آج کل حج کے موقع پر بہت بھیڑ ہوتی ہے اور دن رات بھیٹر رہتی ہے، اس لئے جتنا کٹر کر چل سکے چلے باقی میں اپنی ہیئت پر چل کر طواف پورا کرلے۔
وجه : (ا) وقال عطاء فيمن يطوف فتقام الصلاة او يدفع عن مكانه اذا سلم يرجع الى حيث قطع عليه فيبني . ويذكر نحوه عن ابن عمر و عبد الرحمن بن ابی بکر ۔ ( بخاری شریف، باب اذا اوقف فی الطواف ، ص ۲۶۳ نمبر ۱۶۲۳) اس قول تابعی میں ہے کہ درمیان میں کوئی انقطاع پیش آجائے تو دوبارہ بنا کرے۔(۲) ایسی بھیٹر ہو کہ ختم ہی نہیں ہو پا رہی ہو تو حضرت عبداللہ ابن عباس کے قول پر عمل کر لے، انہوں نے فرمایا کہ رمل سنت نہیں ہے مستحب ہے اس لئے مجبوری کے وقت اس پر عمل کر لے۔ اثریہ ہے عن ابی طفيل قال قلت لابن عباس یزعم قومك أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قد رمل بالبيت و أن ذالك سنة ؟ قال صدقو ا و كذبوا قلت و ما صدقوا و ما كذبوا ؟ قال صدقوا قد رمل رسول الله الله و كذبوا، ليس بسنة - (ابوداؤد شریف، باب فی الرمل، ص ۲۷۵، نمبر ۱۸۸۵) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ریل سنت نہیں ہے۔ (۲) ان ابن عباس و على بن حسين كانا لا يرملان . مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، باب من رخص فی ترک الرمل ، ج ثالث ص ۲۶۵، نمبر ۱۴۱۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ ریل واجب نہیں ہے اس لئے گنجائش نہ ہو تو اس پر عمل کر لے۔
Section: Composition of the Actions of Hajj. (1318) If people crowd him, he stops; then when he finds an opening, he performs raml—it is unavoidable for him. So he stops until he can perform it in the sunnah manner, unlike kissing the Black Stone, because it has a substitute, which is facing it. Translation: (1318) If there is a crowd of people, he should stop; then when he finds an opening, he should perform raml, which is necessary for him. Therefore, he stops so that he can perform it in the sunnah manner, unlike kissing the Black Stone, because its substitute—facing it—is available. Commentary: He was doing raml when a crowd came; he should stop there until the crowd lessens, then perform raml in the sunnah manner. The author says: he should not proceed without raml, because raml is obligatory and has no substitute; so he stops now and completes tawaf with raml in the sunnah manner when the crowd lessens. In contrast, if he cannot kiss the Black Stone, he moves forward because its substitute is to face the Black Stone from a distance and point with his hand and kiss it. Nowadays during Hajj there is much crowd day and night, so he should do raml as much as he can, and for the rest complete tawaf walking normally. Evidence: (1) 'Ata said about one who performs tawaf and the prayer is established or he is pushed from his place: when he says salam, he returns to where he was interrupted and continues. Similar is narrated from Ibn 'Umar and 'Abd al-Rahman ibn Abi Bakr. (Bukhari, Chapter: When one is stopped during tawaf, p.263 no.1623) This saying of a tabi'i indicates that if an interruption occurs, he should resume. (2) If the crowd is such that it never ends, then act on the saying of 'Abdullah ibn 'Abbas: he said that raml is not sunnah but mustahabb, so in necessity act on it. There is an athar from Abu al-Tufayl: he said, I said to Ibn 'Abbas: Your people claim that the Messenger of Allah (SAW) did raml of the House and that it is sunnah. He said: They spoke truth and lied. I said: What did they speak truth and what did they lie? He said: They spoke truth that the Messenger of Allah did raml, and they lied that it is sunnah. (Abu Dawud, Chapter on Raml, p.275 no.1885) This hadith states that raml is not sunnah. (3) Ibn 'Abbas and 'Ali ibn Husayn used not to do raml. (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, Chapter: Who permitted leaving raml, vol.3 p.265 no.1416) This athar indicates that raml is not wajib, so if there is no room, one may act on that.
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding raml (quick walking) during tawaf when there is a crowd. The author first states the ruling: if a person is doing raml and a crowd prevents him, he should stop and wait until he can resume raml in the sunnah manner. This is because raml is necessary (la budda lahu minhu, i.e., wajib according to the Hanafi school) and has no substitute. In contrast, if one cannot kiss the Black Stone, he may substitute by facing it from a distance and pointing, so he can proceed without waiting. The commentary explains that the author emphasizes not moving forward without raml, as it is obligatory and has no alternative. The text then provides evidence from narrations: (1) 'Ata's statement about interruption in tawaf—if prayer is established or he is pushed, he resumes after finishing; this supports resumption after interruption. (2) A narration from Ibn 'Abbas that raml is not sunnah (in his view) but was done by the Prophet; however, the Hanafi school holds raml to be sunnah mu'akkadah or wajib, but this narration is used here to show that in extreme necessity, one may leave it. (3) An athar that Ibn 'Abbas and 'Ali ibn Husayn did not do raml, indicating it is not wajib. The commentary reconciles: if the crowd is constant, one may act on the concession and not do raml. The final note advises that today with constant crowds, one should do raml as much as possible and walk normally for the rest.

Key Terms
رمل (raml): Quick walking with short steps and swaying shoulders during tawaf, specifically in the first three circuits for men.
زحام (ziham): Crowd of people that prevents normal movement during tawaf.
فرجة (furjah): Opening or gap in the crowd that allows resumption of raml.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is performing raml during tawaf and a crowd pushes them, what should they do according to the Hanafi school?
A) Continue walking quickly even if it harms others
B) Stop and wait until they can resume raml in the sunnah manner
C) Skip raml entirely and continue at normal pace
D) Leave the tawaf and restart later

Key Takeaway
Raml is a necessary act during tawaf for men; if prevented by crowd, stop and resume when possible, but if crowd is constant, one may omit it based on a valid concession.

Istilam of the Black Stone: Ruling and Practice
Ruling with dalil on touching the Black Stone each circuit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on istilam of the Black Stone and explain the proper procedure when access is obstructed.

Core Idea
Istilam of the Black Stone is sunnah mu'akkadah each circuit; if unable, point and kiss the hand.

The Black Stone is a revered object set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba. During tawaf, the pilgrim is encouraged to touch or kiss it each time they pass. This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on this practice, the evidence from the Sunnah, and the acceptable substitute when the Stone is unreachable due to crowds.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its hukm level
Istilam (touching/kissing) of the Black Stone is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah in the Hanafi school. This means it is strongly recommended, but not obligatory. Determine what the pilgrim must do if they can and cannot touch it.
The ruling is derived from the Prophet's consistent practice.
2
Locate the dalil (evidence)
Two hadith are cited: (1) Ibn 'Umar reports the Prophet never omitted touching the Yemeni Corner and the Black Stone in any tawaf. (2) Ibn 'Abbas reports that when the Prophet performed tawaf on a camel, he pointed to the Stone with something and said takbir.
These hadith establish both the practice and the substitute.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (how the evidence proves the ruling)
The first hadith shows the Prophet's continuous, deliberate act of touching the Stone, which indicates a sunnah mu'akkadah. The second hadith shows that when direct touch is impossible, pointing and takbir suffice, indicating a valid substitute.
This is a clear daleel for the ruling.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A minority of Hanafi scholars consider istilam merely mustahabb (recommended), but the majority view, based on the Prophet's persistent practice, holds it as sunnah mu'akkadah.
The Zahir al-Riwayah position is the stronger view.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preponderant position)
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling is that istilam is sunnah mu'akkadah at every circuit when possible, and if unable, pointing and kissing the hand is the substitute.
The text uses the hadith as authority, making this the established practice.

ويستلم الحجر كلّما مرّ لغت : رل اکڑ کر چلنا ۔ اشواط : شوط کی جمع ہے ، طواف کے ایک چکر کو ایک شوط کہتے ہیں۔ ھر : حرکت دینا۔ مبارز : برز سے مشتق ہے، باہر نکلنا، جنگ میں مقابلے کے لئے دعوت دینے والا ۔ تینتر : بختر سے مشتق ہے، متکبرانہ چال سے چلنا۔ زحم : بھیڑ فرجہ : کشادگی، راستہ۔
ترجمه : (۱۳۱۹) اور حجر اسود کا استلام کرے جب بھی اس کے پاس سے گزرے۔ اور استلام کے ساتھ ہی طواف پورا کرے،۔ تشریح : ہر طواف میں جب جب بھی حجر اسود کے سامنے سے گزرے اور موقع ملے تو اس کو چھوئے ، اور بھیٹر کی وجہ سے چھونے کا موقع نہ ہو تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کرے اور ہاتھ کو چوم لے۔ اور حجر اسود پر ہی آکر آخری طواف ختم کرے، تو گویا کہ حجر  اسود سے طواف شروع ہوا اور حجر اسود پر ہی آکر ختم ہوا، اور اس وقت بھی موقع ہو تو حجر اسود کو چومے اور موقع نہ ہو تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کر کے ہاتھ کو چوم لے۔
وجه : (۱) جب جب حجر اسود کے پاس سے گزرے تو اگر چوم سکے تو اس کو چومے، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله لا يدع ان يستلم الركن اليماني والحجر في كل طوافه قال وكان عبد الله بن عمر يفعله (ابوداؤد شریف، باب استلام الارکان ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۱۸۷۶/ بخاری شریف، باب تقبيل الحجر ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۶۱۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب جب حجر اسود کے پاس سے گزرے تو اس کو چومے (۲) اور نہ چوم سکے تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کرے اور تکبیر کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال طاف النبي الله بالبيت على بعير كلما اتى الركن اشار اليه بشيء عنده وكبر . ( بخاری شریف ، باب من اشار الی الرکن اذا اتی الیہ ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۱۶۱۳)
And he performs istilam of the Stone every time he passes. Lexicon: raml: walking with a strut. Ashwat: plural of shawt, one circuit of tawaf. ... Translation: (1319) And he should perform istilam of the Black Stone whenever he passes by it. And he completes tawaf with the istilam. Commentary: In every tawaf, whenever he passes in front of the Black Stone and has an opportunity, he should touch it. If due to crowd he cannot touch it, he points to it with his hand and kisses his hand. And he should complete the final circuit at the Black Stone, so that tawaf begins and ends at the Black Stone. At that time too, if possible, he kisses it; if not, he points and kisses his hand. Evidence: (1) Whenever he passes the Black Stone, if he can kiss it, he should. For this there is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah (SAW) never left off touching the Yemeni Corner and the Stone in every tawaf of his.' Ibn 'Umar used to do it. (Abu Dawud, Chapter: Istilam of the corners, p.265 no.1876; Bukhari, Chapter: Kissing the Stone, p.261 no.1611). This hadith states that whenever he passed the Black Stone, he kissed it. (2) If he cannot kiss, he points with his hand and says takbir. For this there is the hadith of Ibn 'Abbas: 'The Prophet (SAW) performed tawaf of the House on a camel; whenever he came to the corner, he pointed to it with something he had and said takbir.' (Bukhari, Chapter: Whoever points to the corner when he comes to it, p.219 no.1613).
Source pages p. 358

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding istilam (touching) of the Black Stone during tawaf. The ruling: the pilgrim should perform istilam of the Black Stone every time he passes by it during each circuit. Ideally, he touches it with his hand and kisses it. If unable due to crowd, he points to it with his hand and then kisses his hand. The tawaf should begin and end at the Black Stone, so the final circuit should be completed by facing the Black Stone. The commentary emphasizes that if possible, one should kiss the Stone; if not, pointing suffices. The evidence provided: (1) The consistent practice of the Prophet (SAW) as narrated by Ibn 'Umar—he never missed touching the Yemeni Corner and the Black Stone in every tawaf. This establishes the sunnah of touching each time. (2) When on a camel and unable to touch, the Prophet pointed and said takbir, showing the substitute. This ruling applies to every circuit; Hanafis consider istilam of the Black Stone to be sunnah mu'akkadah, and if one misses it, no compensation is required, but it is meritorious to perform it.

Key Terms
استلام (istilam): To touch or kiss the Black Stone as an act of veneration during tawaf.
حجر اسود (hajar al-aswad): The Black Stone set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba, kissed or pointed to during tawaf.
ركن يماني (rukn yamani): The Yemeni Corner of the Kaaba, also touched during tawaf.

Key Takeaway
Istilam of the Black Stone is a sunnah mu'akkadah performed each circuit; if unable, pointing and kissing the hand suffices, and tawaf remains valid without it.
