Two Rak'ahs After Tawaf: The Hanafi Wujub Proof
Ruling on the two rak'ahs of tawaf with proofs from Quran and Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the two rak’ahs of tawaf and explain the three proofs (Quran, hadith, and prophetic constancy) that establish their wujub.

Core Idea
The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib — the Prophet never omitted them.

After completing the seven circuits of tawaf, pilgrims are required to pray two rak'ahs. The Hanafi school holds this as a wajib act, a view supported by clear textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah. In this lesson, we unpack the proofs that elevate these rak'ahs to the level of obligation and clarify the school's position vis-à-vis other madhahib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the act: two rak'ahs after every tawaf. Determine its hukm level in the Hanafi school: wajib.
Wajib means necessary; omission without excuse is sinful but does not invalidate the tawaf.
2
Locate the first proof (Quran)
Examine the verse in Surah al-Baqarah 2:125: 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer.' In Hanafi usul, an imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub) unless there is a contrary indicator.
The verse is general in command; no contrary indicator is found.
3
Locate the second proof (hadith of Ibn 'Umar)
Read the hadith from Sahih al-Bukhari where the Prophet prayed two rak'ahs behind Maqam Ibrahim after tawaf. This demonstrates the Sunnah practice.
The hadith is sahih and explicitly describes the act.
4
Locate the third proof (prophetic constancy)
Consider the athar from al-Zuhri: the Prophet never performed seven circuits without praying two rak'ahs. This muwazabah (continuity) is evidence of wujub in Hanafi fiqh.
Constancy transforms a recommended act into a wajib, unlike the Shafi'i view.
5
Note the cross-madhhab dispute
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i holds these two rak'ahs as sunnah mu'akkadah, not wajib. The difference stems from divergent usul: Shafi'is do not consider muwazabah alone as proof of wujub.
Practical consequence: if omitted, a Shafi'i commits no sin, while a Hanafi must observe them.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبركعتين في مقام ابراهيم عليه السلام او حيث تيسر من المسجد (۱۳۲۱) ثم دعا فاستلم الحجر اسود
ترجمه : (۱۳۲۰) دو رکعت پڑھے مقام ابراہیم میں یا مسجد حرام میں جہاں آسان ہو۔ تشريح : ساتوں طواف ختم کرنے کے بعد اگر مقام ابراہیم کے پاس جگہ ہو تو وہاں نماز پڑھے، اور وہاں جگہ نہ ہو تو قریب میں مسجد حرام میں جہاں جگہ ملے وہاں طواف کی دورکعت نماز پڑھے۔
وجه: (1) سمعت ابن عمر يقول قدم النبي عله فطاف بالبيت سبعا وصلى خلف المقام ركعتين ثم خرج الى الصفا. (بخاری شریف باب من صلی رکعتی الطواف خلف المقام، ص ۲۲۰ نمبر ۶۲۷ اسرابن ماجہ شریف، باب الرکعتین بعد الطواف ،ص ۲۲۸، نمبر ۲۹۵۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے سات شوط کے بعد مقام ابراہیم پر آئے اور دورکعت طواف کی پڑھے۔ (۲) اس آیت میں ہے۔ واتخذوا من مقام ابراهیم مصلی (آیت ۱۲۵ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں حکم ہے کہ مقام ابراہیم کے پاس نماز پڑھی جائے۔ یہ دورکعت واجب ہے۔ (۳) اس کی دلیل حضور کی مواظبت ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ قلت صلى الله للزهرى ان عطاء يقول تجزئه المكتوبة من ركعتي الطواف فقال السنة افضل لم يطف النبي عله اسبوعا قط الاصلى ركعتين. (بخاری شریف ، باب صلی النبی السیو مد رکعتین ، ص ۲۲۰، نمبر ۱۹۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب جب آپ نے طواف کے سات شوط پورے کئے تو آپ نے دور کعت طواف پڑھی۔ اس ہمیشگی کی وجہ سے رکعت طواف حنفیہ کے نزدیک واجب ہے۔
And (he performs) two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim (peace be upon him) or wherever is easy in the mosque. (1321) Then he supplicates and performs istilam of the Black Stone. Translation: (1320) He should pray two rak'ahs at Maqam Ibrahim or in the Sacred Mosque wherever is easy. Commentary: After completing the seven circuits, if there is space near Maqam Ibrahim, he prays there; if not, he prays the two rak'ahs of tawaf nearby in the Sacred Mosque wherever he finds space. Evidence: (1) I heard Ibn 'Umar say: The Prophet (SAW) arrived, performed tawaf of the House seven times, prayed two rak'ahs behind the Maqam, then went out to al-Safa. (Bukhari, Chapter: Who prayed the two rak'ahs of tawaf behind the Maqam, p.220 no.627; Ibn Majah, Chapter: The two rak'ahs after tawaf, p.228 no.2958) This hadith shows that after seven circuits, he came to Maqam Ibrahim and prayed two rak'ahs. (2) The verse: 'And take the Maqam of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:125) commands prayer near Maqam Ibrahim. These two rak'ahs are wajib. (3) The proof is the Prophet's constancy. There is an athar: I said to al-Zuhri that 'Ata says the obligatory prayer suffices for the two rak'ahs of tawaf. He said: The sunnah is better. The Prophet never performed seven circuits without praying two rak'ahs. (Bukhari, Chapter: The Prophet prayed two rak'ahs after tawaf, p.220 no.1923) This hadith shows that whenever he completed seven circuits, he prayed two rak'ahs. Due to this constancy, the two rak'ahs of tawaf are wajib according to the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof concerning the two rak'ahs performed after completing the seven circuits of tawaf. The ruling: after tawaf, the pilgrim should pray two rak'ahs. The preferred location is behind Maqam Ibrahim (the Station of Abraham) based on the Prophet's practice. If there is no space there, he may pray anywhere in the Sacred Mosque (al-Masjid al-Haram) that is convenient. The commentary explains that these two rak'ahs are wajib (obligatory) in the Hanafi school, based on three proofs: (1) The explicit hadith of Ibn 'Umar describing the Prophet's action—he prayed two rak'ahs behind Maqam after tawaf. (2) The Quranic command (2:125) to take the Maqam as a place of prayer, interpreted as a command to pray there. (3) The Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah)—he never omitted these two rak'ahs after tawaf. The Hanafi position is that this constancy indicates wujub. The athar from al-Zuhri refutes the view that the obligatory prayer can substitute, stating that the sunnah (i.e., the two rak'ahs) is better and the Prophet always prayed them. Thus, for Hanafis, these two rak'ahs are wajib, meaning they are necessary and should not be left; if left unintentionally, one should perform sajdah al-sahw, and if left deliberately, the tawaf is still valid but sinful.

Key Terms
مقام إبراهيم (maqam ibrahim): The stone on which Prophet Ibrahim stood while building the Kaaba; now enclosed in a glass case near the Kaaba. It is the preferred location for praying the two rak'ahs after tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying two rak'ahs after tawaf?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Mustahabb
D) Fard 'ayn

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs of tawaf are wajib in the Hanafi school, proven by the Prophet's constant practice and the Quranic command to take Maqam Ibrahim as a place of prayer.

beginner
5 min
The Sunnah of Istilam After Tawaf Prayer
Ruling on performing istilam of the Black Stone after the two rak'ahs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended sequence after the two rak'ahs of tawaf and identify the ruling (sunnah) of returning to the Black Stone for istilam.

Core Idea
After tawaf prayer, return to the Black Stone for istilam—it completes the tawaf as you began.

The pilgrim has completed tawaf and prayed two rak'ahs. The tawaf began with istilam of the Black Stone; the sunnah recommends ending with istilam. This lesson clarifies the correct sequence and the legal status of this action, emphasizing that it is a confirmed sunnah, not obligatory, and is performed when possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is returning to the Black Stone and performing istilam (touching or kissing) after the two rak'ahs of tawaf. The Hanafi ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed recommended).
Sunnah mu'akkadah means the Prophet ﷺ consistently performed it; omitting it is not sinful but loses reward.
2
Place it in the tawaf sequence
The correct order: 7 circuits of tawaf → two rak'ahs (preferably at Maqam Ibrahim) → return to Black Stone for istilam → then proceed to sa'y between Safa and Marwah.
This sequence is from the practice of the Prophet ﷺ.
3
Note the condition of feasibility
The text says 'if possible' (إن أمكن), indicating it is not wajib. The sunnah is performed only when the area around the Stone is accessible without harming others.
If crowded, one may point or simply pass by; no compensation needed.
4
Understand the legal effect of omission
If the pilgrim does not return for istilam, the tawaf and subsequent sa'y remain valid. No dam (compensatory sacrifice) or sajdah sahwu is required.
This distinguishes it from a wajib act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم دعا فاستلم الحجر اسود
ترجمه : (۱۳۲۱) پھر لوٹ کر حجر اسود کا استلام کرے۔
تشریح : مقام ابراہیم پر نماز پڑھنے کے بعد اگر ہو سکے تو دوبارہ حجر اسود کو چومے۔
Then he supplicates and performs istilam of the Black Stone. Translation: (1321) Then he returns and performs istilam of the Black Stone. Commentary: After praying at Maqam Ibrahim, if possible, he should again kiss the Black Stone.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This is a brief ruling statement: after completing the two rak'ahs of tawaf (preferably at Maqam Ibrahim), the pilgrim should return to the Black Stone and perform istilam (touching or kissing) if possible. The commentary clarifies that this is done after the prayer, and it is recommended to kiss the Stone again. This action is not wajib but is a sunnah to end the tawaf rituals with istilam, mirroring the beginning. The sequence: tawaf → two rak'ahs → istilam → then proceed to sa'y between Safa and Marwah.

Key Terms
استلام (istilam): Touching or kissing the Black Stone as a veneration; here after the tawaf prayer.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Beginning and Ending Tawaf at the Black Stone and the Two Rak'ahs
Rulings on tawaf initiation and completion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on istilam of the Black Stone at each circuit of tawaf and the obligation of the two rak'ahs after completing tawaf, and cite the primary evidence for each.

Core Idea
Tawaf begins and ends at the Black Stone; the post-tawaf two rak'ahs are wajib, not optional.

This passage from Thamaratun Najah presents two connected rulings: the proper way to start and end each circuit of tawaf at the Black Stone, and the obligation of praying two rak'ahs after completing all seven circuits. The Hanafi school bases these on the Prophet's consistent practice and the Quranic command to take the Station of Ibrahim as a place of prayer. Understanding the difference between the sunnah act of istilam and the wajib act of the two rak'ahs is essential for performing a sound tawaf.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts under discussion
The passage addresses: (1) istilam (touching or kissing) of the Black Stone at the beginning and end of each circuit, and (2) praying two rak'ahs after completing all seven circuits of tawaf.
The text separates them with reference numbers (1320) and (1321).
2
State the ruling and evidence for istilam
For the Black Stone: it is sunnah to kiss it if possible; otherwise, gesture towards it and say takbir. The evidence is the hadith from Ibn Umar showing the Prophet never omitted istilam in any tawaf (Bukhari 1611, Abu Dawud 1876) and from Ibn Abbas gesturing while on a camel (Bukhari 1613).
Istilam is a recommended act of veneration, not an obligation.
3
State the ruling and evidence for the two rak'ahs
The Hanafi ruling: the two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib. Evidence includes the Quranic verse (2:125) commanding to take Maqam Ibrahim as a place of prayer, the hadith of Ibn Umar that the Prophet prayed behind the station, and the constant practice (mudawamah) confirmed in Bukhari 1923 that the Prophet never omitted them.
The imperative 'ittakhidhu' combined with the Prophet's continuous practice establishes wujub in Hanafi usul.
4
Distinguish between the Hanafi position and other schools
While all schools agree on the desirability of istilam, some other madhhabs (e.g., some Shafi'is) consider the two rak'ahs as sunnah, not wajib. The Hanafi reliance on the continuous practice (mudawamah) as a sign of obligation is the key difference.
The thamarah al-khilaf is the obligation level: missing a wajib requires compensation (sajdah al-sahw if in prayer, or dam if in hajj context), whereas missing a sunnah does not.

Source Text

فصل تركيب افعال الحج
به ويختم الطواف به (۱۳۲۰) وبركعتين في مقام ابراهيم عليه السلام او حيث تيسر من المسجد (۱۳۲۱) ثم دعا فاستلم الحجر
اسود سے طواف شروع ہوا اور حجر اسود پر ہی آکر ختم ہوا، اور اس وقت بھی موقع ہو تو حجر اسود کو چومے اور موقع نہ ہو تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کر کے ہاتھ کو چوم لے۔
وجه : (۱) جب جب حجر اسود کے پاس سے گزرے تو اگر چوم سکے تو اس کو چومے، اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله الله لا يدع ان يستلم الركن اليماني والحجر في كل طوافه قال وكان عبد الله بن عمر يفعله (ابوداؤد شریف، باب استلام الارکان ص ۲۶۵ نمبر ۱۸۷۶/ بخاری شریف ، باب تقبيل الحجر ص ۲۶۱ نمبر ۱۶۱۱) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب جب حجر اسود کے پاس سے گزرے تو اس کو چومے (۲) اور نہ چوم سکے تو ہاتھ سے اس کی طرف اشارہ کرے اور تکبیر کہے اس کے لئے یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال طاف النبي الله بالبيت على بعير كلما اتى الركن اشار اليه بشيء عنده وكبر . ( بخاری شریف ، باب من اشار الی الرکن اذا اتی الیہ ص ۲۱۹ نمبر ۱۶۱۳)
ترجمه : (۱۳۲۰) دو رکعت پڑھے مقام ابراہیم میں یا مسجد حرام میں جہاں آسان ہو۔
تشريح : ساتوں طواف ختم کرنے کے بعد اگر مقام ابراہیم کے پاس جگہ ہو تو وہاں نماز پڑھے، اور وہاں جگہ نہ ہو تو قریب میں مسجد حرام میں جہاں جگہ ملے وہاں طواف کی دورکعت نماز پڑھے۔
وجه: (1) سمعت ابن عمر يقول قدم النبي عله فطاف بالبيت سبعا وصلى خلف المقام ركعتين ثم خرج الى الصفا. (بخاری شریف باب من صلی رکعتی الطواف خلف المقام، ص ۲۲۰ نمبر ۶۲۷ اسرابن ماجہ شریف، باب الرکعتین بعد الطواف ،ص ۲۲۸، نمبر ۲۹۵۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کے سات شوط کے بعد مقام ابراہیم پر آئے اور دورکعت طواف کی پڑھے۔ (۲) اس آیت میں ہے۔ واتخذوا من مقام ابراهیم مصلی (آیت ۱۲۵ سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں حکم ہے کہ مقام ابراہیم کے پاس نماز پڑھی جائے۔ یہ دورکعت واجب ہے۔ (۳) اس کی دلیل حضور کی مواظبت ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ قلت صلى الله للزهرى ان عطاء يقول تجزئه المكتوبة من ركعتي الطواف فقال السنة افضل لم يطف النبي عله اسبوعا قط الاصلى ركعتين. (بخاری شریف ، باب صلی النبی السیو مد رکعتین ، ص ۲۲۰، نمبر ۱۹۲۳) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ جب جب آپ نے طواف کے سات شوط پورے کئے تو آپ نے دور کعت طواف پڑھی۔ اس ہمیشگی کی وجہ سے رکعت طواف حنفیہ کے نزدیک واجب ہے۔
Chapter: Composition of Hajj Actions. With it (the Black Stone) he begins and ends the tawaf (1320) and two rak'ahs at the Station of Ibrahim, peace be upon him, or wherever is convenient in the mosque (1321) then he makes supplication and touches the Black Stone. Tawaf begins from the Black Stone and ends at the Black Stone, and at that time if there is opportunity he kisses the Black Stone, and if no opportunity he gestures towards it with his hand and then kisses his hand. Evidence: (1) Whenever he passes by the Black Stone, if he can kiss it, he kisses it. For this there is this hadith: From Ibn Umar: 'The Messenger of Allah would not abandon touching the Yemeni Corner and the Black Stone in every tawaf.' He said: 'And Abdullah ibn Umar used to do it.' (Sunan Abi Dawud, Chapter of Touching the Corners, p. 265, no. 1876 / Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of Kissing the Black Stone, p. 261, no. 1611). In this hadith, whenever he passed by the Black Stone he kissed it. (2) And if he cannot kiss it, he gestures towards it with his hand and says the takbir. For this there is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas: 'The Prophet performed tawaf around the House on a camel; whenever he came to the corner he gestured towards it with something he had and said the takbir.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of Gesturing to the Corner When Reaching It, p. 219, no. 1613). Translation: (1320) He prays two rak'ahs at the Station of Ibrahim or in the Sacred Mosque wherever is easy. Explanation: After completing seven circuits of tawaf, if there is space near the Station of Ibrahim, he prays there; if there is no space there, he prays the two rak'ahs of tawaf near it in the Sacred Mosque wherever he finds a place. Evidence: (1) 'I heard Ibn Umar say: The Prophet arrived, performed tawaf around the House seven times, prayed two rak'ahs behind the Station, then went out to Safa.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of Whoever Prays the Two Rak'ahs of Tawaf Behind the Station, p. 220, no. 627 / Sunan Ibn Majah, Chapter of the Two Rak'ahs after Tawaf, p. 228, no. 2958). From this hadith it is known that after seven circuits of tawaf he came to the Station of Ibrahim and prayed two rak'ahs of tawaf. (2) In this verse: 'And take the Station of Ibrahim as a place of prayer' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:125). This verse commands that prayer be offered near the Station of Ibrahim. These two rak'ahs are wajib. (3) Its proof is the constant practice of the Prophet. There is an athar: 'I said to al-Zuhri: Ata says the obligatory prayer suffices for the two rak'ahs of tawaf. He replied: The Sunnah is better. The Prophet never completed a single circuit without praying two rak'ahs.' (Sahih al-Bukhari, Chapter of the Prophet Praying Two Rak'ahs, p. 220, no. 1923). This hadith states that whenever he completed seven circuits of tawaf, he prayed two rak'ahs. Due to this constancy, the two rak'ahs of tawaf are wajib according to the Hanafis.
Source pages p. 359

Commentary
This passage combines two related rulings of tawaf. First, it establishes that tawaf must begin and end at the Black Stone. The Prophet's practice was to kiss the Black Stone at the start of each circuit, or gesture if kissing wasn't possible. Two authentic hadiths from Ibn Umar and Ibn Abbas confirm this. Second, after completing all seven circuits, the pilgrim must pray two rak'ahs, preferably at the Station of Ibrahim, or anywhere in the Haram. The Hanafi school classifies these two rak'ahs as wajib, based on the Quranic command ('Take the Station of Ibrahim as a place of prayer'), the Prophet's constant practice, and the explicit statement in the hadith that he never omitted them. The passage distinguishes between the recommended (sunnah) act of kissing/gesturing and the obligatory (wajib) nature of the two rak'ahs.

Key Terms
استلام (istilam): Touching or kissing the Black Stone or Yemeni Corner during tawaf as an act of veneration.
حجر أسود (al-hajar al-aswad): The Black Stone set in the eastern corner of the Kaaba; tawaf must begin and end at its location.
مقام إبراهيم (maqam Ibrahim): The Station of Ibrahim, a stone near the Kaaba where Ibrahim stood while building it; the preferred place for the two rak'ahs after tawaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The two rak'ahs after tawaf are wajib in the Hanafi school, based on the Quranic command and the Prophet's consistent practice; the istilam of the Black Stone is a sunnah act of devotion.
